1001 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. State


No. 27692


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 726; 199 S.E.2d 183; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 1046


February 12, 1973, Submitted  
July 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Distributing obscene material. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Kelley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Dougherty Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of distributing obscene materials in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 26-21.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was based upon a movie that defendant exhibited in a local movie theater. On review the court found that Ga. Code Ann. § 26-2101(b) provided that material was obscene if, considered as a whole, applying community standards, its predominant appeal was to prurient interest, that is, a shameful or morbid interest in nudity, sex or excretion, and utterly without redeeming social value and if, in addition, it went substantially beyond customary limits of candor in describing or representing such matters. Defendant argued that the accusation was defective because it failed to include the definition of obscene materials as defined in § 26-2101(b), but the court held that a statute could have provided criminal punishment without the definition of obscenity being included within that specific code section. The court held that the chapter in which Ga. Code Ann. § 26-2105 was included, amply defined obscenity, and sections of the code that relate to the same subject matter had to be construed together.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distributing obscene materials.

1003 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hancock County v. Williams


No. 27916


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 723; 198 S.E.2d 659; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 1045


May 14, 1973, Argued  
June 29, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages; constitutional question. Hancock Superior Court. Before Judge Jackson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment of the Hancock County Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled the county's motion to dismiss appellee children's complaint that sought to recover for the death of their mother, and the county's motion to dismiss a power company's cross-claim against the county that sought to indemnify the power company for any recovery against it under the terms of an easement contract.


OVERVIEW: The children filed an action against the county after their mother drowned when the automobile in which she was a guest passenger ran into an artificial lake owned by the power company on a road that ran directly into the lake without any warning signs. The power company and the county had an easement contract for the purpose of providing access to the lake for recreational boating by the public. The court found that (1) the Act of 1946, 1946 Ga. Laws 152, Ga. Code Ann. ch. 69-6, authorized the county to enter into contracts so as to provide recreational facilities within the county, (2) the easement contract was authorized, and (3) the contract provided that the county had agreed to indemnify the power company for any damages arising from the use of the easement by the county. The court held that the complaint set forth a cause of action against the county based upon the contract that was valid and for that reason, the judgment of the superior court overruling the motions of the county to dismiss the complaint and cross-complaint were properly overruled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that overruled the county's motions to dismiss the complaint and the power company's cross-complaint.

 

1004 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


J & L Oil Co. v. Carrollton


No. 27848


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 817; 199 S.E.2d 190; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 1070


April 9, 1973, Argued  
June 28, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 12, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. Carroll Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant license applicant, an oil company, asserting that an ordinance of appellee, the City of Carrollton, Georgia, was unreasonable, unconstitutional, and contrary to Georgia law and that the city was estopped, sought mandamus to compel the city to issue to it a license to operate a self-service motor fuel station within the city limits. After a hearing, the Carroll Superior Court (Georgia) denied the relief sought. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The controversy involved an abandoned service station which the applicant purchased and was renovating for the purpose of operating a self-service station. The city had adopted an ordinance which stated that it was unlawful for anyone other than the owner of a service station, manager, operator, or his agent to dispense motor fuel to the general public in the city limits. The trial court denied the applicant's challenge to the ordinance. On appeal, the court held that even if it should declare the city's ordinance invalid for any reason, such a declaration would not entitle the applicant to the relief sought, for there was nothing in the state law requiring the city to give further consideration to the matter and issue a license for said operation. Moreover, the court did not consider the city ordinance invalid for any reason argued and insisted upon. At the time enacted it represented a legitimate exercise of the police power of the city. It also represented a determination consonant with the "local option" policy adopted by the state under the "local option" law, 1971 Ga. Laws 683, 684 9 (codified at Ga. Code Ann. §§ 23-2713, 23-2714), which became effective three weeks later.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

J & L OIL CO. v. CITY OF CARROLLTON

1006 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Pendley v. Lake Harbin Civic Asso


Nos. 27837, 27838, 27839, 27840


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 631; 198 S.E.2d 503; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 1012


April 10, 1973, Argued  
May 24, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Banke.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant individuals sought review of the judgment of the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), which continued the temporary restraining order that was previously granted in full force and effect against them pending a jury trial. Plaintiffs, association and homeowners, sought review of the judgment, which failed to grant relief under the remaining grounds of their complaint for temporary injunction against the individuals.


OVERVIEW: The association and the homeowners owned homes in the area that were affected by the attempted rezonings. The individuals had requested the rezoning of the tracts in question to allow construction of a shopping center and other projects. A hearing on this issue was held and from 1,200 to 1,500 people were present, although the hearing was held in a room that only accommodated 50 people. The people who were interested in the various petitions could not get close to the door of the hearing room. The association and homeowners introduced unrebutted lay and expert evidence that such construction would be harmful to the area, causing dangerous traffic conditions, inadequate water and sewage, overcrowded schools, and other land use problems. The trial court later partially granted the association and homeowner's action for temporary injunction to stop the rezoning. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting a temporary injunction until a final trial to determine whether a "public hearing" had been held because the evidence suggested that the public did not have a sufficient opportunity to be heard at the rezoning hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which continued the temporary restraining order that was previously granted in full force and effect against the individuals pending a jury trial, and which failed to grant relief under the remaining grounds of the association and homeowners' complaint for temporary injunction against the individuals.

 

1007 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Breaux v. State


No. 27761


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 506; 197 S.E.2d 695; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 967


March 13, 1973, Argued  
April 25, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Use of obscene language; constitutional question. Fulton Criminal Court. Before Judge Tucker.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court of Fulton County (Georgia) of violating Ga. Code Ann. § 26-2610(b). Prior to the trial defendant attacked the constitutionality of this statute. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional. The jury found that defendant was guilty and he was sentenced to 12 months imprisonment. He filed an amended motion for new trial, which was overruled. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ga. Code Ann. § 26-2610(b) was unconstitutional in violation of the due process and equal protection clauses of the Constitutions of the United States and Georgia. Defendant argued that "obscene and vulgar or profane language" was too vague, indefinite and overbroad to give notice of the prohibited conduct. The statute punished unprovoked obscene, vulgar or profane language used in the presence of a female or a male under 14 years of age. The court held that the statute was constitutional because language was obscene, vulgar or profane when, under the circumstances and manner in which such utterance was made, it would clearly offend a reasonable person's sense of decency. The jury was authorized to find from the evidence that an 11-year-old girl was asked by defendant "Have you ever been laid before?" Defendant argued that the girl did not understand the meaning of the words and therefore no crime was committed. The girl testified that she knew its meaning because her mother had told her but that she did not "want to say it." The court held that the jury was authorized to find from her testimony that she knew the meaning of the words spoken to her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1008 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ruff v. Lee


No. 27758


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 426; 197 S.E.2d 376; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 936


March 13, 1973, Argued  
April 13, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cancellation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Alverson.

In 1963 Adia Mae Bell, as grantor, conveyed real property by a deed to secure debt to John C. Lee. In 1965 the property was sold by the grantee under a power of sale provided for by such deed. Lee purchased the property at such public sale as the terms of the deed to secure debt permitted him to do. In 1970 a complaint in equity was filed seeking to set such deed aside. The complaint, as amended, was brought in numerous counts and Count 5 of the amended complaint attacked the constitutionality of section 2 of the Act of 1935 (Ga. L. 1935, p. 381) (Code Ann. § 67-1506), which provides: ". . . no sale of real estate under powers contained in mortgages, debt, deeds, or other lien contracts shall be valid unless the sale shall be advertised and conducted at the time and place and in the usual manner of sheriff's sales in the county in which such real estate, or a part thereof, is located." The contention in such count of the complaint is that the statute does not provide for due process and a hearing before the sale, and thus such a sale is void. A motion for summary judgment on this count of the complaint was filed [***2] by the plaintiff and overruled. Upon a certificate of immediate review being granted the present appeal was filed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grantor's successor sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which denied the grantor's successor's motion for summary judgment in an action to set aside a deed held by defendant grantee on the ground that Ga. Code Ann. § 67-1506 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The grantor conveyed real property by a deed to secure a debt owed to the grantee. The grantee sold the property at a public sale and according to the terms of the deed. The grantor's successor filed an action to have the deed set aside, alleging that § 67-1506 was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the grantor's successor's motion for summary judgment, filed on the ground that § 67-1506 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Section 67-1506 provided that no sale of real estate under a debt or deed was valid unless the sale was advertised and conducted at the time and place and in the usual manner of sheriff's sales in the county in which such real estate was located. The grantor's successor contended that § 67-1506 deprived the grantor of due process. The court held that even if § 67-1506 were unconstitutional, the terms of the deed would have to be against public policy for the deed to be set aside because the grantee followed the terms therein in making the sale. The deed did not allow the grantee to sell the property without following certain steps calculated to notify the grantor of the sale. Thus, it was not void as against public policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied the grantor's successor's motion for summary judgment in an action to set aside a deed held by the grantee on the ground that a certain statute was unconstitutional.

 

1009 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. Kiff


No. 27458


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 277; 196 S.E.2d 445; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 882


September 12, 1972, Submitted  
March 15, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Macon Superior Court. Before Judge Marshall.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former inmate was convicted of the unlawful possession of marijuana. During the pendency of the appeal, the former inmate was paroled and was serving the balance of his sentence on parole. The Superior Court of Macon County (Georgia) denied the habeas corpus application filed by the former inmate attacking his conviction because the evidence was procured in violation of his Fourth Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: Atlanta law enforcement officers received information from a law enforcement officer in California that a package believed to contain marijuana had been shipped to the airport. No other information concerning the informer, his reliability, or corroborating circumstances on the tip appeared in the record. The Atlanta officers went to the airport and waited for the package to arrive. When it arrived, they examined its contents and determined that it contained marijuana. They waited for someone to call for the package. The former inmate signed for the package, took it to his car, and he was arrested. At trial, the package was introduced into evidence. The former inmate did not move to suppress the evidence or object to its introduction. The inmate's conviction was affirmed on appeal. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that there was no evidence of probable cause to arrest the former inmate and that the seizure was illegal. However, because the trial court had not ruled on that issue, the court remanded the case to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on whether there was probable cause for the arrest and the search and seizure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the habeas corpus judgment and directed the habeas corpus court to enter an order allowing the State to try to show that there was an adequate constitutional basis for the search. If the State's attempt was successful, then the judgment of conviction could stand. If the State was unsuccessful, then the judgment of conviction was constitutionally erroneous and had to be set aside.

 

1010 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Griggs v. Greene


Nos. 27719, 27741


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 257; 197 S.E.2d 116; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 880


January 12, 1973, Argued  
February 22, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Case No. 27719. Injunction. Fayette Superior Court. Before Judge Whalen.

Case No. 27741. Injunction. Brooks Superior Court. Before Judge Calhoun.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in Case No. 27719 affirmed. Judgment in Case No. 27741 affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax assessors appealed the orders from the trial courts (Georgia), which enjoined them from proceeding with any assessment against appellee taxpayers, and held that the provisions of a Georgia statute were unconstitutional in that they denied equal protection and due process of law.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers timely filed tax returns declaring their intangible property subject to taxation at the fair market value. The tax assessors adjusted the taxpayers' valuations and assessed each parcel of real property and all tangible personal property at 40 percent of the fair market value. The trial courts enjoined the tax assessors from proceeding with any assessment against the taxpayers. On appeal, the court affirmed and affirmed in part and reversed. The court concluded that in all counties of the state all tangible property, both real and personal, except automobiles and trailers, constituted a single class of property for the purposes of taxation, and had to be assessed and taxed alike. The General Assembly had no authority to establish different classes or sub-classes of tangible property other than as fixed by Ga. Const. art. VII, § I. The orders complained of were void and illegal because they did not follow the mandate of the Acts nor of the constitutional provisions under which they purportedly were issued, and insofar as the trial court's judgments enjoined the enforcement of the orders of the revenue commissioner they were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and affirmed in part and reversed the orders from the trial courts, which enjoined the tax assessors from proceeding with any assessment against the taxpayers, and held that the provisions of the Georgia statute were unconstitutional in that they denied equal protection and due process of law.

Cox v. Blackmon


No. 27682


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 275; 196 S.E.2d 403; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 881


January 9, 1973, Submitted  
February 22, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Macon Superior Court. Before Judge Marshall.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Macon County (Georgia), which denied the property owners' request to treat the action against appellee board of tax assessors (board) as a class action or to enjoin the submission of the tax digest for approval.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed an action with the trial court that sought relief from re-evaluation of rural property for ad valorem taxes by the board. The trial court entered a judgment that required the board to provide notice to the property owners but denied the property owners' request to treat the case as a class action and to enjoin the submission of the digest to the state revenue commissioner for approval. The property owners argued that the various statutes involved were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that the trial court correctly overruled the attacks on the constitutionality of the statutes. The court concluded that the case was moot as to certain other parties that failed to seek arbitration. The court found that the other arguments raised by the property owners were not meritorious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied the request of the property owners to treat the action against the board as a class action or to enjoin the submission of the digest for approval.

 

1012 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Overstreet


No. 27528


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 112; 195 S.E.2d 906; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 828


October 10, 1972, Argued  
February 8, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petition. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Cheatham.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant home owners sought review of a final order from the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia), which ordered payment of insurance policy proceeds held by the court's registry to appellee contractor.


OVERVIEW: Appellee contractor brought an action in equity against appellant home owners, the first-lien holder and the fire-loss insurer, to enforce an equitable lien on policy proceeds for the contract price of his repairs to a fire-damaged home. The insurer, which had received a properly executed proof of loss and release from appellants for payment, alleged that it was a mere stakeholder with respect to the policy proceeds and asked the trial court to grant an order directing to whom such proceeds should be paid. The trial court initially ordered the insurer to pay the proceeds into the registry of the court and, after a second hearing, ordered that such proceeds in the registry be paid to appellee in the amount of his lien. On review, appellants asserted that they were entitled to a trial by jury, that they had neither expressly nor impliedly waived that constitutional right, and that the trial judge's entry of final judgment was therefore improper. The court affirmed the order, noting that the Georgia Constitution did not require trial by jury in equity cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order directing that insurance proceeds be paid to appellee contractor in the amount of his lien.

 

1013 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


National Advertising Co. v. State Highway Dep't


No. 27630


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 119; 195 S.E.2d 895; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 830


December 12, 1972, Argued  
February 8, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.

The State Highway Department, acting pursuant to § 18 of the Georgia Outdoor Advertising Control Act, Ga. L. 1971, Ex. Sess., pp. 5, 21, approved and effective October 6, 1971; Code Ann. § 95-2016a, sought and obtained injunctive relief on July 10, 1972, against the National Advertising Company, the appellant here, from the continuance of the existence and maintenance of two outdoor advertising devices located on Interstate Highway 75 in Bartow County.

The stipulated facts disclose that in respect to one of the sites the State Highway Department issued a permit on September 27, 1971, acting under the law then in effect, Ga. L. 1967, p. 423, but that the National Advertising Company took no action to erect a device at the site until on or after February 29, 1972. In respect to the other site the National Advertising Company sought but did not obtain a permit under the 1967 law. Nonetheless, the company on August 19, 1971, did erect poles at the site, and thereafter, during December, 1971, and on or about February 29, 1972, the company used the site for advertising. The company obtained no [***2] permit under the 1971 law for either site. Both sites are within 600 feet from the nearest edge of a right-of-way of Interstate Highway 75, and are visible from the traveled portion of the highway.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advertising company challenged an order from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted an injunction sought by appellee State Highway Department, Georgia, prohibiting the company from exhibiting two outdoor advertising devices near an expressway and denied appellant's motion to dismiss. The company argued that the Georgia Outdoor Advertising Sign Control Act of 1971 (Act of 1971) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The company obtained a permit under the Georgia Outdoor Advertising Control Act of 1964 (Act of 1964) to erect outdoor advertising signs along an interstate highway in Georgia. The company did not display the outdoor advertising signs until after the Georgia Legislature had enacted the Act of 1971 following a declaration by the court in another action that the Act of 1964 was unconstitutional. The company placed its signs too close to the highway under the requirements of the Act of 1971. The company alleged that the Act of 1971, specifically §§ 3 and 18 codified at Ga. Code Ann. §§ 95-2003a and 95-2016a, was unconstitutional under the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution and under Ga. Const. art. I, § III, para. I and Ga. Const. art. I, § I, paras. II, III. Upon review, the court held that the Act of 1971 was constitutional. The court found that the Act of 1971 was an exercise of the police power of the State to zone property to prevent its use for certain purposes in the future. The court concluded that Ga. Code Ann. §§ 95-2003a and 95-2016a were not applied in an unconstitutional manner to the company.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

 

1014 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bryant v. Prior Tire Co.


No. 27675


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 137; 196 S.E.2d 14; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 838


January 9, 1973, Submitted  
February 8, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on contract; constitutional question. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Mitchell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the State Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), which denied her motion to dismiss plaintiff's action against her. Defendant claimed that a statute upon which service was based was unconstitutional. The appeal was taken upon a certification of immediate review prior to any determination of the merits of plaintiff's action.


OVERVIEW: The statute allowed service of process by leaving a copy at a party's most notorious place of abode where the amount involved in the litigation was less than a statutory amount. Plaintiff's action was for less than this amount. On appeal, the court held that the judgment of the trial court refusing to declare the statute unconstitutional was correct. Although the amount in litigation brought defendant within the class with respect to whom the statute allegedly was unconstitutional, defendant failed to show any resultant injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1015 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


F. P. Plaza, Inc. v. Waite


No. 27484


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 161; 196 S.E.2d 141; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 844


October 11, 1972, Argued  
February 8, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 22, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge McKenzie.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicants sought review of an order from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which entered judgment in favor of appellee county landowners and declared certain notice provisions of a county comprehensive zoning resolution unconstitutional because of their violation of the due process and equal protection requirements of the Georgia and Federal Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The landowners attacked the county commissioners' decision to rezone certain land in the county. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment upon finding that the notice given to the landowners was not constitutionally deficient. The court held that (1) the only notice required to be given for a preliminary public hearing before the planning commission was the posting of the sign on the property and mailing a notice to specified property owners; (2) the planning commission had no authority to rezone property where the extent of its power was to make recommendations to the governing authority; (3) the power to rezone property was vested totally and exclusively in the governing authority of the county; and (4) defective notice or lack of notice of the preliminary hearing before the planning commission was not violative of procedural due process or equal protection where the landowners had due and legal notice of the hearing on the matter of rezoning before the county governing authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment holding the that certain notice provision of a county zoning resolution were unconstitutional.

 

1016 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Drake v. Chesser


Nos. 27551, 27552


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 148; 196 S.E.2d 137; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 841


November 13, 1972, Argued  
January 22, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 9, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages; constitutional question. Clarke State Court. Before Judge Smith from Hall State Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed on cross appeal; reversed on main appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for damages, plaintiff appealed a decision of the Clark State Court (Georgia), which granted defendant union's motion for a directed verdict. The union filed a cross-appeal of the order that denied its motion to dismiss challenging the venue statute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought an action for damages, basing jurisdiction on Ga. Code Ann. §§ 3-118, 3-119, 3-120, 3-121 because defendant agent was the business representative of the union and did business in the county where the suit was filed. Special pleas to the jurisdiction were filed by both the union and the agent, and the union filed another motion to dismiss, alleging that the venue statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 3-120, was unconstitutional. The motion to dismiss was overruled. The union filed a motion for directed verdict, which was granted by the trial court, and plaintiff appealed. The union cross-appealed the denial of its motion based on the venue statute. The court held that the purpose of the statute at issue was to avoid having to locate a group of individuals in order to file suit in the county where each resided. Therefore, Ga. Code Ann. § 3-120 was not unconstitutional for the reasons urged, and the trial court did not err in overruling the motion to dismiss. The court held that it was error for the trial court to find as a matter of law that the union was not doing business in the county when it had an agent and employees there. Thus, there was a question of fact as to venue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the union's motion to dismiss and reversed the trial court's grant of a directed verdict in favor of the union based on jurisdiction.

 

1017 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Stull v. State


Nos. 27478, 27479


Supreme Court of Georgia


230 Ga. 99; 196 S.E.2d 7; 1973 Ga. LEXIS 825


October 11, 1972, Argued  
January 4, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 8, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Theft by taking; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Holt.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled the defendant's demurrers to two indictments and convicted the defendant of theft by taking in violation of the provisions of Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1802.


OVERVIEW: The defendant filed demurrers to two indictments, which charged the defendant of theft by taking, contending that the statute prohibiting theft by taking, Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1802, was unconstitutional. The trial court overruled the defendant's demurrers to the two indictments and convicted the defendant of theft by taking in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1802. The defendant appealed, contending that § 26-1802 was violative of the defendant's right to due process because it was so vague, uncertain, and indefinite that it failed to inform the defendant of the conduct proscribed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the statute was sufficiently definite in its terms to reasonably inform one charged thereunder as to the conduct proscribed thereby, that the jury was authorized to find that the defendant embarked on a fraudulent scheme of use of letterheads purporting to be those of a legitimate business concern, and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to order separate trials as to the two indictments. The crimes were similar in nature, and the scheme which resulted in their consummation was substantially identical in each case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted the defendant of theft by taking.

 

1018 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Watson v. State


Nos. 27153, 27435


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 787; 194 S.E.2d 407; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 774


May 9, 1972, Argued; November 13, 1972, Argued  
December 4, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Davis. (Case No. 27153).

Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 126 Ga. App. 554. (Case No. 27435).



DISPOSITION: Judgment in No. 27435 reversed; judgments in No. 27153 affirmed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant specially pled insanity. The jury found that he was not insane. Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Muscogee County (Georgia) of eight capital felonies including murder and he was sentenced to death. In one case, defendant appealed his conviction and sentence. In the other case, the court granted a writ of certiorari to consider the reversal of the judgment in the sanity trial by the Court of Appeals of Georgia.


OVERVIEW: The jury determined that defendant was mentally competent to stand trial, so the trial court conducted the criminal trial and refused to admit certain documents into evidence about defendant's mental condition in 1967. The documents contained findings by two doctors that defendant was suffering from a mental disorder. The trial court found that the documents were not relevant to defendant's mental condition at the time of his criminal trial. The jury convicted defendant and the trial court sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed the sanity trial portion of his case. The Court of Appeals of the State of Georgia accepted the case. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the Court of Appeals committed error in accepting the appeal without a certificate of immediate review, therefore, it had to reverse that decision; (2) the exclusion of the documents on defendant's mental condition was not error, and even if it was error, it was harmless; (3) even if defendant was mentally deficient in some respects, he was a danger to society and his confinement was proper; and (4) the death penalty had been declared unconstitutional, so defendant had to serve life in prison.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but it vacated the death penalty sentence and remanded the case with directions for the trial court to substitute a life sentence in its place.

1020 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. Smith


No. 27277


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 781; 194 S.E.2d 414; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 773


June 13, 1972, Submitted  
November 20, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 4, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Tattnall Superior Court. Before Judge Caswell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tattnall County (Georgia), which denied him relief under his postconviction petition for habeas corpus relief after he was convicted of rape and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: The victim identified defendant at a line-up, which occurred the day after the crime and before the indictment was returned. The victim later identified defendant at trial as the man who raped her. Defendant argued that he had been denied the assistance of counsel at the line-up. The trial court found that the in-court identification of defendant was sufficiently independent of the line-up so that, even if the line-up were defective, the positive identification at trial did not deprive defendant of his constitutional rights of due process and equal protection. On appeal, defendant challenged the death sentence and the composition of the jury. On review, the court affirmed the denial of the habeas corpus relief, but it ordered the sentence vacated and remanded the case to the sentencing court for it to impose a life sentence because Georgia's death penalty procedures had been declared unconstitutional; therefore, defendant could only be sentenced to life in prison. The court also held that: (1) the right to counsel attached only after the onset of formal prosecutorial proceedings; and (2) defendant did not show racial bias with respect to the grand jury or the traverse jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the habeas corpus court with directions for it to vacate the death sentence and remand the case to the trial court. The trial court was to sentence defendant to prison for life, which was the only lawful sentence which was permitted by law. Defendant did not have to be present in open court or represented by counsel, but he and his counsel had to be served with a copy of the sentence of life imprisonment.

 

1021 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


McCrary v. State


No. 27341


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 733; 194 S.E.2d 480; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 759


July 10, 1972, Submitted  
November 16, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Rape. Upson Superior Court. Before Judge Whalen.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Upson County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of rape, overruled his motion for a new trial, and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice followed the victim when she came out of a hospital, bumped her car from the rear, took the victim against her will, and drove to a secluded spot and forcibly raped her. In an unsworn statement to the jury defendant argued that he was intoxicated at the time and not responsible for his actions. The trial court convicted defendant of rape and sentenced him to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but remanded the case for the trial court to resentence defendant to life in prison because death could not be imposed for rape. The court held that: (1) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in not continuing the case in order for defendant to find an absent witness because defendant did not show the materiality of the testimony which he expected to procure from the witness; (2) there was no evidence that the jury had been biased due to pretrial publicity or that the State had used peremptory challenges to strike black men from the jury; (3) the evidence was sufficient to charge the jury on a theory of conspiracy; and (4) sufficient evidence sustained the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court except the death sentence for the crime of rape, which had been declared unconstitutional. Therefore, the sentencing court had to resentence defendant to life in prison and notify defendant and his attorney of the new sentence.

Smith v. State


No. 27494


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 727; 194 S.E.2d 82; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 757


October 11, 1972, Submitted  
November 15, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Theft by conversion; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Hames.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a demurrer to an indictment for theft by conversion, alleging Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1808(a) was unconstitutional. The Cobb Superior Court (Georgia) overruled defendant's demurrer and certified the issue for immediate review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for theft by conversion as defined in Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1808(a). The trial court overruled defendant's demurrer, which alleged that the application of the state statute constituted imprisonment for debt, involuntary servitude, and deprivation of liberty without due process of law in violation of Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. XXI. On review, the court affirmed. The court stated the case and the application of the statute to defendant's acts was distinguishable from common law in which there was an assumption of fraud implied for legal indebtedness for wages and services due. The court ruled the statute did not provide for an unconstitutional imprisonment for debt or peonage; instead, it created a form of larceny after trust. The law punished fraudulent conversion, not for the failure to comply with a contractual obligation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which overruled defendant's demurrer challenging the constitutionality of the state statute providing punishment for theft by conversion.

1024 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Arnold v. Selected Sites, Inc.


No. 27333


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 468; 192 S.E.2d 260; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 653


July 11, 1972, Submitted  
September 20, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Establishment of private way; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner brought an action against defendant adjoining landowner to have a private right of way of necessity established pursuant to O.C.G.A. §§ 83-101 through 83-106.2 for his use over the property of the adjoining landowner. The Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) entered a judgment dismissing the complaint on the grounds that §§ 83-101 through 83-106.2 were unconstitutional. The landowner appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The adjoining landowner filed a motion to dismiss on the grounds that O.C.G.A. § 83-106.1 was unconstitutional because it allowed the granting of a private right of way of necessity without first compensating the owner of the property burdened with the right of way. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that § 83-106.1 was unconstitutional under Ga. Const. art. I, § III, para. I, O.C.G.A. § 2-301, because it allowed for the granting of the right of way prior to the payment of just compensation. However, § 83-106.1 was severable because it was not such an integral part of the statute that the entire statute must fall. Accordingly, the landowner could maintain his action under the remaining provisions of O.C.G.A. §§ 83-101 through 83-106.2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that a statute allowing the creation of a right of way of necessity on adjoining property without first requiring the payment of just compensation was unconstitutional under the Georgia Constitution. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the landowner's action because the unconstitutional provisions of the statute were severable.

 

1025 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Fulghum v. Paul


No. 27318


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 463; 192 S.E.2d 376; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 651


July 10, 1972, Submitted  
September 12, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to set aside judgment; constitutional question. Oglethorpe Superior Court. Before Judge Williford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father sought to vacate a judgment from the Oglethorpe Superior Court (Georgia), which, upon respondent mother's application, changed the surname of the father's child to that of the child's stepfather.


OVERVIEW: The mother received custody of the father's child upon the couple's divorce. The mother filed an application to have the child's surname changed to that of the child's stepfather. The application was granted after the mother published the change in a newspaper. The father sought to vacate the trial court's judgment on the ground that he was deprived of procedural due process because he was not given notice of the name change. The court denied the father's request for vacation. First, the father did not have a property interest in maintaining his child's surname. The child's bearing of the father's surname was merely customary and could be changed for any purpose other than a fraudulent one. Second, the general assembly had the power to prescribe what notice was required prior to the trial court's acting on an application to change a name. The general assembly provided for notice by publication in accordance with Ga. Code Ann. § 79-501. Finally, the court noted that although the father did not have a property right in having his child bear his surname, trial courts did take into account a father's "protectible interest" in such when it considered a proposed name change.


OUTCOME: The court denied the father's petition to vacate the trial court's judgment, which, upon the mother's application, changed the surname of the father's child to that of the child's stepfather.

 

1026 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Yeomans v. State


No. 27308


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 488; 192 S.E.2d 362; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 660


July 10, 1972, Argued  
September 7, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 25, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation; constitutional question. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Knox.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Glynn County (Georgia) of selling an informant one tablet of acid. He appealed, enumerating as error the trial court's allowance of witnesses whose names were not furnished to defendant prior to trial, its overruling of defendant's request to open and close the closing argument, and its failure to give requested charges.


OVERVIEW: An undercover agent testified that that he told several people in a pool hall that he needed some acid. Defendant later approached him and asked how many he wanted. The agent purchased one tablet of acid from defendant, which he gave to police. Affirming, the court held that defendant's demand for a list of witnesses was not specific in that it did not demand the names of witnesses who would testify at trial. A state crime lab employee was not named because the prosecutor did not know who the lab would send. Another witness was a rebuttal witness, whose name was not required to be furnished. Ga. Code Ann. § 27-1403. The court rejected defendant's argument that because Ga. Code Ann. § 27-2201 allowed defendants who presented no evidence the right to open and close during closing argument, it was unconstitutional as a violation of defendant's right to equal protection. The purpose of the statute was to give an accused with no defense every opportunity to persuade the jury that the State failed to prove his guilt. This was a reasonable exception to the general rule. The trial court did not err in refusing to charge that the jury could find that the agent was an accomplice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

DeKalb County v. Allstate Beer, Inc.


No. 27304


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 483; 192 S.E.2d 342; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 659


July 11, 1972, Argued  
September 7, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 25, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a decision of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) that enjoined the county from further collection of an audit fee imposed upon appellee malt beverage dealers.


OVERVIEW: This was a dispute between malt beverage dealers (dealers) and the county over an audit fee imposed by the county. The trial court held that the audit fee was a tax imposed for raising revenue. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in holding that the audit fee was a tax because the local ordinance allowing for the fee was enacted to cover the cost of auditing the books of the dealers, so that it was clearly a license fee. However, the trial court did not err in enjoining further collection of the audit fee by the county. It noted that the 1958 constitutional amendment pursuant to Ga. La. 1958, pp. 582, 583, which authorized the levy of license taxes on businesses, was not self-executing. Therefore, the state statute under Ga. L. 1950, which limited a license fee to $ 100, controlled, with the result that the audit fee of $ 500 was invalid.


OUTCOME: The decision of the superior court that enjoined the county from further collection of an audit fee imposed upon the dealers was affirmed.

Massell v. Leathers


No. 27340


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 503; 192 S.E.2d 379; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 665

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee applicants filed an action against appellant members of a beer licensing authority, to restrain and enjoin them from refusing to issue a beer license to the applicants. The Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) issued an injunction enjoining the members of the licensing authority from refusing to issue the beer license. On appeal, the court reversed. The court concluded that the denial of a beer license did not deprive the applicants of anything to which they had an absolute right.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

DeKalb County v. Empire Distributors, Inc.


No. 27315


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 497; 192 S.E.2d 346; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 663


July 11, 1972, Argued  
September 7, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 25, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Peeler.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), which restrained and enjoined the county from enforcing a licensing ordinance against appellee liquor distributors.


OVERVIEW: The distributors were licensed and domiciled outside the county. The county contended that the distributors were doing business within the county by means of delivery and sale to retailers therein. The distributors argued that the county lacked authority to require them to obtain a license and pay a fee. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of injunctive relief to the distributors, holding that 1958 Ga. Laws 582-583, which authorized the county to impose license fees on persons, firms, and corporations doing business in the unincorporated area of the county, did not authorize the county to impose such license fees upon the distributors. The distributors sold at wholesale only, had no business offices in the county, and made deliveries to customers in the county from warehouses outside the county. The court held that such activities did not constitute doing business in the county for purposes of licensing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of injunctive relief to the distributors.

 

1030 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Southall v. Carter


No. 27194


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 240; 190 S.E.2d 517; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 569


May 8, 1972, Argued  
June 15, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Partitioning. Lowndes Superior Court. Before Judge Franklin.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant joint tenant brought an action against appellee joint tenant seeking partition of the land owned by them in Lowndes County as tenants in common. The Lowndes Superior Court (Georgia) granted appellee's motion to dismiss for improper venue and lack of jurisdiction, finding Ga. Code Ann. § 85-1504 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Section 85-1504 provided for a partition action to be brought in the county where the land was situated. In finding § 85-1504 unconstitutional, the trial court held that a partition action was not one "respecting titles to land" within the realm of Ga. Code Ann. § 2-4902, but was in the category of "all other civil cases" provided for under Ga. Code Ann. § 2-4906. The court reversed, holding that a statutory partition action in Georgia, which could bestow title on both parties and divest both parties of title, was a case "respecting titles to land," and proper venue was in the county where the land was situated. Therefore, § 85-1504 was not in conflict with the Georgia Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the partition action and found the venue statute constitutional.

Cain v. Lumpkin County


No. 27188


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 274; 190 S.E.2d 910; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 579

June 15, 1972, Decided

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Tax Commissioner of Lumpkin County (Georgia) and his surety, challenged a judgment of the Lumpkin Superior Court (Georgia) in favor of appellee, Lumpkin County (Georgia). The county had, pursuant to Ga. Code § 89-824, issued an execution against appellants in a specified amount. The sum was the amount of the county tax and commissions collected by the tax commissioner, which he had failed to account to the county.


OVERVIEW: The tax commissioner filed a suit in equity against the county seeking a judgment declaring the execution void and to set the same aside and cancel it of record. The county filed defensive pleadings by which it defended the validity of the execution. The trial court rendered a judgment in favor of the county from which the commissioner appealed. The tax commissioner argued that the 1963 Act, Ga. L. 1963, p. 2422, did not comply with the constitutional requirement that local or special bills could not be passed unless notice of the intention to apply therefore was published in the newspaper in which the sheriff's advertisements for the locality affected were published once a week for three weeks during a period of 60 days immediately preceding its introduction into the General Assembly. Ga. Const. art. III, § 7, para. 15, Ga. Code Ann. § 2-1915. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the notice disclosed by the record was sufficient to meet this requirement. The court further held that Ga. Code Ann. § 92-5304 provided that the tax commissioner was entitled to a 10 percent commission of all taxes collected in excess of 90 percent of the net tax digest, along with his salary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1032 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Wood v. Atkinson


No. 27049


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 179; 190 S.E.2d 46; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 546


February 15, 1972, Submitted  
May 19, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petition. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment not reviewed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former wife sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) that temporarily enjoined the wife from enforcing an order for unpaid child support against appellee former husband. The husband filed a cross appeal and a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The wife obtained a child support order against the husband pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 30-204. The husband challenged the order and the constitutionality of § 30-204 because the order was issued without notice or hearing. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the statute, but enjoined the wife from enforcing the order. The wife appealed. The husband cross appealed and moved to dismiss the appeal because it was not filed within 30 days as required by the Appellate Practice Act, § 6-803(a). The wife did not file a brief or an enumeration of error. The court held that the 30-day limitation for filing an appeal was jurisdictional. Therefore, the court did not have jurisdiction over the appeal. In fact, it had previously been dismissed for want of prosecution. The court also held that it had no jurisdiction over the husband's cross appeal. Under § 6-803(a), the jurisdiction of the court had to be properly invoked before a cross appeal could be perfected. Because the court was without jurisdiction over the wife's attempted appeal; it was also without jurisdiction over the husband's attempted cross appeal. Therefore, the court could not review the judgment below.


OUTCOME: The court had no jurisdiction to consider the attempted appeal by the wife or the attempted cross appeal by the husband. Therefore, the judgment below was not reviewed and stood as rendered.

March 15, 1972, Argued  
April 6, 1972, Decided

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner sought review of the order of the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia), which denied issuance of a petition for writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: The only issue for determination by the trial judge was whether the subject land was legally annexed so as to become a part of the City of Atlanta and under its jurisdiction rather than remaining outside the corporate limits and being under the jurisdiction of Fulton County. The trial judge found that there were no issues of fact for determination; and held as a matter of law that the subject land was legally annexed by the City of Atlanta so as to come within the city's jurisdiction; and he denied appellant's prayer for the issuance of a writ of mandamus. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Ga. Code Ann. § 69-904 was a "general law" and provided a method of municipal annexation as contemplated by the 1965 Home Rule Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 69-1016, and that laws that operated uniformly throughout the state with respect to the subject-matter, but applied only to cities or counties of a common class having a certain number of inhabitants or more, were general statutes having uniform operation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Camp v. Metropolitan Atlanta Rapid Transit Authority


No. 27156


Supreme Court of Georgia


229 Ga. 35; 189 S.E.2d 56; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 940


March 15, 1972, Argued  
April 6, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wofford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted the motion of defendants, authority, revenue commissioner, and county commissioners, to dismiss the taxpayer's complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed a complaint against defendants seeking declaratory and injunctive relief with regard to the Metropolitan Atlanta Rapid Transit Authority (MARTA) Act and the authorization of taxes by it. The trial court denied injunctive relief and granted defendants' motion to dismiss. The taxpayer appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. Ga. Const. art. XVII, § I, paras. I-V, Ga. Code Ann. §§ 2-8601- 2-8605, was properly ratified because it should have been submitted only to the named city and counties for ratification as the provision did not directly effect the state as a whole. The court rejected the taxpayer's argument that the MARTA Act was unconstitutional as violative of Ga. Const. art. III, § VII, para. VIII because all the provisions of the MARTA Act related to the subject matter of creating a rapid transit system and the title of the Act and its amendments put legislators on notice that the Act imposed a financing system. The sales and use tax levied under § 25 of the MARTA Act was not unconstitutional because there was no requirement that the persons paying the taxes receive equal benefits from the facilities for which the taxes are used.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court granting defendants' motion to dismiss the taxpayer's complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief.

McGuire v. McGuire


No. 27018


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 782; 187 S.E.2d 859; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 907


February 14, 1972, Submitted  
March 9, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Alimony modification. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Flexer.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband challenged a decision from the Glynn Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled his motion to dismiss an action brought by appellee former wife to modify the terms of a Florida divorce and support decree so as to require the husband to pay triple the amount previously ordered for the support of the parties' children. The husband alleged, in part, that the court was without jurisdiction of the subject matter.


OVERVIEW: The controlling question to be answered was whether a Georgia court could modify a final decree of a court of a foreign state, Florida, which awarded permanent alimony for support of minor children. The court reversed the trial court's decision to overrule the husband's motion to dismiss the wife's action. The court held that, under 1955 Ga. Laws 630, codified at Ga. Code Ann. §§ 30-220, 30-223, amended by 1969 Ga. Laws 98, codified at Ga. Code Ann. § 30-225(1) (effective March 17, 1969), it could not. The instant proceeding was expressly based on the 1955 law, and such law applied only to the modification of Georgia final decrees so as to permanent alimony; and, because the instant petition sought a modification of a final Florida decree, the trial court should have sustained the motion to dismiss the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that overruled the husband's motion to dismiss the wife's action in her attempt to modify the Florida divorce decree.

Johnson v. Caldwell


No. 27006


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 776; 187 S.E.2d 844; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 906


February 14, 1972, Submitted  
March 9, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Tattnall Superior Court. Before Judge Caswell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed denial of his writ of habeas corpus against defendant warden by the Superior Court of Tattnall County (Georgia). Defendant had been convicted by the same court of the murder of a police officer and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: The inmate contended he was deprived of effective assistance of counsel at trial, but the court held that this was mere hindsight. The inmate's contention that his confession was erroneously admitted was contrary to the facts, which showed that a Jackson-Denno hearing had been held and there was evidence that Miranda requirements had been met. The inmate failed to show that any person with scruples against the death penalty was excluded from service on the jury. The jury was properly instructed because the principles of manslaughter were not involved in the evidence. Such a complaint could not have been raised in a habeas corpus proceeding. There was no election for a jury trial based upon unconstitutional coercion. The inmate, who was African American, urged that he was denied equal protection and due process of law because he was indicted by a grand jury and tried by a traverse jury which were drawn from a jury list that did not represent a fair cross-section of the community, contrary to O.C.G.A. § 59-106 et seq., but the statistics presented by the testimony failed to establish a prima facie case of discrimination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Road Builders, Inc. v. Hawes


Nos. 26856, 26857


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 608; 187 S.E.2d 287; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 862


December 13, 1971, Argued  
February 11, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motor fuel tax; constitutional question. Dade Superior Court. Before Judge Painter.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the final judgments of the Superior Court of Dade County (Georgia), which assessed their tax liability under the State Motor-Fuel Tax Law, specifically O.C.G.A. § 92-1403(E)(1) (amended 1966).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers' companion appeals contended that O.C.G.A. § 92-1403(E)(1) (amended 1966) was unconstitutional because it contained matter not expressed in the title. Section 92-1403(E)(1) provided that in no case were the exemptions provided by the paragraph to have been allowed upon motor fuel used for the purpose of construction, reconstruction, maintenance, or repair of public highways. Although § 92-1403(E)(1) (amended 1966) had the effect of eliminating a theretofore existing exemption, the court was unable to say that the provision was not germane to the provisions of the State Motor-Fuel Tax Law specifically referred to in the caption, which was notice that the particular section granting the exemption was being repealed and reenacted. The phrase, "in order to clarify the legislative intent," in the caption considered with the fact that the statute had already been judicially construed, showed a clear intent to deal comprehensively with the subject matter prospectively. Thus, the court held that § 92-1403(E)(1) (amended 1966) was constitutional and applicable to the taxpayers. Therefore, the trial court did not err in its judgments assessing their tax liability based thereon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1038 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Harrison v. May


No. 26847


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 684; 187 S.E.2d 673; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 885


November 9, 1971, Argued  
February 11, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 28, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Peeler.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a county and the chairman and members of the county board of commissioners, challenged a judgment by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) holding 1956 Ga. Laws 2764 (Act) to be constitutional and granting mandamus absolute to defendants, officers and members of a county board of education and the county school superintendent. Plaintiffs had sought declaratory relief as to the parties' rights and responsibilities arising under the Act.


OVERVIEW: The Act required the commissioners of roads and revenues to pay to the county board of education a set amount per month from funds derived from sources other than taxes. The county board of education passed a resolution directing the superintendent to demand payment of the sum from the commissioners. The commissioners refused to make the payment demanded, and plaintiffs sought a declaration that the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court found the Act to be constitutional, dismissed plaintiff's prayer for summary judgment, and granted defendant's prayer for mandamus absolute. Reversing, the court held that the Act was unconstitutional and void as being in violation of Ga. Const. of 1945, art. VIII, § XII, para. I, as amended. The court concluded that any fines, forfeitures, and license fees were required to be paid into the county treasury and deposited with the general funds derived from taxes. The funds thus became a part of the general operating funds of the county, which had to be applied only to those purposes for which the county had authority to spend tax moneys as provided by the Georgia Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

DeKalb County v. Atlanta Gas Light Co.


Nos. 26815, 26816, 26817


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 512; 186 S.E.2d 732; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 820


November 9, 1971, Argued  
January 6, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hubert.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Chairman and Members of the Board of Commissioners of Roads and Revenues and other county officials challenged the judgments of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) in cases brought by respondents Atlanta Gas Light Company, Southern Bell Telephone & Telegraph Company, and Georgia Power Company, which declared an ordinance of the county to be null and void, and granted interlocutory injunction against its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: Appellants enacted an ordinance required respondent companies doing business in the unincorporated area of the county, and using rights of way owned, acquired, and maintained by the county, to obtain a license for such privilege. Electric and gas companies were required to pay a percentage of non-industrial gross revenue from sales in the area, and telephone companies were required to pay sums based on the number of telephones in service in the area. The ordinance also required a fee of $ 75 and $ .50 per square yard before any company could make any cut, excavation, or tunnel in, upon, under, or across any sidewalk, roadbed, street, pavement, or right of way in the area, in addition to restoring such area to its previous condition. The ordinance provided for fine and imprisonment for any person violating it. The trial court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional and issued an injunction enjoining respondent from enforcing it. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that because the ordinance did not regulate respondents, it was not a licensing ordinance, rather it was a taxing ordinance, which appellants had no constitutional or statuary authority to impose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not err in holding the ordinance void, and granting interlocutory injunction against its enforcement by appellants.

Dudley v. State


No. 26766


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 551; 186 S.E.2d 875; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 841


October 13, 1971, Argued  
January 6, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 19, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Credit card theft; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Holt.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), of credit card theft, raising numerous issues related to the legality of telephone interceptions and of the search and seizure of his person and business premises.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for credit card theft on numerous grounds, mainly related to his motions to suppress evidence obtained by the search and seizure, executed by agents of the Federal Bureau of Investigation, on warrants issued for the search of his person and the business premises of which he was an occupant. The court affirmed the conviction. It held that 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 2510 - 2518 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I; that the search warrant was not illegal due to the fact that the order authorizing the interception of telephone communications did not show the month and year; that an order authorizing interception of telephone communications was not defective for failure to describe with more particularity the type of conversation to be intercepted; that the search and seizure of the premises was not such a general search as would be unconstitutional; that the hearsay information relied upon in applying for the warrants was mainly from fellow officers engaged in the same investigation and thus was sufficient evidence of probable cause; and that the trial judge did not err in allowing a witness to testify that the character and reputation of defendant were bad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for credit card theft.

 

1041 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Gordon v. Green


No. 26782


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 505; 186 S.E.2d 719; 1972 Ga. LEXIS 819


October 12, 1971, Argued  
January 6, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Bibb State Court. Before Judge Phillips.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment from the State Court of Bibb County (Georgia) that granted habeas corpus absolute to defendant former inmate and ordered his discharge from custody. The trial court sustained the inmate's contentions that challenged the constitutionality of a city ordinance to which he pled guilty of violating, which prohibited the operation of a motor vehicle on the city's streets while under the influence of intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: The city passed the ordinance pursuant to 1955 Ga. Laws 736 et seq. (Act of 1955), which amended § 47 of the Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways in 1953 Ga. Laws § 566 et seq. (Act of 1953). After the inmate pled guilty in the municipal court, he filed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the trial court alleging that the Act of 1955 attempted to create the municipal court and to delegate to the city authority to operate a state court contrary to Ga. Const. art. VI, § I, para. I, O.C.G.A. § 2-3601, and Ga. Const. art. I, § IV, para. I, O.C.G.A. § 2-401. The court held that neither the Act of 1955 nor the city ordinance enacted pursuant to the Act of 1955 were repugnant to the Constitution of the State of Georgia. Therefore, the trial court incorrectly held that the Act of 1955 and the city ordinance were unconstitutional and erred in discharging the inmate from custody. The court ruled that the city had a right to punish as a municipal offense conduct that was also an offense by general law of the State. The court determined that the city's right arose in part from the fact that the Act of 1955 was not a special act, but a general act of statewide application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the state court's judgment.

Moore v. Moore


No. 26839


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 489; 186 S.E.2d 531; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 603


November 8, 1971, Submitted  
December 1, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 17, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Interpleader; constitutional question. Dodge Superior Court. Before Judge O'Connor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant widow appealed an order from the Dodge Superior Court (Georgia), which denied her motion for summary judgment. Defendants, a parent and the widow, had claimed benefits under a decedent's insurance policy, which was held by plaintiff insurance company. The insurance company had interpleaded the proceeds of the insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: The widow killed the decedent and claimed that she was entitled to the proceeds under the decedent's insurance policy either under 5 U.S.C.S. § 8705 or because she was the named beneficiary. The parent of the decedent also made a claim for the proceeds of the policy and stated that she was entitled to the proceeds under Ga. Code Ann. § 56-2506. The widow filed a motion for summary judgment with the trial court and alleged that § 56-2506 was unconstitutional and was in conflict with 5 U.S.C.S. § 8705. The trial court denied her motion for summary judgment, and she appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that because the widow had murdered the decedent, she could not claim the proceeds under the insurance policy. This rule was applicable in both state and federal jurisdictions. The common law principle applied independently of Ga. Code Ann. § 56-2506.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied the widow's motion for summary judgment.

 

1043 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. Haynes


Nos. 26785, 26786


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 462; 186 S.E.2d 115; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 596


October 12, 1971, Argued  
December 1, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 17, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. Spalding Superior Court. Before Judge Whalen.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for mandamus to compel the payment of increased retirement benefits, appellants, a retirement board and related parties, challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Spalding County (Georgia), ordering the board to recompute pension benefits payable to appellee retirees, in accordance with 1970 Ga. Laws 1153-1154. Appellants attacked the constitutionality of the constitutional amendment.


OVERVIEW: The retirees, who were former peace officers, sought an increase in retirement benefits, based on 1970 Ga. Laws 1153-1154, a constitutional amendment, which allowed the general assembly to appropriate funds to increase retirement benefits, after the completion of an individual's service. The board refused to pay the increased benefits on the grounds that the amendment was unconstitutional. The retirees brought an action for mandamus to compel the board to refigure their benefits. The trial court rendered judgment for the retirees and ordered the board to recompute their benefits. Appellants sought further review, and the court reversed. It explained that the words "appropriates funds" in the constitutional amendment meant the appropriation of funds from the state treasury. Thus, it concluded that the constitutional amendment did not apply to the retirement system for peace officers. Accordingly, it held that neither of the retirees was entitled to mandamus absolute to require a recomputation and increase of his retirement benefits in accordance with the constitutional amendment because the service of each had terminated at the time of the effective date of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

DeKalb County v. Carriage Woods Civic Asso.
