Crowder v. Dep't of State Parks


No. 26641


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 436; 185 S.E.2d 908; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 591


September 15, 1971, Argued  
November 18, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 123 Ga. App. 793 (182 SE2d 512).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged an order of the Court of Appeals of Georgia, which dismissed his tort action against appellees, state, Department of State Parks, its director, and the superintendent of the park.


OVERVIEW: The citizen was injured when he fell while using the facilities of the Department of State Parks. The trial court dismissed the citizen's tort action, holding that the state had not waived its sovereign immunity. The court of appeals affirmed. On appeal, the citizen contended that adherence to sovereign immunity deprived him of life, liberty, and property without due process of law and equal protection of law. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment. In so ruling, the court stated that it was not authorized to alter or vary the rule that the state was not amendable to suit without its consent. Rather, authority to do so was within the province of the legislature. Further, immunity applied not only to the state but also to the Department of State Parks, its director, and the superintendent of the park because any judgment in favor of the victim would have had to be satisfied from assets of the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which dismissed the citizen's tort action against the state, Department of State Parks, its director, and the superintendent of the park.

 

1046 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


De Palma v. State


No. 26633


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 272; 185 S.E.2d 53; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 539


September 13, 1971, Argued  
November 5, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Armed robbery. Coweta Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Coweta Superior Court (Georgia) that, upon a jury verdict, convicted defendant of armed robbery. Defendant contended that the evidence was wholly circumstantial, that seizure of stolen items from his apartment was illegal because the items were not specified on the search warrant as items to have been seized, and that the search was an unconstitutional "general search."


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery based on evidence found in his apartment, including burglary tools and the victims' stolen property. The court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) defendant's contention that the evidence was wholly circumstantial had no merit because one of the victims positively identified defendant by his voice, so the burden was not upon the state to prove facts that excluded every reasonable hypothesis save that of defendant's guilt; (2) a charge on circumstantial evidence was not warranted because the evidence was not wholly circumstantial; (3) while the stolen items were not specified on the search warrant, it was reasonable in the search for burglary tools and narcotics to make a thorough search of defendant's apartment, so that when the items were discovered under a mattress and in the back of a dresser, the officers had probable cause to believe that the items were stolen property and subject to seizure; and (4) when the officers had probable cause to believe that the property seized was stolen property, the seizure of property did not make the search an unconstitutional "general" search even though the items were not in the warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for armed robbery.

DeKalb County v. Florentine Corp.


Nos. 26694, 26720, 26695, 26721


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 228; 185 S.E.2d 85; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 529


September 16, 1971, Argued  
October 21, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two actions to declare O.C.G.A. §§ 58-1003, -1010.1 unconstitutional, appellants, DeKalb County (Georgia), commissioners, ordinary, and State of Georgia, challenged summary judgments from the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), in favor of appellee licensees. Appellants asserted that the trial court erred in finding that §§ 58-1003, -1010.1 violated Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the U.S. Const. and Ga. Const.


OVERVIEW: The corporate licensees brought actions against appellants, seeking to declare §§ 58-1003, 58-1010.1 unconstitutional because they required a petition signed by 35 percent of the registered voters of a county as a prerequisite to a liquor referendum. The trial court granted summary judgment to the licensees, ordering the call of an election. Appellants sought review, insisting that the licensees lacked standing to attack the constitutionality of the laws. The court agreed, explaining that, although the licensees could have attacked the statutes as individual citizens and potential consumers of intoxicating liquors, their complaints, brought in their corporate capacities, were based upon their alleged rights to have the liquor referendum laws construed so as to facilitate the issuance to them of licenses to sell intoxicating liquors. The licensees had no property rights to have such licenses issued to them, under O.C.G.A. § 58-1068. Thus, they were without standing to attack the statutes' constitutionality. Further, they were not entitled to continue their purported "lawful" sales of intoxicating liquor, as these were unlawful sales of intoxicating liquor in a dry county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgments in favor of the licensees.

Farmer v. State


No. 26670


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 225; 184 S.E.2d 647; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 527


September 16, 1971, Submitted  
October 21, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bribery; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hubert.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), convicting him of bribery. He asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress wiretap evidence which was obtained without a warrant, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV, and in denying his motion to quash the indictment because it was based on the illegally obtained wiretap evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of bribery and he appealed, urging that the trial court improperly refused to suppress wiretap evidence from a warrantless wiretap and erred in failing to quash the indictment that had been based on the fruits of the illegal wiretap. The State contended that the wiretap evidence was admissible in evidence even though obtained without the proper warrants because it was not unlawful. The court disagreed, explaining that the fact that the wiretap was not subject to prosecution under the statutes, did not alter the mandate of the Fourth Amendment, which rendered a warrantless wiretap an unlawful search and seizure. Thus, the court held that the wiretap evidence should not have been admitted. The court further held that the trial court properly denied the motion to quash the indictment because the evidence that the grand jury had received in finding a true bill was not subject to inquiry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1049 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


No. 26669


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 145; 184 S.E.2d 453; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 488


September 13, 1971, Argued  
October 7, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Burglary; constitutional question. Coffee Superior Court. Before Judge Hodges.



DISPOSITION: Transferred to the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Coffee County (Georgia), convicting him of burglary. He attacked the constitutionality of "the Acts of 1970."


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary, and he appealed, urging that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to evidence on the grounds that "the Acts of 1970" were unconstitutional. The court determined that it had no jurisdiction over the appeal. It noted that to properly raise a question as to the constitutionality of a "law" required: (1) stating the statute or the particular part or parts of a statute being challenged with fair precision; (2) clearly designating the constitutional provision allegedly violated; and (3) showing wherein the statute, or some designated part of it, violated such constitutional provision. The court held that defendant's attempted attack on the constitutionality of "the Acts of 1970" utterly failed to meet the first two of these requirements, if not in fact the third, and was, therefore, insufficient to draw in question before the trial court the constitutionality of any law. As the question had not been raised properly in the trial court, the enumeration of error failed to confer jurisdiction on the court. The court found no other basis on which to exercise jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the appeal to the appellate court.

S. R. Co. v. Ins. Co. of N. Am.


No. 26603


Supreme Court of Georgia


228 Ga. 23; 183 S.E.2d 912; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 453


July 13, 1971, Argued  
September 8, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Constitutional question. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Tidwell.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad sought review of a judgment of the Civil Court of Fulton County (Georgia) that denied the railroad's motions for summary judgment in appellees', brick company and insurer, suit for damage caused to the brick company's property.


OVERVIEW: The railroad entered into a contract with the brick company for the construction of an overhead conveyor above an industrial track and an unloading pit beneath the track. The contract included a covenant to indemnify the railroad from loss, injury, or damage in connection with the facilities, resulting from the railroad's negligence or otherwise. The insurer sued the railroad after the brick company's property was damaged by the railroad. The railroad raised as a defense the indemnification covenant contained in the contract. The trial court held that the covenant was void as against public policy pursuant to a 1970 amendment to Ga. Code Ann. § 20-504. The railroad, contending that the amendment was unconstitutional, appealed. The court reversed as to the denial of its summary judgment motion against the insurer and affirmed the denial of its summary judgment motion against the brick company. The amendment was not subject to constitutional attack; however, it was not applicable here because the amendment was not intended to apply to contractual rights accruing prior to its enactment, which was the case here.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part a judgment denying the railroad's motions for summary judgment in an action against it by appellees for damage caused to the brick company's property.

Forbes v. Lovett


No. 26551


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 772; 183 S.E.2d 371; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 840


June 14, 1971, Argued  
July 9, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge McMillan from Middle Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two individuals, filed an action in the Superior Court of Chatham County (Georgia) to compel defendant county commissioners to appoint the individuals to their posts as members on a county civil service board following an election. The trial court granted the commissioners' motion to dismiss the action and denied mandamus. The individuals sought review of the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The individuals alleged that the Georgia legislature had created a civil service system for the county and established a civil service board, that they had been duly elected to the board, but that the commissioners refused to perform their public duty of appointing the individuals to the board. The commissioners filed a motion to dismiss asserting that the individuals had no legal right to the claimed posts. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of mandamus on the ground that the provision of 1969 Ga. Laws under which the individuals claimed the right to office was expressly repealed by an ordinance adopted by the commissioners as authorized by the Home Rule Amendment for Counties to the Georgia Constitution, O.C.G.A. § 2-8402 et seq. As to a claim that the commissioners had a duty to appoint the individuals because at the time they appeared before the board of commissioners the ordinance had not yet been certified by the Secretary of State as required by the Home Rule Amendment, the court ruled that although the individuals might have been entitled to mandamus on the date they appeared before the board they were not entitled to mandamus after the ordinance became effective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

DeKalb County v. Brown Builders Co.


No. 26554


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 777; 183 S.E.2d 367; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 842

Corley v. Lewless

Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 745; 182 S.E.2d 766; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 827

June 17, 1971, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and uncle, sought review of an order of the Richmond Superior Court (Georgia), which denied their motion for summary judgment in appellee child's action for damages predicated on Ga. Code Ann. § 105-113.


OVERVIEW: The child was involved in a fracas with other children, including the son and nephew of appellants. The child initiated an action against appellants under Ga. Code. Ann. § 105-113. The trial court denied appellants' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed. Steele v. State


Nos. 26460, 26461, 26462, 26463


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 653; 182 S.E.2d 475; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 807


April 12, 1971, Argued  
June 2, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Malpractice in office; constitutional question. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Sosebee.

These are four separate cases, special presentments in which were returned by a grand jury in Henry County. Defendant Austin is charged with fourteen counts of malpractice in office for various transactions as alleged in the presentment against him. The other three defendants are each charged with twelve counts of malpractice in office for the same conduct as that charged against defendant Austin. The difference in numbers of counts arises by reason of the fact that some of the other three defendants did not participate in all of the transactions as charged against defendant Austin. Identical demurrers were filed in each case and the issues of law presented with respect to each case are identical. All demurrers were overruled and certificates of review voluntarily given by the court.

Each of the defendants is charged with the offense of malpractice in office for conduct allegedly occurring on specified dates. The conduct charged to be malpractice in office is the doing of certain acts on the dates specified without following the provisions of Sections 10 and 12 of Georgia Laws of [***2] 1921, page 490 et seq. which, it is alleged, constitutes malpractice in office in violation of Code § 89-9907. In view of the fact that the special presentment against defendant Austin in Case No. 26461 contains charges which are common to all of the defendants in this brief, we will rule on the charges against Austin separately, for a disposition of the various counts with respect to him will dispose of the counts against the other defendants which are common to those against Austin.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, four county commissioners who were charged with malpractice in office, appealed from a judgment of the Henry Superior Court (Georgia), which denied their demurrers to the presentments against them, which were returned by a grand jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with malpractice in office concerning the entering of certain contracts and accepting of certain bids. The trial court overruled defendants' demurrers to the charges against them. In reversing in part, the court found that all of the counts charging that defendants improperly "authorized" purchases to be made without obtaining three bids were defective because the law applicable did not provide that "authorizing" a contract was equivalent to "entering into" or "making" a contract under O.C.G.A. § 26-601. Further, the act creating the county board of which defendants were members contained no provision for receiving three bids for services. Thus, the counts alleging that defendants improperly failed to receive three bids were defective and subject to the demurrers urged. In addition, a charge that defendants failed to accept the lowest bid for a "comparable model" was defective because it failed to sufficiently allege that the lowest bids were for goods of the same quality. In affirming the trial court's judgment in part, the court found that certain statutory provisions that defendants challenged were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portions of the trial court's judgment , which overruled the demurrers charging that defendants authorized purchases to be made without obtaining three bids and that defendants failed to accept the lowest bid. The court reversed other portions of the trial court's judgment in which the allegations lacked the requisite specificity. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment.

Prudential Ins. Co. v. Willis

227 Ga. 619; 182 S.E.2d 420; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 799

1056 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bentley v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. 26272


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 708; 182 S.E.2d 770; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 822


March 9, 1971, Argued  
May 20, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 17, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 122 Ga. App. 738 (178 SE2d 700).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in part; affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Georgia Insurance Commissioner challenged the order of the Court of Appeals (Georgia), which held that the commissioner erred in disapproving of appellee insurer's homeowner's insurance premium rates as excessive under Ga. Code Ann. § 56-507(a).


OVERVIEW: The commissioner determined that a reasonable degree of competition in pricing was absent and ordered the insurer to reduce its premiums. The insurer appealed. The appellate court reversed. The commissioner appealed. The court reversed in part and affirmed in part. Under § 56-507(a), rates were excessive only where the rate was unreasonably high and there was not a reasonable degree of competition. The commissioner's determination that there was competition in service but not competition in rates was reasonable. The court rejected the insurer's assertion that its rates were not unreasonable because they were lower than the majority of companies because under Ga. Code Ann. §§ 56-507(b), (c) the excessiveness of rates was to be individually examined for each insurer. When the insurer's individual performance was examined it was apparent that profits were higher than average and the rate increases were excessive in view of the insurer's actual experience. The court affirmed the appellate determination that unfair discrimination arose where like policyholders were treated differently, but found it had not application to excessive rates under Ga. Code Ann. § 56-507(d).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court, which reversed the commissioner's finding that the insurer's rates charged for homeowner's insurance were excessive, and affirmed the determination that rate discrimination was irrelevant.

 

1057 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Partain v. Maddox


Nos. 26441, 26447


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 623; 182 S.E.2d 450; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 800


April 14, 1971, Argued  
May 20, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Hames.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in the main appeal affirmed in part, reversed in part; judgment in the cross appeal reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff board member and defendant chairman appealed from the Cobb County Superior Court (Georgia) judgment that a temporary restraining order remain in effect and sustaining the chairman's motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of indispensable parties in the member's action seeking damages and an injunction to prevent interference with performance of his public duties and the chairman's action in quo warranto.


OVERVIEW: When the member was appointed to the parole board, he gave the governor a signed and undated resignation letter. Later, the governor accepted the resignation. The member filed an action against the chairman seeking damages and an injunction prohibiting interference with the performance of his duties. After a temporary restraining order (TRO) issued, the chairman filed a motion to dismiss and an action in quo warranto. The trial court ruled that the TRO remain in effect pending trial and that the motion to dismiss be granted for failure to join the member's replacement as an indispensable party. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed it in part. The court ruled that the governor lacked authority to shorten the seven-year term mandated by Ga. Const. art. V, § I, para. XI and Ga. Code Ann. § 2-3011. The court ruled that the member did not abandon his office or cease to perform his duties for purposes of Ga. Code Ann. § 89-501. The court ruled that the replacement was not an indispensable party because he never took the oath of office or laid claim to the office. The court also ruled that the member was entitled to the TRO pending a determination of rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court sustaining the chairman's motion to dismiss for lack of indispensable parties and ruling that the issue of the member's resignation be tried to a jury. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the member was entitled to injunctive relief.

 

1058 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. Brown


Nos. 26427, 26428


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 549; 181 S.E.2d 840; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 768


April 12, 1971, Argued  
May 6, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Election contest; constitutional question. Franklin Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an election contest for the offices of mayor and city councilman, appellant candidates, who were declared elected upon a plurality of the votes, challenged a judgment of the Franklin Superior Court (Georgia), which found that a majority vote was required for election and ordered runoff elections.


OVERVIEW: Appellants claimed that O.C.G.A. § 34A-1501(a) was unconstitutional because of failure to provide for notice hearing to the successful candidate in a municipal election. The provision of the statute attacked provided that upon the filing of a contest petition, a hearing would be set and conducted in accordance with certain standards. The court found that no hearing was held by the municipal governing authority because the disqualification of certain members prevented a quorum. The contests were appealed by consent of the parties to the trial court. Thus, appellants could not challenge the constitutionality of a statute for failure to provide due process for a hearing that they had waived. The court also rejected the argument of the candidate for councilman that a presumption existed that the city exercised its charter power to provide that councilmen would be elected by a plurality of votes and that the burden of proof was on the contesting party to show otherwise. The court held that the burden was on the candidate for councilman to show an exception to the general provisions of the Municipal Election Code requiring a majority vote.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Doraville v. S. R. Co.


No. 26357


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 504; 181 S.E.2d 346; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 755


March 9, 1971, Argued  
April 22, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed a judgment of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), in favor of defendant railroad companies, in the city's action that sought to temporarily and permanently enjoin the railroad companies from constructing a proposed switching yard facility within the city limits.


OVERVIEW: The railroad companies applied to the Georgia Public Service Commission (commission) and sought authority under Ga. Code Ann. § 94-321 (1933) to institute condemnation proceedings for purposes of constructing a new railroad switching yard. The city presented evidence at the hearing of new city ordinances that prevented the proposed yard. The commission granted the authority requested. The railroad companies began the condemnation proceedings, two of which were against the city. The superior court entered judgment in favor of the railroad companies. The city filed a complaint for an injunction to prevent the construction. The court granted the railroad companies' motion to dismiss, which the court affirmed. The court found that the railroad companies' application to the commission complied with § 94-321, and that the rights sought were necessary and essential for the construction of the proposed yard. The court held that the city could not by ordinance impose upon a public utility essential to the welfare of the people, conditions of operation or maintenance of its property, which would confiscate or destroy its power to serve the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that granted the railroad companies' motion to dismiss the city's complaint that sought to temporarily and permanently enjoin the railroad companies from constructing a proposed railroad switching yard after the commission gave the railroad companies the authority to institute condemnation proceedings regarding the proposed property.

 

1060 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Burson v. Faith


No. 26310


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 526; 181 S.E.2d 827; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 761


February 9, 1971, Argued  
April 12, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 6, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Director of the Department of Public Safety of the State of Georgia, challenged a judgment from the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) that denied the Director's motion to dismiss for improper venue plaintiff driver's action against the Director that arose when the driver's license was suspended under the state's "Implied Consent Law." Defendant officer appealed a judgment that was rendered against him.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license was suspended pursuant to the implied consent law. The driver named the Director and the officer, who was the Director's subordinate, in their individual capacities. On appeal, the court ruled that the Director's motion to dismiss should have been granted because venue as to him was in the county of residence, and not in the forum county. Because no activity in individual capacity was alleged and because none could be alleged to authorize the relief sought, the only theory upon which the driver could proceed, under the driver's allegations, was that defendants were acting under color of their offices. In such case they were required by law to act as they did until the implied consent law was held to be unconstitutional. They were not guilty of concerted action that authorized a complaint against either of them outside of their counties of residence. Moreover, because the driver did not exhaust his administrative remedies by challenging the suspension in the superior court of the county of his residence, or that of Fulton County, Georgia, under O.C.G.A. §, 3A-120, the driver lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the implied consent law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that denied the Director's motion to dismiss and reversed the judgment that was rendered against the officer.

 

1061 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Lane v. Morrison


No. 26390


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 468; 181 S.E.2d 339; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 740


March 8, 1971, Submitted  
April 8, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Arbitration. Stewart Superior Court. Before Judge Marshall.



DISPOSITION: Transferred to the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee board of tax assessors and others challenged sought review in the Stewart Superior Court (Georgia) of an award of arbitrators decreasing the valuation of real and personal property of appellant taxpayer for ad valorem taxation from that set by the assessors. The taxpayer appealed from the trial court's denial of her motion to declare unconstitutional O.C.G.A. § 92-6912.


OVERVIEW: Section 92-6912 granted the right of appeal from the arbitrators' decision when the difference between the valuation of the board of tax assessors and the valuation of the arbitrators exceeded $ 1,000. The ground of the attack was that the statute was discriminatory in that it denied to the taxpayer the equal protection of the laws in violation of Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. II. The court held that to raise a question as to the constitutionality of a statute, it had to be shown wherein the statute violated the constitutional provision specified. The taxpayer's constitutional attack failed to state wherein the statute was discriminatory in violation of the constitutional provision specified. The attack was insufficient to raise the question of the statute's constitutionality. Because there was no other basis for the court's jurisdiction, the case had to be transferred to a court of appeals.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case to the court of appeals.

Mayson v. Davis


No. 26185


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 399; 181 S.E.2d 64; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 715


November 12, 1970, Argued  
March 18, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a city director of finance, filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, several individuals and corporations, court officials, a sheriff, and an ordinary, to have § 5A of the Act approved March 24, 1970, 1970 Ga. Laws 724-728, declared unconstitutional. Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which declared the law unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Section 5A of the Act provided that O.C.G.A. ch. 46-8 was amended by striking O.C.G.A. § 46-805 in its entirety. O.C.G.A. ch. 46-8 was one of several chapters covering the garnishment law. The trial court declared § 5A of the Act to be unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that § 5A was unconstitutional because it failed to comply with Ga. Const. art. III, § VII, para. XVI, which provided that any act amending or repealing a law or statute had to distinctly describe the law to be amended or repealed, as well as the alteration to be made. The court concluded that § 5A of the Act failed to contain a sufficient description of the content of O.C.G.A. § 46-805.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1063 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Evans Theatre Corp. v. Slaton


No. 26249


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 377; 180 S.E.2d 712; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 710


January 13, 1971, Argued  
March 4, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant litigants challenged a decision from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which enjoined the litigants from showing or exhibiting a certain film after the trial court determined the film was obscene. Plaintiff district attorney brought an action for an injunction against the showing of the film. The trial court also ordered the film seized as contraband.


OVERVIEW: At the hearing the trial judge viewed the film before making his finding that it was obscene. The film was produced in Sweden. It showed a young Swedish woman questioning the social, political, and moral values of her own country and other countries. In extended scenes the young woman and her various partners were shown in explicit sex scenes. On appeal, the litigants argued that the failure of the district attorney to introduce any evidence of community standards to determine the question of obscenity required a reversal of the judgment finding the film obscene. The court held that after viewing the film themselves, the trial judge did not err in finding the film obscene, whether viewed by the standards of the local community or national standards. The court held that the fact that the film contained some non-obscene matter did not preclude a finding it was utterly without redeeming social value. The court affirmed the finding that the film was obscene. The court held that where the welfare of the whole community was served by restraining the showing of the obscene film, a court of equity was authorized to enjoin the exhibition of the obscene film to the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision enjoining the litigants from showing the film in question. However, the court directed that the trial court's order be amended to show that it was not a permanent injunction, but only one to continue in force until the final hearing of the case by a jury.

Johnston v. State


No. 26330


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 387; 181 S.E.2d 42; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 713


February 8, 1971, Submitted  
March 4, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Possession of drugs; constitutional question. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.

The defendants were arrested on August 26, 1969, in a motel room in Bibb County, rented by one of them. The arrest resulted from a search of the premises executed under a search warrant of the same date. The search revealed quantities of LSD and "marijuana" (as spelled in Code Ann. § 79A-903 (b, 5) Ga. L. 1967, pp. 296, 344, as amended, Ga. L. 1970, pp. 470, 471; or "marihuana," as spelled in Code Ann. § 79A-802 (13), Ga. L. 1967, pp. 296, 325, as amended, Ga. L. 1970, p. 470) and the defendants were charged with possession of narcotic drugs and possession of depressant or stimulant drugs.

The defendants filed demurrers to the indictments and moved to suppress evidence obtained as a result of the search on the grounds that the warrants were invalid due to their insufficiency to establish probable cause and that the search exceeded the scope authorized by the warrants.

After hearing on the issues presented, the trial judge overruled the demurrers to the indictments and the motions to suppress. The joint nonjury trial of both defendants resulted in [***2] their convictions on two counts, hereinabove stated, from which judgment they appeal. Enumerated as error are the overruling of the defendants' motion for a new trial, their second and third demurrers to Count 2 of their indictments and their motion to suppress evidence.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Bibb Superior Court (Georgia), which denied their motions to suppress evidence found during the execution of a warrant, and which convicted them of possession of drugs in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 79A-903(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: After an informant advised law enforcement officials regarding defendants' possession of illicit drugs, a search warrant was executed at the hotel where defendants were staying. When drugs were found, defendants were charged with and convicted of possession of drugs in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 79A-903(b)(3). Defendants appealed, and the court affirmed their convictions, holding that the trial court had properly denied the motions to suppress evidence because the State met its burden of proving that the search warrant was valid. The officer's affidavit gave sufficient information of the underlying circumstances from which he concluded that the informant was reliable. Further, the occurrence of the facts listed in the affidavit were recent enough to create a reasonable belief that the same conditions described in the affidavit still prevailed at the time of the issuance of the warrant. Section 79A-903(b)(3) was constitutional because although it referenced federal law, it did not make future federal legislation a part of the law in the State upon that subject. Further, any change to the federal law would not have any effect upon § 79A-903(b)(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

1066 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Mitchum v. Stynchcombe


No. 26125


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 226; 179 S.E.2d 919; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 649


October 14, 1970, Submitted  
January 29, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge McKenzie.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) remanding the inmate to custody under an executive warrant granting extradition to a demanding state and denying habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate challenged the validity of the executive warrant on appeal, arguing that the demand, requisition, and supporting documents showed that the inmate was not a fugitive within the accepted meaning of that term. The inmate also contended that the statute of the demanding state under which he was charged was held to be unconstitutional. The court held that when, in the trial of a habeas corpus case, a petitioner was held in custody under an executive warrant based upon an extradition proceeding, and the warrant was regular on its face, the burden was on the petitioner to show some valid and sufficient reason why the warrant should not be executed. The presumption of the validity of the warrant continued until the contrary appeared. Upon such a showing, however, evidence as to the guilt or innocence of the inmate was not relevant because the courts of the asylum state could inquire into that question or into the constitutionality of the law under which the inmate was charged in the demanding state. In affirming, the court held that the warrant was issued pursuant O.C.G.A. § 44-407 of the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act and was not void for any reason urged by the inmate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Black v. Blanchard


No. 26073


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 167; 179 S.E.2d 228; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 627


September 16, 1970, Argued  
January 11, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Quo warranto. Columbia Superior Court. Before Judge Kennedy.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county residents challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Columbia County (Georgia), which, in the county residents' quo warranto action, entered an order finding that appellee superintendent was qualified to hold the office of Superintendent of Schools of Columbia County and that 1963 Ga. Laws 356-357 did not violate Ga. Const. art. I, § IV, par. I, the state constitution's equal protection clause.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed a law that greatly increased the minimal professional requirements for all county school superintendents; however, it also exempted, or grandfathered in, individuals who already held such positions when the act became effective or had served at least one term as a county school superintendent. Some county residents argued that provision violated the state constitution's equal protection clause and that the current superintendent of Columbia County schools was not qualified. The trial court disagreed, and the residents sought review. On review, the court held that the purpose of the act was to insure that qualified people held the office of county school superintendents. Permitting a class of experienced people to retain their positions despite the additional qualifications was a judgment call of the legislature that the court had to respect unless it was blatantly wrong. The court held that it could not say as a matter of law that permitting experienced people to keep their jobs was not a legitimate ground of differentiation or bore no reasonable relation to the law's objectives. Because the law applied to all candidates statewide, it was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Atlanta Processing Co. v. Brown


No. 26231


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 203; 179 S.E.2d 752; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 639; 3 ERC (BNA) 1319; 2 ELR 20114


December 15, 1970, Argued  
January 7, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 21, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Banke.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant processing plant sought review of a decision of the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), which denied its motions to dismiss and motion for new trial in plaintiff's action against the plant seeking a declaration that the plant was a public nuisance and an injunction against the plant's emission of noxious odors.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action seeking a declaration that the plant was a public nuisance and an injunction prohibiting the plant from operating in such a way as to emit offensive odors. The plant filed two motions to dismiss, arguing that the laws regarding nuisances were unconstitutionally vague, which were denied. Pursuant to a jury verdict the court entered a judgment declaring the plant a public nuisance and enjoining it from emitting the offensive odors. The plant filed a motion for new trial, which was denied, and it appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found no merit to the motions to dismiss because the nuisance laws were not vague. The court found sufficient evidence to sustain the jury verdict because plaintiff produced 25 witnesses who testified about the adverse effects of the plant's odors on their lifestyles, families, and businesses. The court found that the evidence met the requirement of Ga. Code Ann. § 72-102, which defined a public nuisance as one that damaged all persons who came within the sphere of its operations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the plant's motions to dismiss and motion for new trial.

 

1069 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dougherty County v. Bush


No. 26190


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 137; 179 S.E.2d 343; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 614


December 14, 1970, Argued  
January 7, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Kelley.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Dougherty County (Georgia), which upheld the constitutionality of a statute that required counties with populations between 70,000 and 110,000 residents to create a board known as the board of trustees of the county law library. Appellants' complaint was dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted a statute that required counties with populations between 70,000 and 110,000 residents to create a county law library. The population determination was to be made under the 1960 United States census or any future census. Under the 1960 census, one county was affected; under the 1970 census, four counties were affected. The statute was challenged, but the trial court determined that it was constitutional. On appeal, the court noted that the legislature could classify for purposes of legislation but that the basis of the classification had to have some reasonable relation to the subject matter of the law. A statute that involved classification by population was required to be a general, not a special statute, which let a county out of the classification as well as in. The classification must not have been crafted to apply to only one county. The classification by population must have had some reasonable relation to the subject matter and a legitimate ground for differentiation. The classification had no reasonable relationship to the subject matter, and it was a special statute that violated the special laws provision of the Georgia Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1070 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Pruitt v. State


No. 26181


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 188; 179 S.E.2d 339; 1971 Ga. LEXIS 633


November 10, 1970, Argued  
January 7, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 21, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Misdemeanor. Houston Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Transferred to the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Houston County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of the possession of gambling devices. Defendant sought direct appeal before the court, and not the Court of Appeals, on the grounds that O.C.G.A. § 26-3004(a) of the Invasion of Privacy Statute, O.C.G.A. § 26-3001 et seq., which exempted law enforcement officers from its application, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The only issue before the court was whether it had the jurisdiction to hear defendant's appeal. Normally, an appeal of a misdemeanor conviction would be before the Court of Appeals. But defendant argued that the portion of the Invasion of Privacy Statute that precluded its operation against law enforcement officers was unconstitutional and that, therefore, the evidence in his case should have been suppressed. On review, the court held that it had a duty to determine whether it had the jurisdiction to hear the appeal. To determine that, the court had to decide if a constitutional question was presented on the record. The court concluded that based on the record, the police officer viewed the illegal gambling equipment from a public place, as defined by O.C.G.A. § 26-401(M), and not a private place protected under the statute. Consequently, the constitutionality of the statute was not at issue, and the jurisdiction of the appeal rested solely with the Court of Appeals.


OUTCOME: The court held that it had no jurisdiction to hear defendant's appeal and transferred the case to the Court of Appeals.

 

1071 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Gornto v. State


No. 26166


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 46; 178 S.E.2d 894; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 394


November 9, 1970, Argued  
December 3, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Distributing obscene materials; constitutional question. Glynn State Court. Before Judge Little.

This is an appeal from a conviction, in the State Court of Glynn County, of the offense of distributing obscene materials, Code Ann. § 26-2101 (Ga. L. 1968, pp. 1249, 1302), which provides in part as follows: "(a) A person commits the offense of distributing obscene materials when he sells, lends, rents, leases, gives, advertises, publishes, exhibits or otherwise disseminates to any person any obscene material of any description, knowing the obscene nature thereof, or who offers to do so, or who possesses such material with the intent so to do. (b) Material is obscene if considered as a whole, applying community standards, its predominant appeal is to prurient interest, that is, a shameful or morbid interest in nudity, sex or excretion, and utterly without redeeming social value and if, in addition, it goes substantially beyond customary limits of candor in describing or representing such matters. Undeveloped photographs, molds, printing plates and the like shall be deemed obscene notwithstanding that processing or other acts may be required to make the obscenity patent or to disseminate [***2] it. (c) Material, not otherwise obscene, may be deemed obscene under this section if the distribution thereof, or the offer to do so, or the possession with the intent to do so is a commercial exploitation of erotica solely for the sake of their prurient appeal."



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Glynn State Court (Georgia) convicting him of the offense of distributing obscene materials, a violation of O.C.G.A. § 26-2101. The trial court denied defendant's motions to dismiss, for a directed verdict, for a new trial, and in arrest of judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal from his conviction for the distribution of obscene materials that O.C.G.A. § 26-2101 was not violative of the First and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution on the ground of vagueness. On review, the court disagreed. The court also disagreed with the argument that § 26-2101 was violative of the First, Fourth, Fifth, Ninth, and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution on the ground that the constitutional right to mere possession of obscene material necessarily implied the right to purchase such material and, hence, the right of others to distribute it. The court relied on a United States Supreme Court opinion which specifically negated any relationship of interdependence between the states' recognized broad power to regulate the public distribution of obscenity and the mere possession of such material by the individual in the privacy of his home. In affirming, the court held that the jury was correctly charged as to the statutory definition of obscene material, as contained in O.C.G.A. § 26-2101(b), (c). The evidence authorized the jury's finding that the material sold by defendant came within the statutory definition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1072 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Plantation Pipe Line Co. v. City of Bremen


No. 25873


Supreme Court of Georgia


227 Ga. 1; 178 S.E.2d 868; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 381


June 8, 1970, Argued  
November 23, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petition. Haralson Superior Court. Before Judge Winn.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a company and two county boards of education, appealed an order of the Haralson Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained appellee city's motion to dismiss the petition attacking certain statutes and annexation ordinances and sought an injunction to prevent the city's collection of the 1969 taxes in the annexed areas.


OVERVIEW: The city annexed four tracts of land, two under the 60 percent method and two under the 100 percent method. Two of the annexations extended the city into the neighboring county. Appellants challenged the annexations as violative of Ga. Code Ann. § 69-904 and the trial court dismissed their petition. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that, in view of the local nature of municipal annexation and Ga. Const. art. XV, § I, para. I (1954), the general assembly could delegate its power to extend city boundaries. However, the two annexations under the 60 percent method were illegal and void because they violated the prohibition in Ga. Code Ann. §§ 69-904, 69-908 against the annexation of territory across the boundary lines of political subdivisions. A school district was a political subdivision and each county composed one school district; thus, the ban included school districts. Also, because one of the 100 percent annexation ordinances was contiguous to one of the void 60 percent annexations, that 100 percent annexation ordinance was illegal and void and the city had no authority to levy and collect taxes there.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the city's motion to dismiss appellants' petition and intervention, which challenged the city's annexation ordinances.

 

1073 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Campbell v. State


No. 25913


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 883; 178 S.E.2d 257; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 725


July 13, 1970, Argued  
November 5, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 18, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Receiving stolen goods; constitutional question. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Bibb Superior Court (Georgia) convicting him of receiving stolen goods.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that there was an insufficient showing of probable cause to justify the issuance of a search warrant for his home, that the seizure of goods from his home was unconstitutional, and that the record did not show that he knew the seized goods to be stolen. The court held that (1) the affidavit in support of the search warrant set out the names of the persons to be searched, the addresses of the places to be searched, it particularly described the things to be seized and the sworn evidence before the magistrate, considered in its totality, justified the issuance of the search warrant; (2) the seizure of articles from appellant's home which appellant contended were not listed in the search warrant, were not fruits of the crime listed on the warrant, and were not known to be stolen property was not unconstitutional because the seizure was authorized pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 27-303 (1966) and because police officers had probable cause to believe the seized articles were stolen; and (3) jurors had more than the mere fact of appellant's possession of the seized articles to rely on as evidence that he knew they were stolen and thus, appellant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction.

State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Murphy


No. 25916


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 710; 177 S.E.2d 257; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 646


July 13, 1970, Argued  
September 10, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 24, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Coweta Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company appealed a decision from the Coweta Superior Court (Georgia), which awarded damages in favor of defendants, children and administrators of decedent's estate, allowing recovery under the uninsured motorist provisions of two separate insurance policies. The insurance company asserted that the trial court erred in allowing recovery under both policies.


OVERVIEW: The mother of the family was killed while riding as a passenger in a vehicle driven by the insured driver and recovery was sought under the driver's coverage with the insurance company. The insurance company paid the estate's claim and the claims filed by the decedent's children, which were filed under the same policy. The children then sought to recover under the uninsured motorist coverage of the mother's automobile policy with the same insurance company. The trial court denied the insurance company's motion for injunctive relief and denied its prayer for a declaration that the children were not entitled to additional sums, and that the insurance company was not liable to the children under the second policy. The court affirmed the judgment holding that the other insurance provisions of each of the insurance policies was contrary to portions of the uninsured motorist statute and were void.

Smith v. Merchs. & Farmers Bank


Nos. 25926, 25927


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 715; 177 S.E.2d 249; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 647


July 14, 1970, Argued  
September 10, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 24, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Baldwin Superior Court. Before Judge Jackson.

The present action was filed to secure the cancellation of a security deed from the plaintiff's predecessor in title to the defendant bank, and to enjoin both temporarily and permanently the foreclosure of such security deed. The defendant filed numerous defenses including a constitutional attack upon a statute. The trial court sustained the constitutional attack and declared the statute unconstitutional. The plaintiff appeals from such judgment adverse to her while the defendant, by cross appeal, appeals from the judgment of the trial court overruling other defenses. The trial court signed a certificate of immediate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed on main appeal; affirmed on cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff debtor filed an action to secure the cancellation of a security deed from plaintiff's predecessor in title to defendant bank and to enjoin both temporarily and permanently the foreclosure of such security deed. The Baldwin Superior Court (Georgia) declared the Act of 1941, O.C.G.A. § 67-1308 unconstitutional. The debtor appealed the judgment adverse to her, and the bank appealed the trial court's judgment overruling other defenses.


OVERVIEW: The bank argued that the Act was unconstitutional. The court held that as applied to deeds to secure debt executed after the effective date of such Act such Act did not offend the constitutional provisions prohibiting retrospective legislation. The court reversed the judgment declaring the Act unconstitutional and striking allegations with reference to such Act. The bank contended that the Act was unconstitutional because the caption made no reference to the duty of the clerk of the superior court to record deeds to secure debt while the body of the Act made such provision and sets fees for such services. The court held that the language of the title was sufficiently broad to include the language complained of. The bank contended that the trial court erred in overruling its motion to dismiss the cause for failure of the debtor to state a claim. The bank contended that the debtor failed to name a necessary party. The court held that because neither the motion to dismiss nor the judgment of the trial court disclosed any intent to raise or pass upon such question the failure to name the party was an amendable defect not subject to being dismissed for failure to state a claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment on the main appeal by the debtor and affirmed the trial court's judgment on the cross appeal by the bank.

1080 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Barresi v. Browne


Nos. 25703, 25704


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 456; 175 S.E.2d 649; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 564


March 11, 1970, Argued  
June 15, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Clarke Superior Court. Before Judge Barrow.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; affirmed in part on the main appeal. Reversed on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed a decision of the Clarke Superior Court (Georgia) that denied their petition for injunctive relief, which sought to enjoin defendant school board from implementing its proposed school desegregation plan. The board appealed a decision that enjoined them from serving free breakfasts in some schools under the Child Nutrition Act, 42 U.S.C.S. ch. 13A.


OVERVIEW: The board adopted a school desegregation plan. In the plan, white students were bussed distances to predominately Negro schools while Negro students were bussed distances to primarily white schools. As such, white and Negro children were denied admission to public school facilities available to other white and Negro children similarly situated. Parents initiated an action to enjoin the plan on the grounds that it violated the Equal Protection Clause. The parents also alleged that the board's practice of serving free breakfasts in certain schools and not others violated the clause. The trial court denied the injunction regarding the plan, ordered the board to submit a new plan to the trial court, and enjoined the board from serving free breakfasts. In reversing the decision in part, the court found that the plan violated equal protection principles by effectively excluding students from attending a school based upon their race. The trial court also erred in enjoining the board from serving free breakfasts because the board was complying with the Child Nutrition Act. The court affirmed in part the trial court's decision, but did not explain its affirmance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that denied the parents' petition for injunction relief, but affirmed portions of the decision. The court reversed the decision that enjoined the board from serving free breakfasts in some schools.

 

1081 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Pettiford v. Frazier


No. 25787


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 438; 175 S.E.2d 549; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 555


May 11, 1970, Submitted  
June 9, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petition. Ben Hill Superior Court. Before Judge McMurray.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the illegitimate daughter of a decedent, challenged an order of the Ben Hill Superior Court (Georgia), which held that the illegitimate daughter was not entitled to inherit the estate of her father, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 113-904. On appeal, she asserted that § 113-904 was unconstitutional because it violated the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: O.C.G.A. § 113-904 provided that illegitimate children could inherit from their mother and from one another, but did not provide for inheritance from the child's father unless the child was made legitimate under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 74-103. The illegitimate daughter filed an action seeking to inherit her father's estate after he died intestate. The trial court held that she was not entitled to inherit the estate under O.C.G.A. § 113-904. She asserted that the denial of her right of inheritance violated the Fourteenth Amendment by denying her equal protection. The court held that the right of succession to the property of a deceased person was not a natural and inalienable right guaranteed by the Constitution. As such, each state had the power to regulate and control such succession as it deemed necessary. Under Georgia law, the daughter had no right of inheritance, and the denial of her inheritance did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1082 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Pharris v. Mayor


No. 25784


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 489; 175 S.E.2d 845; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 570


May 11, 1970, Argued  
June 9, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 25, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Jackson Superior Court. Before Judge Dunahoo.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, citizens and taxpayers, appealed an order of the Jackson Superior Court (Georgia), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a mayor and city council, in plaintiffs' action for injunctive relief and for a declaratory judgment stating that O.C.G.A. § 69-904, and a city ordinance adopted in accordance, were unconstitutional. The trial court held the Attorney General had not been properly served under O.C.G.A. § 110-1106.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' motion to dismiss asserted that dismissal was required because the record did not show that the Attorney General of Georgia had been served. Section 110-1106 required the Attorney General have been served if the petition sought a declaration that a state statute was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs advised the trial court that they had served a copy of the petition on the Attorney General by letter and that the Attorney General had acknowledged receipt of the petition. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss without allowing plaintiffs to introduce evidence establishing that the Attorney General had been notified and had acknowledged receipt of the petition by mail. It held that the Attorney General had not been properly served. The court held that it was error for the trial court to dismiss the petition on the ground that the record did not show that the Attorney General had been served. Under § 110-1106, the Attorney General was not a party to the proceeding and service of process was not required. He only had to have been given notice of the constitutional attack on the statute and the opportunity to have been heard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment granting defendants' motion to dismiss.

Brown v. Olen


No. 25786


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 492; 175 S.E.2d 838; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 572


May 12, 1970, Argued  
June 9, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 25, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Plea to jurisdiction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Thibadeau.

Mrs. Bennie W. Brown filed an action in the Superior Court of DeKalb County in which she sought to recover from Maurice Olen the amount of a judgment obtained previously against Merit Dollar Stores, Inc. Olen is alleged to be a resident of Alabama and service and jurisdiction is sought under the Act of 1966 (Ga. L. 1966, p. 343) as amended (Code Ann. § 24-113.1 et seq.). The defendant made a special appearance for the purpose of raising the issue of jurisdiction of the court over his person and moved to quash the process on that ground. In addition to alleging that he had not transacted any business in Georgia or committed any tortious act in Georgia, he attacks the above Act as violating various provisions of the State and United States Constitutions "in so far as [the Act] . . . purports," etc. The trial court sustained the defendant's motion "as to jurisdiction" without specifying the ground upon which the judgment was based. The appeal is from this judgment adverse to the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained a motion to dismiss filed by defendant, the principal of a corporation, for a lack of personal jurisdiction over defendant under the Civil Practice Act of 1966.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action seeking to recover from defendant the amount of a judgment she had previously obtained against the corporation. She alleged that defendant was a resident of Alabama, and sought service and jurisdiction under the Act. Defendant made a special appearance and attacked the superior court's jurisdiction over his person. He alleged that he had not transacted any business in Georgia or committed any tortious act in Georgia, and asserted that the Act was unconstitutional. The superior court sustained the motion and plaintiff appealed. The court held that plaintiff's petition was not defective for not being verified, so as to prevent the superior court from obtaining jurisdiction over defendant, because the Act did not require it have been verified. However, the petition did not allege sufficient facts to state a cause of action, precluding the superior court from obtaining jurisdiction over defendant. The petition failed to assert that the corporation's assets had been liquidated or the funds derived therefrom appropriated to defendant's own use. Without such allegations, the petition simply alleged fraud without damage, which was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order sustaining defendant's motion to dismiss.

Pye v. State Highway Dep't


No. 25600


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 389; 175 S.E.2d 510; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 549


January 14, 1970, Submitted  
June 8, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Condemnation of land; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Emeritus Horne.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed the judgment by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted defendant state highway department's motion to strike the portions of the landowner's complaint which sought damages, granted the department's motion for possession of the landowner's property, and dismissed all of the landowner's pleadings except those portions related to questions of value.


OVERVIEW: The department filed a condemnation petition for the landowner's property. The landowner answered the condemnation petition and filed an equitable complaint, and the two proceedings were consolidated. The landowner contended that the amendment to Ga. Const. art. I, § 3, regarding condemnation was never effective because the ballot used was defective. The court held that the ballot was sufficient because it was not necessary that the entire amendment be printed on the ballot. The court held that the condemnation statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 36-1303, did not violate the separation of powers or the landowner's due process or equal protection rights. The court held that the landowner had the right to bring up other defenses besides just compensation, and that the trial court had given him adequate opportunity to do so. The court held that the director of department had the authority to exercise eminent domain powers, that the notice attached to the condemnation petition was adequately certified, and that the condemnation petition was not defective. The court held that the proposed highway was properly established and lawfully designated. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment striking or dismissing all but the valuation contentions from the landowner's complaint and granting the department's motion for possession of the landowner's property.

 

1085 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Harding v. Decatur


No. 25737


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 474; 175 S.E.2d 507; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 568


April 14, 1970, Argued  
May 14, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 9 and June 25, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Peeler.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), which sustained the motion to dismiss of defendants, governmental entities and insurance companies. The claimants' complaint sought to enjoin the governmental entities from collecting ad valorem taxes and to enjoin the insurance companies from paying the taxes.


OVERVIEW: The property owners contended that the assessments on their property were unconstitutional. They sought to enjoin the governmental entities from collecting ad valorem taxes on their property until a proper tax digest and assessment had been made. They also sought to enjoin the insurance companies from disbursing any funds for the payment of the property owners' taxes. The trial court dismissed the property owners' complaint on the motion of the governmental entities and insurance companies. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that the property owners had not done equity by paying taxes owed. Therefore, they were not entitled to equitable relief. O.C.G.A. § 92-6402 required the property owners to pay taxes owed by a certain date. The property owners had not done so. The court found that it was apparent from their complaint that the property owners did not claim that they did not owe any taxes. Therefore, in order to do equity, the taxes acknowledged to be owed must have been paid or tendered in order to afford the property owners an opportunity to have their case considered on the issue that the taxes were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the property owners.

Dennis v. State


No. 25743


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 341; 175 S.E.2d 17; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 534


April 13, 1970, Argued  
May 7, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Operating overweight vehicle; constitutional question. Bibb State Court. Before Judge Phillips.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the State Court of Bibb County (Georgia) upon a conviction for operating an overweight vehicle upon a public highway.


OVERVIEW: A highway patrol officer directed defendant to drive his truck upon scales. Defendant complied, and his truck was determined to be overweight. Defendant was convicted of operating an overweight vehicle upon a public highway. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that the officer was authorized under O.C.G.A. § 68-406.3 to direct defendant to the scales. The court found that the State could impose reasonable conditions on the issuance of a driver's license, including forfeiting a driver's license for 90 days for failure to comply with an officer's direction to have a vehicle weighed. The court found that defendant was not compelled to comply. His refusal did not result in a penalty but in the breach of a condition upon which his right to operate the truck was predicated. The court concluded that defendant's constitutional protection against self-incrimination was not violated. The court ruled that defendant was not entitled to the warnings prescribed by the Escobedo and Miranda cases because the evidence obtained was not a result of an "in-custody" interrogation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant.

Stith v. Hudson


No. 25750


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 364; 174 S.E.2d 892; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 542


April 15, 1970, Argued  
May 7, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 21, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cancellation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wofford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) overruling their motion to strike defenses filed by defendants to their action seeking cancellation of a tax deed.


OVERVIEW: In their defenses, defendants relied upon O.C.G.A. §§ 92-8315, 92-8316 and claimed that plaintiffs' opportunity to redeem the property had expired more than 18 years earlier. Plaintiffs claimed that there were no such provisions in the Georgia Code that had been enacted by the Georgia General Assembly and that defendants' claim that plaintiffs were barred as a matter of law from maintaining their action had to be predicated on the Act of 1949, 1949 Ga. Laws 1143, which plaintiffs claimed violated U.S. Const. art. I, §10 and O.C.G.A. § 2-302, Ga. Const. art. I, § 3, para. 2. Thus, the trial court's judgment overruling the motion to strike on the ground that the Act was unconstitutional did not constitute reversible error.

1088 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Flanigen v. Preferred Development Corp.


No. 25679


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 267; 174 S.E.2d 425; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 501


March 11, 1970, Argued  
April 9, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Zoning petition. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee and declared that the Mayor of the City of Atlanta lacked authority to veto a zoning ordinance adopted by the Board of Aldermen.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the mayor lacked authority to veto a zoning ordinance adopted by the Board of Aldermen, and appellant sought review. Appellant contended that the trial court erred when it found that the mayor was not part of the governing authority; that the trial court erred when it held that that the city charter power, which enabled the mayor to veto ordinances, was unconstitutional; and that the trial court erred when it held that legislative acts were in conflict with the general laws of the state. The court reversed, finding that the mayor was part of the governing authority as described in Ga. Code Ann. ch. 69-8 et seq. because the city charter specifically provided for the mayor to be a part of the governing authority and provided that the mayor could veto ordinances which were adopted by the board of aldermen. The charter power did not violate Ga. Const. art. III, § VII, para. XXIII, because it was consistent with the constitutional provision and because the mayor was part of the governing authority. Further, the state legislation, which granted the mayor veto power, did not conflict with the general laws of the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held that the city charter, which granted the mayor the power to veto zoning ordinances adopted by the Board of Aldermen, was not unconstitutional.

 

1089 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Landers v. Smith


No. 25701


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 274; 174 S.E.2d 427; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 503


March 9, 1970, Submitted  
April 9, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Tattnall Superior Court. Before Judge Caswell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Tattnall County (Georgia), which found in favor of respondent warden in the prisoner's habeas corpus action.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner contended that the practice in Georgia of reading his criminal record to the jury before the verdict in the principal case was rendered violated his rights under the United States and the Georgia Constitutions. The court affirmed the superior court's judgment that was rendered in favor of the warden. O.C.G.A. § 27-2511 provided that anyone who had a prior conviction of a crime that was punishable by confinement in a penitentiary, and who was subsequently convicted for another such crime, was to receive the maximum sentence for the second conviction. In order to sentence defendant pursuant to § 27-2511, the superior court submitted the prior convictions in the indictment that was read to the jury before the principal issue of guilt or innocence was determined. This practice was constitutional. In order for defendant to succeed on his due process challenge, he was required to demonstrate such fundamental unfairness that a fair trial was precluded. Any prejudice could have been cured by proper jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

25705.


Supreme Court of Georgia
