1091 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bible v. Marra


Nos. 25577, 25578


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 154; 173 S.E.2d 346; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 469


January 13, 1970, Argued  
February 19, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Fleming.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in Case No. 25577; affirmed in Case No. 25578.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff opponents appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia), which denied them a summary judgment in their claim to set aside the action of a city planning commission that rezoned a parcel of land upon the petition of defendant landowners. The landowners appealed the trial court's denial of their motion for summary judgment that sought a dismissal of the opponents' claims.


OVERVIEW: The opponents claimed that the ordinance, which approved the rezoning of the landowners' property, was invalid based upon an insufficient notice of the hearing to determine the rezoning. The landowners claimed that the commission had the authority to rezone the property and there were no defects in the proceedings. The court determined that the notice adequately described the property to be rezoned, which did not require the name of the city, and that the notice provided the opponents with the time and place of the hearing. The court held that the commission had the authority under 1957 Ga. Laws 420 to spot zone the landowners' property and consequently the rezoning of the property was not void as claimed by the opponents. The court held that the trial court erred by denying the landowners' summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that denied the landowners a summary judgment and affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the opponents a summary judgment.

Lee v. State


No. 25603


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 162; 173 S.E.2d 209; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 471


January 13, 1970, Submitted  
February 19, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Richond Superior Court. Before Judge Kennedy.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia) for murder and the trial court's denial of his motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen shooting the victim. Items stolen from the victim's apartment complex were found at defendant's residence and at a pawnshop under defendant's name. Defendant was convicted of murder, and his motion for new trial was denied. Defendant appealed, and argued that jurors were improperly struck, that capital punishment was unconstitutional, that there was insufficient evidence, that the jury charge was erroneous, and that defendant did not receive effective assistance of counsel. The conviction was affirmed. There was no evidence that jurors were struck for cause based on their opposition the death penalty. Capital punishment was constitutional. Defendant failed to ask for a charge on insanity, so any error was waived. The evidence was sufficient. Because there was no evidence of insanity, defense counsel's failure to raise the issue was not ineffective assistance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of murder and denying his motion for new trial.

Simmons v. State


No. 25619


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 110; 172 S.E.2d 680; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 452


January 13, 1970, Submitted  
February 5, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part, with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Chatham County (Georgia), which overruled defendant's motion to quash the indictments, convicted him of murder, and imposed sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for murder, and he was convicted therefor. On appeal, the court held that: (1) a motion to quash indictments on the ground that there had been systematic exclusion of an ethnic group from the grand jury was improper because the proper method for raising errors in an indictment was a challenge to the array before the indictment was returned, unless it was shown that defendant had no knowledge of such illegality prior to the indictment; (2) the exclusion of certain evidence was proper because it did not reasonably tend to support the charge of systematic exclusion; (3) 1953 Ga. Laws 256, which provided that in all Superior Court Judicial Circuits, jurors were competent to serve during the year not more than 20 days and which was applicable only to two counties, was not unconstitutional; and (4) the trial court erred by excusing two jurors solely on the basis that they stated on a voir dire question that they were conscientiously opposed to capital punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of murder and the court reversed that part of the trial court's judgment imposing a sentence. The court directed a new trial on the issue of punishment and that the jurors be qualified with the proper questions.

Williams v. State


No. 25584


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 140; 173 S.E.2d 182; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 463


January 13, 1970, Argued  
February 5, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 19, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rape. Screven Superior Court. Before Judge Emeritus Durrence.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Screven County (Georgia), which, after a retrial as to the sentence only, sentenced him to death upon his conviction for rape, and denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for rape and death sentence was upheld by the court. After an appeal to the court from the denial of habeas corpus relief, the court remanded defendant to the trial court for a new jury trial on the sentence issue only. Defendant was again sentenced to death. After the trial court denied his motion for new trial, defendant filed an appeal. The court upheld the sentence. It held that the trial court had correctly charged the jury on alibi as it pertained to the sentencing issue. The applicable sentencing statute, O.C.G.A. § 26-1302, was constitutional. As long as the legislature provided for the death penalty in cases of forcible rape, the court would uphold it. The fact that the death penalty was meted out disproportionately upon black men was not a denial of due process or of equal protection under the laws. Evidence of the crime was properly admitted and the new trial was not prohibited by the double jeopardy provisions of the Georgia and Federal Constitutions. The court had authority under O.C.G.A. § 6-1610 to order the retrial of the sentence only. Finally, the trial court properly excluded immaterial, academic evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Maddox v. Fortson


No. 25641


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 71; 172 S.E.2d 595; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 437


January 14, 1970, Argued  
January 26, 1970, Decided

DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a candidate and voters, appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) that dismissed plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action against defendants, the Georgia Secretary of State and officials of political parties. The trial court found that Ga. Const. art. V, § I, para. I (1945) did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV by prohibiting the candidate from running for another term as governor.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed that other state candidates were not restricted to one terms and that Ga. Const. art. V, § I, para. The court determined that the office of governor was different from other state elected positions in that the governor had powers that were different and that based upon those differences there was a rational basis for Article V, § I, para. The court held that the voters were only entitled to vote for a qualified candidate on the ballot and the candidate was not qualified to be a candidate for another terms as governor because he had already served a term.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Register v. Langdale


No. 25571


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 82; 172 S.E.2d 620; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 439


December 9, 1969, Argued  
January 26, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 5, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Equitable petition. Lowndes Superior Court. Before Judge Calhoun.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Lowndes County (Georgia), which denied the taxpayers request for an interlocutory injunction and dismissed their equitable action against appellee tax authorities because of their failure to make a tender of the 1969 taxes upon their property.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed an action against the authorities, which sought equitable relief concerning the collection of property taxes. The trial court relied on precedent from the court, which held that the taxpayers were not entitled to equitable relief because of the failure to make a tender of the 1969 taxes upon their property. At the time that the complaint was filed, and at the time of the interlocutory hearing, no 1969 taxes were due, and the authorities could not have accepted any payment on 1969 taxes. The court concluded that it was error to deny the interlocutory injunction and dismiss the complaint on the ground of the failure to tender the 1969 taxes. In so doing it explicitly overruled Walker v. Burns, 220 Ga. 467 and its progeny. The court also noted that the authorities use of outside appraisal experts and others experiential knowledge was not improper. There was a sufficient compliance with the five-day notice requirement of O.C.G.A. § 92-6911. However, it was apparent that personal property valuations were not based on fair market value and were not fairly and justly equalized, as required by Ga. Const. art. VII, § I, para. III.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

1099 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Cummings v. State


No. 25517


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 46; 172 S.E.2d 395; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 426


November 12, 1969, Argued  
January 8, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Holt.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with offense of murder for the shooting death of a victim. At voir dire, he asserted his right to cross-examine each juror who answered affirmatively to the question of whether or not he was conscientiously opposed to capital punishment and sought permission to ask the jury two additional questions. The trial court ruled that defendant could not further examine the jurors. On appeal from defendant's conviction, the court held that: (1) defendant's challenge to a request to poll the jury, for cause, was to be tried by the trial court on the testimony of a juror to the exclusion of all other evidence, and only the courts, not a party, could sua sponte further interrogate a juror; (2) a witness's testimony, that the bullet that killed the victim was fired from the gun that was offered into evidence by the State, was admissible because there was no objection thereto; (3) there was no error in the admission of the State's exhibits, which were the gun and the bullet, because substantially the same evidence, or the witness's testimony, had been was admitted without objection; and (4) the trial court could submit the issues of guilt and punishment to the same jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1100 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Stynchcombe v. Walden


No. 25542


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 63; 172 S.E.2d 402; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 430


December 9, 1969, Argued  
January 8, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.

John Raymond Walden was convicted of the crime of receiving, harboring, or concealing guilty persons. Code § 26-4601. His appeal from the judgment of the trial court overruling his motion for new trial is pending in the Georgia Court of Appeals. He subsequently sued out a writ of habeas corpus, attacking the constitutionality of Code § 26-4601 on the grounds, generally and substantially, that it abridged his rights under the 4th, 5th and 14th Amendments to the Federal Constitution in that it fails to define what constitutes a violation thereunder and makes the conviction of the principal unnecessary for conviction of the crime of an accessory. The trial court granted the writ, held the aforesaid statute to be unconstitutional and ordered the release of the prisoner, from which judgment the respondent Sheriff of Fulton County appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sheriff appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which granted petitioner prisoner's petition for habeas corpus and released him after he was convicted of the crime of receiving, harboring, or concealing guilty persons.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff contended that the superior court erred in its judgment that held O.C.G.A. § 26-4601, prohibiting the receiving, harboring, or concealing of guilty persons, unconstitutional. The court agreed and reversed the judgment. If there was any ambiguity in the statute under which the prisoner was convicted, the meaning and purpose of the statute was adequately explained in its construction by the state's appellate courts. To hold the statute unconstitutional because the principal did not need to have been convicted would have defeated the obvious purpose of the statute to prevent a criminal from escaping the consequences of his crime by avoiding arrest, prosecution, or punishment. The authoritative interpretation of the statute by the state's highest appellate courts put those words in the statute as definitely as if it had been so amended by the legislature. Furthermore, the statute was not subject to any of the prisoner's specific constitutional attacks. If the indictment was defective for any other reasons, the prisoner waived those defects by going to trial without complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment that had granted the prisoner's petition for habeas corpus and released him following his conviction for receiving, harboring, or concealing guilty persons.

 

1101 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Gainer v. Ellis


Nos. 25495, 25508


Supreme Court of Georgia


226 Ga. 79; 172 S.E.2d 608; 1970 Ga. LEXIS 438


November 10, 1969, Argued  
January 8, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 5, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Equitable petition. Jeff Davis Superior Court. Before Judge Ballenger.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed on main appeal; affirmed on cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the chairman and others, appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Jeff Davis County (Georgia), which found that a local act of the legislature, changing the method of compensating plaintiff county tax commissioner from a fee system to a salary was unconstitutional because of an improper notice. Plaintiffs, the commissioner and others, cross-appealed when other attacks on the constitutionality of the act were overruled.


OVERVIEW: A local Act of the Legislature, 1969 Ga. Laws p. 3418, changed the method of compensating the tax commissioner from fee system to a salary. The legislature abolished the offices of tax receiver and tax collector in the county and consolidated into one office the duties of the two offices. The trial court held the Act unconstitutional on the ground that the notice published in a local newspaper was insufficient. Defendants appealed this ruling. The trial court overruled other attacks on the constitutionality of the Act, and plaintiffs cross appealed. On appeal, the court held that the public was bound to know that the notice in the required publication had reference to the only office in the county government having any relation to collecting taxes. Thus, the public was put on notice of whatever facts a prudent inquiry would have revealed. The court concluded that the Act was not unconstitutional. The legislature was free to deal with one or more county offices to remedy the evil which it found to exist, and it was not necessary to revise the method of compensating all public officials in order to deal in one Act with one official.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court that found the act unconstitutional but affirmed the trial court's decision to overrule the remaining attacks on the constitutionality of the act.

Jackson v. State


No. 25435


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 790; 171 S.E.2d 501; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 647


September 10, 1969, Argued  
December 4, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Rape. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia) convicting him of rape and sentencing him to death. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred by denying his motion for a change of venue, that it erred by refusing to allow him or his attorney to appear before the grand jury, that the submission to the jury of the issues of guilt and punishment was unconstitutional, and that the trial court failed to grant him a thorough psychiatric examination. The court held that (1) no pervasive prejudice existed in the community prior to defendant's trial which denied him a fair trial; (2) there was no error in the trial court's refusal to allow defendant and his attorney to appear before the grand jury as defendant was not on trial and neither his right of confrontation nor equal protection of the laws were at issue; (3) Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1302 (1960) did not unconstitutionally permit simultaneous submission of guilt and punishment to the same jury; and (4) the trial court properly ordered a psychiatric examination of defendant by a court-appointed psychiatrist rather than one defendant selected because the psychiatrist was a witness for the court and where defendant was reported to be sane, a denial of a request to furnish a psychiatrist at public expense did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial.

 

1103 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bauer Int'l Corp. v. Cagles, Inc.


No. 25408


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 684; 171 S.E.2d 314; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 612


September 11, 1969, Argued  
November 6, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to quash service; constitutional question. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Bradford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation, a buyer, sought review of the decision of the Fulton Civil Court (Georgia), which denied the corporation's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction against appellee seller in an action for the delivery of goods sold and delivered to the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed an appeal of the trial court's decision and on appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the language of Georgia's long arm statute could not have been reasonably construed to have included corporations because the words "or his executor or administrator" in the statute referred to a natural person. The court concluded that the interpretation of a statute was not a judicial function but was determined by the intention of the legislature and that it would have been an unreasonable construction of the language used in the long arm statue prior to amendment to hold that the word "nonresident" as used in the statute was intended to include foreign corporations. The court held that it was not the intention of the General Assembly to include corporations. The court noted that the 1966 Act, as amended by the 1968 Act, could not have been applied to the cause of action against the corporation arising prior to the effective date of the 1968 amendment, and the trial court erred in denying the corporation's motion to dismiss the action for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court..

Int'l Asso. of Firefighters v. Floyd


No. 25371


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 625; 170 S.E.2d 394; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 590


September 8, 1969, Argued  
October 8, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge McWhorter.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union sought review of a judgment from the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia) ruling that the statute relied upon by the union, 1968 Ga. Laws p. 2953, was unconstitutional. The trial court sustained those grounds of appellee city's motion to dismiss the complaint which asserted that mandamus would not lie because discretionary and continuous acts were involved, in an action brought by the union seeking to represent firefighter employees.


OVERVIEW: The union sought to represent the majority of the firefighter employees of the city as bargaining agent for the improvement of hours, wages, and conditions of employment. The complaint prayed that mandamus nisi be directed to the city for it to show cause why mandamus should not have been issued requiring the city to recognize the union as the exclusive representative for collective bargaining with respect to pay, wages, hours, and other conditions of employment and methods of resolving disputes, and to begin bargaining and to refrain from changing their designated unit without bargaining. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court agreed with the trial court that 1968 Ga. Laws p. 2953 was unconstitutional. The effect of the 1968 special legislation would have been to place restrictions, in the form of mandatory collective bargaining, upon the unlimited powers granted by the 1962 general law, 1962 Ga. Laws p. 140, codified at Ga. Code Ann. § 69-309, 69-310, which was in clear violation of the constitutional prohibition against the enactment of a special law where provision had been made by existing general law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court that had dismissed the complaint brought by the union seeking to represent the majority of the firefighter employees of the city as bargaining agent for the improvement of hours, wages, and conditions of employment, and denying the mandamus that the union sought requiring the city to recognize the union as the exclusive representative for collective bargaining.

Richmond County v. Richmond County Business Asso.


No. 25321


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 568; 170 S.E.2d 246; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 565


July 15, 1969, Argued  
September 29, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Fleming.

This is an equitable action to enjoin the county authorities of Richmond County from carrying out or attempting to carry out the provisions of an ordinance adopted on January 10, 1969, imposing annual fees in various amounts upon various businesses and professions solely in the unincorporated area of the county on the ground that it is unconstitutional, null and void. The petitioners, in the main, contend that the fees sought to be collected are in reality occupational and professional taxes, which the county has no authority under the Constitution to levy and collect.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia), which granted an injunction in favor of appellees, a county business association and others, to enjoin the county from carrying out or attempting to carry out the provisions of an ordinance that imposed annual fees upon various businesses and professions located solely in the unincorporated area of the county.


OVERVIEW: The county attempted to impose on the various businesses and professionals a license fee that, among other things, purported to regulate business within the county and to make the failure to pay such fee punishable as for a misdemeanor. In a prior action affecting the county, the court nullified an attempt by the county to impose a county tax. The court, in affirming the grant of the injunction, first found that the portion of the ordinance, which attempted to impose a penalty for failure to pay the fee, violated the Home Rule Amendment of the Georgia Constitution, O.C.G.A. § 2-8402(c)(3), and was therefore void. Next, noting that the ordinance contained provisions that appeared to be regulatory in nature, the court nevertheless found that it was merely a tax disguised as a license. In light of its prior determination that the county lacked taxing authority under Georgia's statutes or constitution, the court found that the ordinance was an attempt by the county to impose and collect an occupational tax. Accordingly, the court concluded that the ordinance was null and void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting an injunction to prohibit the county from attempting to enforce the ordinance.

Ray v. Hand


No. 25384


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 589; 170 S.E.2d 692; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 577


September 10, 1969, Argued  
September 29, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant treasurer challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which declared that 1968 Ga. Laws 992, § 6 was unconstitutional and that 1965 Ga. Laws 765, § 1 was not validly submitted to the voters for ratification in a declaratory action brought by appellee district attorney.


OVERVIEW: A district attorney sought a declaratory judgment on the constitutionality of 1968 Ga. Laws 992, § 6, which prohibited district attorneys from engaging in the private practice of law, and of 1965 Ga. Laws 765, § 1, which pertained to write-in votes. The trial court held that 1968 Ga. Laws 992, § 6 was unconstitutional because it contained a matter different from that expressed in the title or because it impermissibly added a condition of eligibility for the office of district attorney, that 1965 Ga. Laws 765, § 1 was not validly submitted to the voters for ratification, and that the district attorney could hold his office, free from any limitation imposed in 1968 Ga. Laws 992, § 6. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the caption of an act was only required to include the general object and subject matter to be dealt with therein, and it was never intended that the substance of an act should be set forth in its caption; (2) the matter contained in § 6 was related to and not in conflict with what was expressed in its caption; and (3) the prohibition against private practice was not a condition of eligibility but related solely to the activities of a district attorney.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1108 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bleckley v. Vickers


No. 25388


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 593; 170 S.E.2d 695; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 578


September 9, 1969, Submitted  
September 29, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Rabun Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens appealed the decision from the Superior Court of Rabun County (Georgia), which entered a judgment in favor of defendant ordinary in the citizens' suit for injunctive relief to bar an election for the Board of County Commissioners of Rabun County, Georgia, pursuant to the Act of 1969, Senate Bill No. 232, 1969 Ga. Laws 2397 et seq. Intervenor other citizens were also parties.


OVERVIEW: The citizens contended that the ordinary was responsible for county matters over roads and revenues. The Act created the Board, but the citizens raised a number of constitutional challenges. The citizens alleged that the election would deprive them of their choice in the running of the county. The court agreed on appeal that the superior court's decision was correct. The court first rejected the contention that proper notice of the Act was not published. An earlier publication of a similar bill that was not passed met the notice requirement when it was a part of the enrolled bill. Second, the Georgia General Assembly had the full authority to create county commissioners under Ga. Const. art. VI, § 17, para. I (1945) (Ga. Code Ann. § 2-5201). The court then found that the Act was not an unconstitutional infringement on the ordinary because the legislature had the legal right to limit the ordinary's authority. Finally, the requirement that Board members must be a resident of the particular district where the member lived was not unlawful because the members were elected county-wide.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of injunctive relief.

Drake v. Barrs


Nos. 25392, 25393


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 597; 170 S.E.2d 684; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 579


September 9, 1969, Argued  
September 29, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cancellation. Jenkins Superior Court. Before Judge Hawkins.

Mrs. L. M. Barrs, formerly Mrs. N. W. (Polly) Drake initially instituted an action under Code § 37-1410 to remove clouds from her titles to two tracts of land described in the petition and other appropriate equitable relief, against Mrs. Katherine Johnson Drake, Dixie Production Credit Association and Mars Wampler. The petition alleges that N. W. Drake, divorced husband of plaintiff, died October 9, 1965. The plaintiff by amendment to her petition alleged that Mrs. Katherine Johnson Drake, Mars Wampler and N. W. Drake conspired to defraud "and/or" practice a fraud upon the plaintiff to wit, to deprive and deny her, by illegal means, her legal title to the ownership of the land described in the petition, based on allegations in the petition which will appear in the discussion of the case. Also sought was damages for timber allegedly cut by defendants. The amendment also added that petitioner and N. W. Drake were divorced on May 11, 1932, and that defendant Mars Wampler is the nephew of Mrs. Katherine Johnson Drake. Mrs. Katherine Johnson Drake and Mars Wampler moved for summary judgments as did the plaintiff, Mrs.  [***2] L. M. Barrs. The judge denied all motions for summary judgments and on certificate the two defendants appeal from the denial of their motions and the plaintiff cross appeals from the denial of her motion for partial summary judgment (title only). Facts necessary for a decision will be stated and discussed in the opinion as two tracts of land are involved attacks upon title to which involve different facts and principles of law. All parties claim under common grantors.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a second wife and nephew, appealed the decisions from the Superior Court of Jenkins County (Georgia), which denied their motions for summary judgment in the suit by plaintiff first wife to remove the clouds to her title to property filed against the second wife, the nephew, and defendant credit association. The first wife also appealed the denial of her partial summary judgment motion for title to one tract only.


OVERVIEW: A landowner divorced the first wife and remarried. The first wife argued that her opponents sought to defraud her. The second wife was the aunt of the nephew. The landowner had executed a promissory note to a bank secured by a deed to one tract. Through a series of transfers, two tracts were deeded to the first wife with a life estate reservation. The husband then conveyed one tract to the second wife with a life estate reservation. The bank transferred its deed to the second wife. The husband that renewed his note. At some point, the second wife conveyed her interests to the nephew. On appeal, the court favored the first wife and the nephew. The bank's interests could have been transferred to the second wife. The Acts of 1941 and 1953 described in Ga. Code Ann. § 67-1308, which the first wife contended barred the transfer, were unconstitutional because they impaired the obligation of contracts. In summary, when the nephew acquired one tract from a chain from the husband to the nephew, his interests were valid. However, the second wife did not acquire a second tract through adverse possession because the seven-year period for possession was not met.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the overruling of the first wife's partial summary judgment motion regarding the second tract. The court reversed the overruling of the nephew's summary judgment motion. In all other respects, the decisions below were affirmed.

Plantation Pipe Line Co. v. Bremen

1111 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Sams v. Olah


No. 25292


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 497; 169 S.E.2d 790; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 548


July 15, 1969, Argued  
September 15, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 29, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Hames.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state bar and bar officials, sought review of the decision of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which found in favor of plaintiff attorney in the attorney's action stating that the state bar was proceeding against him without authority law in a disciplinary matter.


OVERVIEW: The attorney brought an action against the state bar and its officials alleging that they were proceeding against him without authority of law in a disciplinary matter. He further stated that the law under which the state bar was created, 1963 Ga. Laws 70-72, and the rules of the state bar violated the state and federal constitutions. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss an equitable complaint; declared 70-72 unconstitutional, and granted an injunction. The court held that the license fee required under the rules was not a professional tax on attorneys and that a municipality was not precluded from levying a tax on attorneys because of the license fee paid to the state bar. Therefore, the trial court erred in holding that the fee was a tax or gratuity and unconstitutional. The court further held that the State Bar Act (Act) did not deprive the attorney of his freedom of contract, conscience, speech, and liberty, and did not deprive him of his property without due process of law. Further, there was no merit in the contention that the Act did not authorize the adoption of disciplinary rules and regulations; the trial judge erred in holding the Act void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's holding against the state bar and bar officials in the attorney's action against them.

 

1112 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Manor v. State


No. 25260


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 538; 170 S.E.2d 290; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 557


July 14, 1969, Submitted  
September 9, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 29, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant for murder and gave him a death sentence. The superior court denied a new trial motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed a number of errors, including objections to two women who were unqualified to serve on the jury, the failure to grant attorney's fees and costs when defendant had appointed counsel, and the taking of defendant's fingerprints and the admission thereof. On appeal, the court found no reversible errors. Ga. Code Ann. § 59-112 allowed women to exempt from service, but it did not deal with eligibility for jury service. Further, the right was personal and could not be urged by defendant. Therefore, there was no error in allowing the women on the jury. The superior court could have denied access to the State's files of its investigators. A challenge to the constitutionality of the attorney's fees statute was too vague to be reviewed. Defendant's counsel had the right to fees and expenses accounted for after trial, but his request was made at the start of trial. The fingerprints were taken while defendant was in lawful detention, his counsel was notified, and there was no objection. Jurors who objected to the death penalty under any circumstances could have been excused for cause. Other objections to the selection of the jury were disregarded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

1114 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. Georgia Education Authority


No. 25274


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 542; 170 S.E.2d 240; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 558


July 15, 1969, Argued  
September 8, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 29, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the judgment by the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which granted judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants school district and trust company in the taxpayer's action to cancel the sale of bonds to the company and to restrain the company from disbursing the funds collected from the bond sale.


OVERVIEW: The district issued revenue bonds which were purchased by the company to be resold to others. The taxpayers filed an action to set aside the sale and restrain the company from reselling the bonds, and argued that the bonds exceeded the debt limit imposed by Ga. Const. art. VII, § 3, and that the district operated in an unconstitutional manner. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings in favor of the district and the company. On the taxpayers' appeal, the court affirmed. Because the bonds were validated pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 32-1423a, the taxpayers were estopped from arguing that the bonds were invalid, and should have appealed the validation as provided by O.C.G.A. § 87-819. The validation operated as res judicata against the taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment on the pleadings in favor of the district and the company in the taxpayers' action to set aside the sale of bonds and restrain the resale of the bonds.

1116 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Harper v. Burgess


No. 25240


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 420; 169 S.E.2d 297; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 518


June 12, 1969, Argued  
July 10, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Dean.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed from the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), which denied her petition for mandamus to compel defendant court clerk to allow the wife to file a complaint for a divorce without making a "cost deposit" as required by O.G.C.A. § 24-3406 and to permit her to file a pauper's affidavit in lieu of such deposit.


OVERVIEW: The wife contended that O.G.C.A. § 24-3406 and § 24-3413, which prohibited the filing of a pauper's affidavit in a divorce action, were invalid because they denied the wife equal access to the courts under Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. IV and denied her equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV by infringing her right to marry. A mandamus nisi was issued, but the trial court rendered a judgment denying the mandamus absolute. Affirming, the court first ruled that it would not decide a constitutional question where the case could be made upon other grounds. The wife failed to attach a copy of her petition for divorce to her mandamus petition; thus, the court could not determine whether the grant of a writ of mandamus to her would be of any benefit. The wife also stated that she was not suggesting she had a right to a divorce and, as a result, she failed to show that the grant of the writ would be beneficial to her. A writ of mandamus was not available where another specific remedy was available. The wife had another available remedy because she could have brought an action for a declaratory judgment to test the constitutionality of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Roberts v. Markin


No. 25196


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 352; 168 S.E.2d 576; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 496


May 13, 1969, Submitted  
June 12, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petition. Johnson Superior Court. Before Judge White.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff debtor sought review of a decision from the Johnson Superior Court (Georgia), which granted defendants, an executrix of the note holder's estate and her attorney's, motion to dismiss the debtor's petition that sought equitable relief.


OVERVIEW: The debtor filed a petition against defendants that sought equitable relief. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss because of lack of jurisdiction in that the executrix was a nonresident of the state and her attorney a nonresident of the county. On appeal, the court stated that Ga. Const. art. VI, § XIV, para. III; Ga. Code Ann. § 2-4903, provided that equity actions were to be tried in the county where a defendant resided. The court stated that because the debtor's action was equitable action against nonresidents of the county the trial court had properly dismissed the action. The court stated that the constitutional provision controlled and not 1966 Ga. Laws p. 343, because it was an equity action where an in personam judgment was sought against nonresidents of the county and in which not substantial relief was sought against any resident defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of defendants' motion to dismiss the debtor's petition that had sought equitable relief.

 

1118 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Grantham Transfer Co. v. Hawes


Nos. 25194, 25195


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 436; 169 S.E.2d 290; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 524


May 13, 1969, Argued  
June 12, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 10 and July 24, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tax assessment; constitutional question. Houston Superior Court. Before Judge Culpepper.

This is a continuation of a sales and use tax case heretofore considered on appeal and reported in Undercofler v. Grantham Transfer Co., 114 Ga. App. 868, supra, and 222 Ga. 654 (151 SE2d 765). The case as previously reported in this court has no bearing on the issues here as it involved only a certified question of the Court of Appeals on appellate procedure. The case in the Court of Appeals was to review the grant in part and the denial in part of summary judgment on appeal to the superior court from an assessment of the Revenue Commissioner. The Court of Appeals held that a disputed issue existed presenting a jury question as to whether leased equipment or machinery was under the exclusive control of the lessor Grantham. The case involves, in the main, an arrangement of Grantham in which it leased, loaned, or contracted its equipment and machinery including certain services to motor common carriers in interstate commerce in which the written agreements granted exclusive possession, control and use of the motor vehicles involved when operated [***2] by or for such carrier. The affirmance by the Court of Appeals merely left the case pending in the court below, and it proceeded to trial. Both parties moved for directed verdict, and the lower court then discharged the jury and ordered as follows: (1) The third unnumbered paragraph of § 4a of the Sales and Use Tax Act, as amended (Ga. L. 1955, pp. 389, 390; Code Ann. § 92-3448a) is not unconstitutional for any reason assigned; (2) The written agreements by and between Grantham and the motor common carriers are not leases taxable under the Sales and Use Tax Act (Code Ann. Ch. 92-34a, as amended), and the appeal from the assessment was sustained and set aside in a stated amount; (3) The sales (purchases) of certain tangible personal property by Grantham were taxable transactions, and the company had failed to pay these, thus in effect, authorizing the assessment by the Revenue Commissioner in a stated sum; (4) A lease of tangible personal property by the company was a taxable transaction, and the company having failed to pay the taxes thereon, the assessment was likewise sustained in a stated amount; (5) Certain sales (purchases) of tangible personal property were not taxable; yet [***3] the company had paid tax thereon; and (6) A judgment was rendered for the Commissioner for a stated amount, including delinquency penalty and accrued interest for the taxable period.

The assessment involved, in the main, the question of whether or not the commissioner was correct in holding the written agreements were leases and requiring Grantham to collect and pay taxes thereon.

The appeal by Grantham is that the trial court erred in (1) Overruling its constitutional attack upon "the third unnumbered paragraph of Section 4a" of the 1955 amendment to the Sales and Use Tax Act (Ga. L. 1955, pp. 389, 390; Code Ann. § 92-3448a); and (2) Rendering judgment against it for sums claimed to be due in (a) the sale of tangible personal property originally purchased allegedly for its own use, and (b) the leasing of tangible personal property from others. It likewise enumerates error on the allowance in evidence of certain testimony; the refusal to allow certain testimony; the impeachment of the commissioner's witness by his counsel; and the refusal to grant in its entirety Grantham's motion for directed verdict.

The cross appeal by the Revenue Commissioner is from the holding by the trial [***4] judge that the written agreements between Grantham and the motor common carriers did not result in taxable transactions under the Sales and Use Tax Act.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part on the main appeal, and reversed on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged a decision by appellee tax commissioner finding certain business transactions taxable. The Houston Superior Court (Georgia) entered judgment in favor of the commissioner. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer made agreements with trucking companies under which the taxpayer agreed to provide vehicles for use by the trucking companies. Four of the documents specifically stated that they were leases of equipment and designated the parties as lessor and lessee. The other two documents in dispute did not use the lessor/lessee description, but rather referred to the parties as contractor and carrier, but essentially contained the same provisions as the leases. The taxpayer asserted that the transactions were for services, and the equipment was incidental thereto. The trial court found the six transaction in question to not be leases of equipment and not taxable. The commissioner appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's findings and held that the transactions were all leases and taxable as such.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment finding the transactions in question not taxable was reversed.

Sullivan v. State


No. 25147


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 301; 168 S.E.2d 133; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 476


April 15, 1969, Argued  
May 8, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 22, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Lamar Superior Court. Before Judge Sosebee.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Lamar County (Georgia), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Following reversal by the Supreme Court (Georgia) of an initial conviction, defendant was retried and again convicted and sentenced to death. He claimed that the second conviction should be reversed because he was denied a speedy trial, in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. VI; O.C.G.A. § 1-806; Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. V; O.C.G.A. § 2-105, in that 18 months elapsed between the commission of the crime and the second trial. He also claimed that the jury was not a fair cross-section of the population. On review, the court found no merit to the claims. The delay in the second trial occurred when defendant appealed from his first conviction, so there was no denial of a constitutional right to a speedy trial. The court found that both the grand and traverse juries were legally drawn and composed in compliance with Ga. Const. art. I, § I, paras. III, V, and XXV, O.C.G.A. §§ 2-103, 2-105, 2-125, as well as under U.S. Const. Amend. XIV. There was no denial of due process in the failure to grant a change of venue. Further, defendant was not denied any right to counsel under the U.S. Constitution, amend. V, VI, or XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1120 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. Long


No. 25115


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 227; 167 S.E.2d 583; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 442


April 16, 1969, Argued  
April 24, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.

This is a suit to enjoin the alleged illegal operation of a private bank after the passage of legislation requiring all persons doing a private banking business in this State to be chartered under the banking laws (Code Ann. § 13-204; Ga. L. 1960, p. 1170; 1966, p. 691; 1966, pp. 692, 715) and meet the requirements of the Regulated Certificated Bank Act (Ga. L. 1966, pp. 692, 716; Code Ann. Ch. 13-23). The defendant in his answer, as amended, (1) denied the authority of the Superintendent of Banks to bring this action; (2) alleged he had made application as a private banker to become a State Certificated Bank under the above law but the Superintendent of Banks refused to grant a certificated bank charter or certificate as required by the law; and (3) attacked the legislation requiring him to cease doing business as a sole proprietor and become incorporated and meet the various requirements of law as being unconstitutional, null and void.

The case proceeded to an interlocutory hearing of the request for a temporary injunction based upon an affidavit and a stipulation of certain facts as follows: (1) the defendant is a private [***2] banker who commenced operations during December 1959, under the ownership of a predecessor; (2) registered with the Superintendent of Banks as a private banker in 1966; (3) filed an application for incorporation as a regulated certificated bank pursuant to said legislation approved in 1966, which was disapproved by the Superintendent under § 11 (b) of the Act, all of which application and disapproval was attached to the stipulation as exhibits, showing a determination that the applicants were not actively engaged in the banking business. The constitutional attacks upon the legislation are based upon (1) denial of equal protection, (2) denial of due process, and (3) destruction of defendant's business without due compensation therefor. The court denied the request for injunction and held: (1) the parties agree that defendant is engaged in the private banking business; (2) by legislation the General Assembly has undertaken to prohibit all private banking and restrict the right to conduct such banking business to corporations; and (3) the legislation is therefore unconstitutional, null and void in denying the right to individuals to carry on a lawful business, thereby destroying the [***3] defendant's lawfully existing business without compensation. The appeal is from this judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank superintendent appealed the order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) denying its request to enjoin defendant bank from illegal operation for non-compliance with Ga. Code Ann. §§ 13-204, 13-23, and holding that § 13-2311 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff bank superintendent maintained that defendant was illegally operating as a private bank, because it was not properly chartered under Georgia law. Plaintiff filed suit to enjoin the alleged illegal operation by defendant following passage of legislation requiring all persons doing a private banking business in the state to be chartered under Ga. Code Ann. §§ 13-204, 13-2311. Defendant denied plaintiff's authority to bring suit and attacked the legislation as unconstitutional. The trial court ruled for defendant on the grounds that the law was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court disagreed and reversed that ruling. It held that defendant must comply with Georgia law to operate a private bank. Because defendant was so clearly operating contrary to law, the court did not address plaintiff's further allegations regarding the duties of plaintiff as superintendent of banks.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of an injunction to plaintiff bank superintendent on the grounds that defendant's operation of a private bank was clearly in violation of Georgia law, which was not unconstitutional.

Crumley v. Head


No. 25148


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 246; 167 S.E.2d 651; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 451


April 15, 1969, Argued  
April 24, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Pulaski Superior Court. Before Judge O'Connor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Pulaski County (Georgia), which denied his petition for habeas corpus relief to have his convictions declared void because parts of O.C.G.A. tit. 79A were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was charged in a two-count indictment with selling and possessing amphetamine and bithetamine. The prisoner entered pleas of guilty, and he was sentenced to two years on each indictment. The prisoner then filed his petition for habeas corpus, alleging that O.C.G.A. tit. 79A, under which he was indicted, was unconstitutional. On review, the court found that only the first indictment for selling and possessing amphetamines could be considered under the petition because the prisoner had not yet begun to serve his sentence on the second indictment. The court held that tit. 79A was not unconstitutional as violating Ga. Const. art. III, § 7, para. 8, which prohibited the inclusion of more than subject in any act of the general assembly. The court reasoned that the legislature grouped all persons authorized to manufacture, sale, and possess drugs, poisons, and cosmetics. The court concluded that the prisoner was not entitled to challenge the rule-making authority given to the Georgia State Board of Pharmacy under tit. 79A because the prisoner was not convicted of violating any rule of the Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

Holloway v. Mayor & Council of Whitesburg


No. 25058


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 152; 166 S.E.2d 576; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 407


February 10, 1969, Submitted  
February 20, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction, etc. Carroll Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, residents whose property was annexed, challenged the judgment of the Carroll Superior Court (Georgia), which refused to hold unconstitutional Section II of Act No. 619 of March 3, 1964, 1964 Ga. Laws 170 (codified at Ga. Code Ann. § 69-1601), extending the corporate limits of appellee, the Town of Whitesburg, Georgia, and denied the injunctive relief sought.


OVERVIEW: The residents appealed the trial court's judgment refusing to hold Section II of the Act unconstitutional. On appeal, as to the residents' argument that the Act was a legislative construction of the meaning of words and constituted an exercise of the function of the judicial division of the government and that the trial court erred in refusing to so rule, the court held that if the general assembly was authorized to designate a municipal corporation as a "city" or "town" it could not be said that it was without authority to abolish such distinctions for statutory purposes and declare that when municipal corporations were referred to either as "town" or as "city" in an act of the general assembly, such language was to be deemed synonymous; thus, the first enumeration of error which complained of the use of the term "city" and "town" interchangeably was without merit. The enrolled Act, a copy of which was attached as a petition exhibit, showed that a certain individual was one of the authors and that he executed an affidavit showing the necessary publication. The court rejected the contention that annexation without a vote of the residents of the affected area was not valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1123 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Clower


No. 25073


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 165; 166 S.E.2d 363; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 414


February 10, 1969, Argued  
February 20, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 6, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for pension; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an employer and others, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which overruled the constitutional attack on Fulton County Employees' Pension Act, 1968 Ga. Laws 2149, and declared that defendant employee was entitled to benefits under the Act.


OVERVIEW: The employer alleged that the Act was unconstitutional because the advertisement attached to the Act did not comply with the requirements of Ga. Const. of 1945, art. III, § 7, para. 15. Two proposed acts were involved in the dispute. H.B. 734, Gen. Assem. (Ga. 1968); 1968 Ga. Laws 2290, made the amendments to the Act and were expressly set forth in the advertisement. However, H.B. 679, Gen. Assem. (Ga. 1968); 1968 Ga. Laws 2149, amended the Act by making changes that were not included in the purpose of the Act. On review, the court noted that if the advertisement had contained language that expressed an intention to amend the Act, the advertisement would have been sufficient. However, the court also stated that under reasonable rules of construction, more information regarding the law to be enacted was not required in the caption of the bill. The court found that H.B. 679, Gen. Assem. (Ga. 1968), 1968 Ga. Laws 2290, only contained matters completely foreign to the avowed intent contained in the advertisement; it therefore did not meet the requirements of the Georgia Constitution regarding the necessary advertisement of a local act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the superior court.

Robinson v. State


No. 25040


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 167; 167 S.E.2d 158; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 415


February 10, 1969, Submitted  
February 20, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Burglary; constitutional question. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Chatham County (Georgia), which found him guilty, as charged, of burglary, overruled his motion for a new trial, and sentenced him for the offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a review of his conviction for burglary, alleging that 1967 Ga. Laws 251, which amended the jury selection statute, O.C.G.A. § 59-106, was vague and indefinite. Defendant argued that the jury selection statute excluded black persons and women from the jury. On review, the court found that the statute was not subject to the attack because the purpose of its adoption was to secure a more representative cross-section of the intelligent citizens, which included black persons and women. In addition, the court held that 1967 Ga. Laws 725 was not unconstitutional when it excluded certain persons, such as lawyers, police officers, and firemen from jury duty because 1967 Ga. Laws 725 did not arbitrarily exclude them from service if they made a written request to be chosen. The court determined that mere automatic exemption of certain citizens who had a right to serve if they desired did not result in the jury lists chosen not being representative. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to justify a guilty verdict, as one of defendant's companions was found with clothes from the burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

 

1125 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Wallace v. Wallace


No. 25034


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 102; 166 S.E.2d 718; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 392


January 14, 1969, Argued  
February 6, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 20, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Election contest; constitutional question. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw from Atlanta Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the judgment from the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), which held that the attorney was ineligible to hold the office of solicitor general after being elected to that office.


OVERVIEW: The attorney argued that membership in the State Bar of Georgia (bar) or payment of dues to the bar was not part of the requirement to be eligible for the office of solicitor general and that the general assembly considered that admission to the bar and a license to practice was all that was required to constitute the practice of law. The trial court held that the attorney was ineligible to serve as solicitor general. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that although the attorney was admitted to the practice of law during the three years immediately prior to his election, the attorney never registered or paid any license fee to the bar until "right before" he entered the race for solicitor general. Therefore the attorney did not lawfully practice law for the three years preceding the election because Ga. Bar Rule 1-203 and 1-204 stated that no person could legally practice law without first registering and paying the fee. Furthermore, the court held that the practice of law was a function of the judiciary, which disposed of the attorney's arguments asserting that he was deprived of the right to have his duties and obligations defined by the general assembly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court, which held that the attorney was ineligible to hold the office of solicitor general in the State of Georgia.

 

1126 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. State


No. 25032


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 117; 166 S.E.2d 338; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 395


January 14, 1969, Submitted  
February 6, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prostitution, etc.; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wood, Emeritus.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from denial of their petition for a writ of certiorari to the Fulton County Superior Court, subsequent to their convictions for engaging in prostitution and assignation. Their cases had been consolidated. Defendants enumerated as error: (a) the overruling of their demurrers to the accusation and sentence, and (b) the sustaining of the motion by the State to dismiss their motion to quash the accusation.


OVERVIEW: Their demurrers and motion to quash and dismiss the accusation were on the grounds (a) that Ga. Code Ann. § 26-6203, with which they were charged with violating, offended the due process and equal protection clauses of the Federal and state Constitutions in that the statute was vague and indefinite, and (b) that they were entrapped by the arresting officer. The court found that the word prostitution in the statute was not vague and indefinite. A person of ordinary intelligence knew the meaning of the words "prostitute" and "prostitution." The statute was not unconstitutional. The defense of entrapment was without substance because entrapment existed where the idea and the intention to commit the act originated with an officer, who, by undue persuasion and deceitful means, induced a defendant to violate the law. The arresting officer's testimony was that while he was on duty, in a bar one of the defendants had stated that she could get him a girl if he wanted one. They met later at a motel and defendants both offered to have relations with him for $ 40 a piece. Neither the trial nor the lower court had committed error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

 

1127 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. McLendon


No. 25015


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 119; 166 S.E.2d 345; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 396


January 14, 1969, Argued  
February 6, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 20, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which determined that Ga. Code § 105-2003 violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. Amend. XIV, and which denied plaintiff's motion to compel defendant to answer interrogatories regarding his personal assets and financial condition in an action that asserted an injury to plaintiff's peace, happiness, or feelings and sought punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff filed a claim that alleged intentional wrongdoing by defendant and sought punitive damages, plaintiff sought information during discovery that pertained to defendant's financial condition. The trial court denied plaintiff's motion to compel defendant to provide the information on the grounds that Ga. Code § 105-2003 violated the equal protection clause. Plaintiff appealed, and the court reversed, holding that most of the states allowed consideration of defendant's financial condition in the determination of the amount of punitive damages. Ga. Code § 105-2003 required consideration of defendant's financial condition and the amount of bad faith in the transaction with all the attendant facts. Because a wealthy defendant would not feel a sting if a minor punitive award was given to a plaintiff, it was reasonable to consider the wealth of defendant. Due process was not violated because § 105-2003 did not make a visible or arbitrary classification of persons according to wealth, and it was a fair and equitable rule to deter gross misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1128 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanks


Nos. 24992, 24993


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 88; 166 S.E.2d 19; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 388


January 13, 1969, Argued  
January 23, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 6, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dispossessory warrant; constitutional question. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fulton Civil Court (Georgia) allowed defendant tenants, in filing their defense to a dispossessory warrant, to file their counter-affidavits without first posting a bond, as required by Ga. Code Ann. § 61-303, and held that the tenants be permitted to assert their defenses without being subjected to the double rent provision of Ga. Code Ann. § 61-305. Plaintiffs, the State of Georgia and the Housing Authority of the City of Atlanta, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had held that Ga. Code Ann. §§ 61-303, 305 were unconstitutional. The court reversed. The court stated that Ga. Code Ann. § 61-303, requiring a tenant filing a defense to a dispossessory warrant to post a bond to secure the landlord, was not unreasonable because (1) it was entirely appropriate and equitable, under the due process clause of the United States Constitution and the Georgia Constitution, to guarantee payment to the landlord while a tenant resisted eviction and had the use and benefit of the premises; and (2) the fact that a tenant was indigent and unable to furnish a bond did not permit a different conclusion. The court stated that it was not unreasonable to allow appropriate damages, as provided by Ga. Code Ann. § 61-305, against a tenant for unlawfully withholding possession of the landlord's premises because such damages were reasonably calculated to compensate the landlord for having been unlawfully denied the use of his premises and to deter a tenant from asserting frivolous defenses to a rightful dispossession. The court concluded that the provisions were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the statutes in question were not unreasonable.

 

1129 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dobson v. Brown


No. 24931


Supreme Court of Georgia


225 Ga. 73; 166 S.E.2d 22; 1969 Ga. LEXIS 384


November 13, 1968, Argued  
January 10, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 23 and February 6, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Kennedy.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia), which denied their request for an interlocutory injunction against appellees, a tax assessor and other government agencies. The taxpayers sought to enjoin against property assessments and to have 1962 Ga. Laws 3172-3180 declared null and void.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were residents of a city in which the tax assessor, purporting to act under proper authority of 1962 Ga. Laws 3172-3180, assessed their property. It was alleged that 1962 Ga. Laws 3172-3180 was enacted under the authority of 1956 Ga. Laws 453-456. The court held that 1956 Ga. Laws 453-456 authorized cities to consolidate boards of tax assessors and vest the assessment authority in those boards. The court determined that, because 1962 Ga. Laws 3172-3180 vested that same authority in one officer, the tax assessor, it was unconstitutional. Because the act was unconstitutional, the court further found that the taxpayers were not required to follow the requirements for seeking a remedy from the act and could seek review in a court of equity. The court further ruled that, because the assessments would continue unless 1962 Ga. Laws 3172-3180 was declared void, the taxpayers were not estopped from bringing their action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.
