1131 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Maddox v. Coogler


No. 24936


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 806; 165 S.E.2d 158; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 961


November 13, 1968, Submitted  
November 21, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 29, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of a Mineral Leasing Commission representing the State, appealed the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled their oral motion to dismiss appellees' complaint, enjoined appellants individually and jointly from acting on a lease proposal of a corporation, and declared the Act of the General Assembly of 1945, as amended, unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: The members contended that appellees' suit was a suit against the State, instituted without its consent, and that the trial court erred in overruling their motion to dismiss the complaint. The court determined that the trial judge erred in overruling the motion. The court explained that a suit could not be maintained against the State without its statutory consent. The court explained that such rule could not be evaded by making an action nominally against the servants or agents of a State when the real claim was against the State itself and the State was the party vitally interested. The court concluded that where a suit was brought against an officer or agency of the State with relation to some matter in which a defendant represented the State in action and liability, and the State, while not a party to the record, was the real party against which relief was sought so that a judgment for the plaintiff, although nominally against the named defendant as an individual or entity distinct from the State, would have operated to control the action of the State or subject it to liability, the suit was in effect one against the State.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1132 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crane


No. 24720


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 643; 164 S.E.2d 116; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 882


July 9, 1968, Argued  
October 10, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on bond; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bond holder sought review of the decision of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee principal and surety in the bond holder's action to collect upon the bond given under the Motor Vehicle Safety Responsibility Act, 1951 Ga. Laws 565. On appeal, the principal and surety abandoned their contention that a general assembly act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The bond holder filed suit against the surety on the bond of the principal and the principal was named as a third party defendant. Both the principal and surety filed motion for summary judgment that were granted by the lower court. The lower court sustained the principal and surety's attack on the constitutionality of the general assembly act. The principal and surety abandoned their constitutional attack on appeal. They argued that the bond holder's action against the principal was filed too late to be covered by the and that since the principal had later been declared bankrupt the summary judgment was still properly rendered. The court reversed the judgment because it found that the bond was voluntarily filed and by its terms bound the surety to pay upon default of the principal. The bond was filed after the principal's bankruptcy discharge and was an express promise in writing signed by the principal, thus meeting the requirements of O.C.G.A. § 3-902 and the requirement that the action be filed in the prescribed period of time, which could be waived.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1133 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Akins v. State


No. 24765


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 650; 164 S.E.2d 125; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 885


September 9, 1968, Submitted  
October 10, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Misdemeanor; constitutional question. Savannah City Court. Before Judge Oliver.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the City Court of Savannah (Georgia), which overruled his general demurrers to the accusations against him and convicted him of two counts of possession of non-tax-paid liquor and two counts of selling liquor without a state license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by accusation with two counts of possession of non-tax-paid liquor and two counts of selling liquor without a state license. Defendant filed general demurrers to the accusations, contending that O.C.G.A. § 58-1065 (1937-38) was unconstitutional. The trial court overruled the demurrers and convicted defendant on all counts. Upon review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that § 58-1065 was adequately clear and definite to apprise one of the acts that it intended to prohibit. Thus, it was not violative of the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the Federal Constitution for vagueness. The court found that the sale of liquor in Georgia was a privilege, not a right pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 58-1068 (1937-38). Thus, defendant's position that he had a right to possess and sell liquor and that to refuse him this right violated his constitutional guarantees was wholly untenable. The court determined that the application of O.C.G.A. § 58-1065 (1937-38) did not deny defendant any of his rights guaranteed by the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1134 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Reserve Life Ins. Co. v. Davis


No. 24777


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 665; 164 S.E.2d 132; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 891


September 9, 1968, Argued  
October 10, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on insurance policy; constitutional question. Ware Superior Court. Before Judge Hodges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer challenged a judgment from the Ware Superior Court (Georgia), which held in favor of plaintiff insured in awarding him hospital room expenses, penalty, and attorney's fees for the insurer's bad faith in refusing to pay the insured's claim. The insured had filed an action to recover payment under a hospital room expenses policy issued by the insurer for expenses incurred when the insured was confined in a state hospital.


OVERVIEW: An insured held an insurance policy issued by an insurer, which agreed to pay a certain amount of daily hospital room expense, not to exceed in the aggregate 100 days on account of any one accident or disease, actually incurred. The insured was confined to a state hospital, which was a state institution within 1960 Ga. Laws pp. 1138-1143 providing a formulae whereby the amounts charged persons confined in such institutions could be computed, based upon ability to pay, for 114 days, and filed a notice of claim. The insurer declined to pay, and the insured then filed an action seeking payment for the hospital room expenses incurred. On appeal from a judgment for the insured, the court held that: (1) the insurer lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute because its enforcement did not infringe upon the insurer's right; (2) the insurer's obligation to pay depended upon the insured's duty to furnish proof of loss allowable under the policy; and (3) proof of expenses incurred for treatment, which was not covered under the policy, without a showing that it was attributable to charges for covered expenses, did not constitute proof of the amount recoverable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had held in favor of the insured in awarding him hospital expenses, a penalty, and attorney's fees, with directions that the trial judge grant the insurer a new trial solely on the issue of the amount of expenses incurred for room, board, and general nursing care.

 

1135 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Albany v. Bond


Nos. 24784, 24809


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 712; 164 S.E.2d 813; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 916


September 9, 1968, Argued  
October 10, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 7, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Kelley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed on cross appeal, and on main appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, City of Albany and certain citizens, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Dougherty County (Georgia), which held that O.C.G.A. § 58-1083 did not permit the City, upon its own initiative or pursuant to petition, hold a second referendum until two years after a prior referendum governing the sale of liquor by the drink (mixed drinks sale). Appellee citizens also sought review of the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The City proposed a referendum pursuant to § 58-1083. Appellees filed an action to enjoin the election, arguing that the statute did not permit a second election where a prior election had resulted in a vote against mixed drinks sales. Appellants denied the allegations and sought a declaratory judgment on their counterclaim that the statute and the referendum were valid. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional, that under the statute the City could not, on its own initiative or upon petition, hold a second referendum until two years after a prior referendum, and enjoined the City from conducting the proposed referendum until two years after the prior referendum. All parties sought review. The court reversed the judgment with respect to appellees' cross appeal, noting that § 58-1083 twice mentioned that where a referendum vote was against the sale of mixed drinks, the referendum provision would become null, void, and of no force and effect. The court noted further that the statute provided for a subsequent election where a prior election was in favor of the sale of mixed drinks, but was silent as to a second election where the first vote was against such sale.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court on the grounds asserted in appellee's cross appeal and held that its decision on the cross appeal controlled adversely appellants' enumerations of error on the main appeal.

Massey v. Smith


No. 24793


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 721; 164 S.E.2d 786; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 918


September 10, 1968, Argued  
October 10, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 7, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Tattnall Superior Court. Before Judge Caswell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioned for writ of habeas corpus from the Tattnall Superior Court (Georgia) judgment remanding him to the custody of respondent warden after he was convicted of rape and sentenced to death. He alleged that the conviction and sentence were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant complained that his conviction and sentence violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution because the grand jury indicting him and the traverse jury which convicted him were illegal since they systematically excluded "Negroes, women, and persons of limited economic means." He argued that selecting juries from racially segregated tax rolls was inherently discriminatory and resulted in persons of lower incomes being grossly underrepresented. He also complained that his death sentence was because the traverse jury had been purged of those opposed to capital punishment, so it failed to recommend mercy, and that it was cruel and arbitrary to punish a white man by death for rape. The fact that the death sentence for rape had been imposed on fewer white men than others in past years did not show a denial of due process or equal protection. Errors which had already been decided could not be raised on habeas corpus. Appellant lacked standing to question the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 26-301. The court affirmed the rape conviction, but it agreed that, under Witherspoon, the death sentence was illegal and reversed it.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for rape was affirmed, but the sentence imposed on the verdict was reversed as illegal and the case was remanded with directions to the trial court to impanel a capital jury and submit to it the question of whether defendant should have been recommended for mercy and sentenced accordingly.

 

1137 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dep't of Agric. v. Quality Food Prods.


Nos. 24727, 24728


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 585; 163 S.E.2d 704; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 856


July 9, 1968, Argued  
September 24, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore, Emeritus.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with direction on the main appeal; cross appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Georgia Department of Agriculture (department) appealed an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which found that plaintiff corporation's imitation milk product did not come within the prohibition of the "filled milk" rule, Ga. Code Ann. § 42-511(1929) and Ga. Law p. 501 et seq. (1961). The trial court enjoined the department from preventing the corporation's sale of the product.


OVERVIEW: The corporation's imitation milk product contained water, vegetable oil, dry milk solids, organic chemicals, and other ingredients. The corporation planned to label the cartons that it was not a dairy product and sought to enjoin the department from enforcing the "filled milk" rule against it. On appeal, the court affirmed. The product did not contain any condensed milk, evaporated milk, concentrated milk, or evaporated skimmed milk, sweetened or unsweetened, or any of their fluid derivatives. Therefore, it did not come within the prohibitions of the agency's enabling legislation, Ga. Code Ann. § 42-511. The evidence did not reveal that non-fat dry milk solids, which was the only milk contained in the product, was the same thing as one or more of the kinds of milk set forth in § 42-511. The court rejected the department's assertion that marketing of the product in any container would be deceptive to the public because of its resemblance to milk. The rule did not authorize the department to do more than define standards for milk products and to approve labels for containers. The department could regulate packaging, labeling and branding of the product.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the injunction against the department's prohibiting the corporation from manufacture, distribution, and sale of its product in Georgia. The court modified the judgment to allow the department to make and enforce rules and regulations on the packaging, labeling and branding of the product and the marketing thereof so as to prevent deception of purchasers as to the true nature of the product.

 

1138 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Watts v. State


No. 24744


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 596; 163 S.E.2d 695; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 859


July 9, 1968, Submitted  
September 24, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Shoplifting; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Long, Emeritus.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which convicted her in a jury trial of shoplifting in violation of O.C.G.A. § 26-2640; 1957 Ga. Laws 115. Defendant's motion for new trial was overruled. She claimed that the trial court erred by refusing to declare the statute defining shoplifting unconstitutional, in overruling her motion for new trial, and by failing to give a charge to the jury on intent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested by store employees for shoplifting dresses. Defendant gave a fictitious name until she was identified. Defendant's first argument on appeal was that the shoplifting statute, O.C.G.A. § 26-2640; 1957 Ga. Laws 115, was too vague and indefinite to be enforceable and that it offended the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution as well as Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. III; O.C.G.A. § 2-103. The court disagreed, holding that the language of the statute clearly spelled out what acts amounted to shoplifting and was thus amply definite and certain. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the trial court should have granted her a new trial because the evidence showed that she had no intent to deprive the owner of possession of the dresses. The court found the evidence sufficient to authorize the conviction. Finally, the jury instructions relating to the requisite intent to convict for violating the shoplifting statute adequately covered the issue by defining intent as an element of the offense, and by instructing that the State had the burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's shoplifting conviction.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed an action against defendant bank to recover converted funds. The corporation and the bank filed motions for summary judgment. The Bleckley Superior Court (Georgia) denied the corporation's motion and granted the bank's motion. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation entered into a contract with a company under which the corporation agreed to loan money to the company and the company agreed to assign to the corporation title to its account receivables as security for the loan. OVERVIEW: The victim was an elderly man who was found dead in the hallway of his daughter's home. The victim was stabbed to death with a sharp instrument. Marter v. State


No. 24811


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 569; 163 S.E.2d 702; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 851


September 12, 1968, Submitted  
September 23, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Burglary; rogue and vagabond; constitutional question. Walker Superior Court. Before Judge Coker.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Walker County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of burglary and being a rogue and vagabond.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to quash the rogue and vagabond indictment. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that it was not necessary for the indictment to name the offense with which defendant was charged where the averments of the indictment described an offense against the laws of the State of Georgia. The rogue and vagabond statute, O.C.G.A. § 26-7101, did not violate the due process clause of the United States Constitution because it clearly required two elements for a conviction: (1) being found in or upon certain described buildings, and (2) with intent to steal any goods or chattels. Section 26-7101 was not unconstitutional as a bill of attainder. The court also held that an enumeration of error not raised in the trial court could not be raised for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of burglary and being a rogue and vagabond.

 

1144 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Pharr Rd. Inv. Co. v. Atlanta


No. 24639


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 403; 162 S.E.2d 333; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 796


May 16, 1968, Argued  
June 20, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore, Emeritus.

This case involves the constitutionality of an ordinance of the City of Atlanta levying and assessing license fees upon occupations and businesses therein for 1968 and thereafter, based upon (1) taxable gross revenue, whether received or accrued, during the period of one calendar year, and (2) the total number of employees during the third quarter of the calendar year. The ordinance was amended after the filing of the equitable action, apparently, to meet certain of the complaints in the petition which was then amended to attack other portions of the amended ordinance in named particulars.

A restraining order previously granted was dissolved, and the court, after hearing argument, struck certain paragraphs of the petition on the ground that the attacks thereon were now moot because of the amendment to the ordinance, sustained the motion to dismiss, and dismissed the entire complaint. The appeal is from this final judgment.

The original attacks were based primarily on the fact that gross receipts for the previous year were required for some taxpayers and for the current year for others; and the number of employees [***2] of some taxpayers was determined from the third quarter of the previous year and for others for a certain quarter in the current year. After the ordinance was amended, the petitioner attacked the fee schedules based on (a) the volume of business in the various classifications; and (b) the number of employees -- both of which determined fixed fees to be charged all the various businesses coming within the subclassifications -- as well as the appropriate parts of the ordinance to which these tables referred as being invalid because they are unreasonable, arbitrary, discriminatory and capricious and violative of Art. VII, Sec. I, Par. III (uniformity); Art. I, Sec. I, Par. III (due process); Art. I, Sec. I, Par. II (equal protection) of the Georgia Constitution (Const. of 1945; Code Ann. §§ 2-5403, 2-103, 2-102), and the 14th Amendment of the Federal Constitution (Code § 1-815) in that all businesses in a particular class are not taxed uniformly; and an additional attack upon the discriminatory nature of the ordinance in taxing those persons with rentals for real estate exceeding $ 8,000 taxable gross revenue and no tax on those persons whose rentals are less than that sum in taxable [***3] gross revenue.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review of orders of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which dissolved a previously granted restraining order, struck certain paragraphs of the taxpayer's petition as moot, sustained defendant city's motion to dismiss and dismissed the entire complaint. The petition challenged the constitutionality of a city ordinance levying and assessing license fees upon occupations and businesses.


OVERVIEW: Following the taxpayer's initial petition, the city amended its tax ordinance. After that, the taxpayer amended its petition to challenge the fee schedules, which were based on (1) the volume of business in various classifications and (2) the number of employees. The taxpayer alleged the ordinance violated the Georgia Constitution of 1945, O.C.G.A. §§ 2-5403, 2-103, 2-102, with regard to uniformity, due process, and equal protection and U.S. Const. amend. XIV with regard to uniformity. On appeal, the court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional because its classifications were discriminatory and not related to the law's purpose, which was to generate income based upon an entity's ability to pay and the burdens upon the city to furnish facilities and protection to the entity. The court specifically rejected classifications that exempted those entities receiving less than a certain amount in rental revenue from taxation, which charged a smaller license fee to manufacturers than to non-manufacturers that had identical numbers of employees and gross receipts. and which charged a license fee that jumped by $ 4,000 when one additional employee was added.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1145 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hogan v. Atkins


No. 24632


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 358; 162 S.E.2d 395; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 776


May 14, 1968, Argued  
May 23, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Kennedy.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia), which denied his application for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for violating O.C.G.A. § 26-2701. Defendant contended that § 26-2701 was unconstitutionally vague in violation of the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that § 26-2701 did not make possession the exclusive source of one's guilt. The statute required two elements for conviction: (1) possession of the tools and implements and (2) intent to use these tools and implements in the commission of a crime or knowing that the same are intended to be so used. The court held that § 26-2701 was not unconstitutional for vagueness because it established a reasonably certain standard of conduct. The court also held that it could not hold that the statute was void for vagueness as applied to the evidence because no transcript of the trial was before the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Clark's Valdosta, Inc. v. Valdosta


No. 24574


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 331; 161 S.E.2d 867; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 762


April 8, 1968, Argued  
April 22, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 9 and May 23, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Lowndes Superior Court. Before Judge Lilly.

A general merchandising establishment in the City of Valdosta brought this equitable action against the city alleging there exists a Sunday closing ordinance which is discriminatory against it in favor of other merchants with whom it competes, and for this reason is in violation of the State and Federal Constitutions since it fails to give equal and impartial protection to all persons thereunder. By amendment it also alleges that the ordinance is a special law where there exists a State statute of like import. A motion to dismiss the complaint was filed, and after a hearing the court denied the application for temporary injunction and dismissed the petition, as amended.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant merchant sought review of a dismissal by the Lowndes Superior Court (Georgia) of his suit to enjoin the enforcement of a Sunday closing law he contended was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The merchant contended that a Sunday closing ordinance was in violation of both State and Federal constitutions. The merchant sought to enjoin appellee city from the enforcement of the ordinance. The trial court dismissed the merchant's petition and the merchant appealed. The court determined that the ordinance was the functional equivalent of a state law. The court found that the merchant lacked standing to make a constitutional challenge to the law because he had failed to show any injury as a result of enforcement of the law. The court affirmed the prior dismissal of the merchant's petition for injunction against the city's enforcement of a Sunday closing law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the prior dismissal of the merchant's petition for injunction.

 

1147 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Stanley v. State


No. 24484


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 259; 161 S.E.2d 309; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 736


February 13, 1968, Argued  
April 9, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 22, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: Possession of obscene matter; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Tanksley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) for the possession of obscene matter under an indictment framed under the provisions of Ga. Code Ann. § 26-6301.


OVERVIEW: The obscene material was seized when officers searched defendant's residence pursuant to a search warrant for bookmaking records. The trial court held that the evidence was not to be suppressed, and the court agreed and affirmed the conviction. Police officers in the process of conducting a lawful search were permitted to seize any contraband that would be tangible evidence of the commission of a crime. The court held that defendant's indictment sufficiently charged him with a crime, as it was not essential to charge that he possessed the obscene material with the intent to sell or circulate the material. Ga. Code Ann. § 26-6301 was not unconstitutional in its enactment, and § 26-6301 was not in conflict with the freedom of press as guaranteed by the First and Fourteenth Amendments. Section 26-6301 required reasonable knowledge on defendant's part as to his knowledge that the material was obscene, and such knowledge could be proven solely by circumstantial evidence. The prosecution was not required to prove that defendant knew the community standards for obscenity, nor was there a requirement that the materials in question had to have been previously found to be obscene by a court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of obscene material.

Allison v. Medlock


No. 24362


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 37; 159 S.E.2d 384; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 657


November 14, 1967, Argued  
January 18, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Guess.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: With respect to the grant of injunctive relief in favor of plaintiff truck owner, the owner enumerated as errors a requirement by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) that the owner post a bond, a finding that the city's weight ordinance was valid, and the trial court's dismissal of the complaint.


OVERVIEW: After the city's weight ordinance was declared unconstitutional, defendants, mayor and general council, enacted a new ordinance and declared their intention to arrest and any driver who violated it. The owner sought injunctive relief and argued he complied with Ga. Code Ann. § 68-405(c)(i) by not exceeding the gross weight limit. After granting interlocutory injunctive relief, the trial court ordered that the owner post a bond, and subsequently dismissed the action. The court held that the state weight limits were not intended to withdraw from the city the street regulatory charter power granted to it or upon all municipalities by a subsequent act. Under that power the city was authorized to require trucks of certain weights to travel upon designated streets only. There was thus no conflict between the ordinance and the general law. However, the court reversed because the owner alleged that the permitted streets were wholly inadequate for use by the trucks without great danger to the drivers, the trucks, residents, and traffic. Because the owner was entitled to prove the allegations, dismissal was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the owner's action for injunctive relief with respect to weight limits enacted by defendants.

Tuggle v. Manning


No. 24422


Supreme Court of Georgia


224 Ga. 29; 159 S.E.2d 703; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 654


December 12, 1967, Argued  
January 5, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 18, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hubert.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, landowners and lessee, appealed the judgment of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed their petition against defendants, Board of Commissioners of Roads and Revenues (board), chairman, and building inspectors, for a declaration that a zoning ordinance was unconstitutional and for a mandamus to issue a certificate of zoning compliance and a building permit for the construction of a shopping center.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought to build a shopping center on a tract of land that was zoned for residential and agricultural purposes. Plaintiffs sought to have the land re-zoned in light of its proximity to commercial, religious, and educational developments. However, the board denied their applications for the same. The building inspectors also denied plaintiffs' application for a certificate of zoning compliance and a permit to construct the shopping center. Plaintiffs filed an action against defendants, but the trial court dismissed their petition. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and held that plaintiffs' petition stated a claim upon which relief could be granted. It alleged why the property was not desirable for any of the permitted uses by the existing zoning ordinance and why it was unreasonable and arbitrary as applied to the land. Further, it alleged that the existing zoning ordinance as applied to the land was unconstitutional and arbitrary because it prohibited the use of the land for the only use for which it was reasonably and economically suited, which had the effect of completely destroying plaintiffs' property rights without the payment of just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that dismissed plaintiffs' petition against defendants.

1151 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Grimes v. Burch


No. 24403


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 856; 159 S.E.2d 69; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 988


December 12, 1967, Submitted  
January 4, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Schell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Sheriff of Fulton County (Georgia), citing O.C.G.A. § 26-403, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) discharging appellee inmate from the custody of the Sheriff after a hearing on the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus based on a claim under U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted in municipal court of drunkenness, had escaped, and had been convicted of escape. The inmate contended that she had chronic alcoholism, a disease, at the time of her escape and thus was not guilty of a crime. The court reversed the judgment. The court observed that the inmate's contention that the municipal court sentence was void was without substance and that where one was confined by lawful authority it was his duty to submit until delivered by due process of law. The court noted that as to drunkenness or intoxication, which, depriving men of their reason, put them in a temporary frenzy, the law looked upon it as an aggravation of the offense, rather than an excuse for any criminal misbehavior. The court stated that although the argument that the inmate being a chronic alcoholic, it would amount to cruel and unusual punishment to punish her for violating the law, and that she should not be crucified on a cross of public indifference to her condition, might arouse moral sympathy, it should not control or influence the court's judgment. The court stated that the trial court erred in discharging the inmate from the custody of the Sheriff.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court discharging the inmate from the custody of the Sheriff in her habeas corpus proceeding.

 

1152 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


McLennan v. Aldredge


Nos. 24365, 24387, 24388


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 879; 159 S.E.2d 682; 1968 Ga. LEXIS 1000


November 14, 1967, Argued  
January 4, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Stevens, from Toombs Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which denied their petition for a temporary injunction restraining defendant school officials from enforcing an allegedly illegal ad valorem tax. The school officials appealed from the order overruling their general demurrers to the petition.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature submitted a constitutional amendment to the voters that ratified a system under which a city maintained an independent school system for which an annual ad valorem tax was levied, the city's county had a separate school system for other residents, and city children could not attend the county school system without paying a fee. The voters approved the amendment. Decades later, the taxpayers brought an action against the officials alleging that the amendment violated the Due Process and Equal Protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The trial court entered a judgment denying the taxpayers' petition for a temporary injunction and overruling the officials' general demurrer. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that (1) the ballot on which the amendment was voted did not violate Ga. Const. art. XIII (1877), which left details concerning submission of amendments to the legislature; and (2) the amendment's classification based on population was not unconstitutional because it had a rational basis reflecting the financial and taxable wealth disparity between the city and county systems.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denied the taxpayers' petition for a temporary injunction restraining school officials from enforcing an allegedly illegal ad valorem tax and denying the officials' general demurrers to the petition.

1154 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


S. R. Co. v. Overnite Transp. Co.


No. 24256


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 825; 158 S.E.2d 387; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 720


September 14, 1967, Argued  
November 22, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 7, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Subrogation; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant carrier appealed from a ruling of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) that overruled the carrier's demurrers to plaintiff company's claim for subrogation, along with litigation costs.


OVERVIEW: The company alleged that notice of its subrogation rights under Ga. Code Ann. § 114-403 was given to the carrier before a settlement was made between the parties and that the carrier acted in bad faith, was stubbornly litigious, and caused the company unnecessary expenses. The company sought legal expenses as a part of the damages. The carrier asserted that the petition failed to set forth a cause of action and that § 114-403 was void based on federal interstate commerce preemption. The trial court overruled the carrier's demurrers. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the interstate commerce clause did not prevent states from legislating local concerns, even though such legislation indirectly or incidentally affected interstate commerce. The company's action was not one to recover compensation as the carrier's employee, but was to indemnify the company for a monetary loss caused by the carrier's tortious act to the company's employee. Subrogation was a matter of equity, without regard to any agreement made with the person paying the debt. Further, the allegations in the petition were sufficient to carry the issue of legal expenses to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's overruling of the carrier's demurrer to the company's subrogation claim and request for litigation expenses.

 

1155 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Northeast Factor & Disc. Co. v. Jackson


No. 24285


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 709; 157 S.E.2d 731; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 667


September 14, 1967, Submitted  
October 20, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petition. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Dean.

On May 11, 1966, W. M. Jackson, as Superintendent of Banks of the State of Georgia, filed a bill in equity to enjoin the Northeast Factor & Discount Company, Inc., and James A. Ross from continuing the operation of a private bank (The Exchange Bank) in Ludowici, Ga., and for the appointment of a receiver to liquidate such banking business as directed by the court. A temporary restraining order was issued and after demurrers and an answer, later amended, were filed by the defendants and demurrers to such answer filed by the plaintiff, an interlocutory hearing was held and the temporary restraining order continued and rulings adverse to the defendants on the demurrers were rendered. The defendants now appeal and enumerate as error all the rulings adverse to them.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff bank superintendent's action in equity to enjoin defendants corporation and individual from continuing the operation of a private bank and for the appointment of a receiver to liquidate such banking business, the defendants appealed a judgment of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which issued a temporary restraining order and overruled their demurrers.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the trial court did not err in overruling the defendants' demurrers to the petition inasmuch as the petition alleged that the defendants had engaged in the banking business by continuing the operation of a private bank and because the exercise of such powers by a superior-court chartered corporation authorized the superintendent to petition for the appointment of a receiver to liquidate the banking business, inasmuch as the banking law applied to corporations doing a banking business. The court further found that while a superior-court chartered corporation could not operate a private bank it could purchase and sell the same, and that there could be no limitation on the original owner's right to dispose of the bank, nor could there be any limitation upon the superior-court chartered corporation's right to dispose of it after purchasing the same from the original owner. The court also found that because the sole evidence with reference to the financial standing of the bank showed solvency, not insolvency, it was an abuse of discretion to fail to dissolve the temporary restraining order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment overruling the defendants' demurrers and reversed the trial court's refusal to dissolve the temporary restraining order.

Ward v. Big Apple Super Mkts.


No. 24226


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 756; 158 S.E.2d 396; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 687


September 13, 1967, Argued  
October 20, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 9, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Chairman of the Georgia Milk Commission (commission) sought review of an injunction by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) in favor of appellee supermarket, which alleged that Ga. Code Ann. § 42-523 et seq. (1952) violated the Georgia constitution because it conferred upon the Milk Control Board the authority to fix the price of milk.


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued an injunction unfavorable to the commission, which was authorized to fix the price of milk through the Milk Control Board. On appeal the court affirmed the injunction and held § 42-523 et seq. violated the Due Process Clause of the Georgia Constitution. Because a previous decision, which ruled that that § 42-523 et seq. was unconstitutional, was made by the court in a full bench decision, the court noted that it could only be reversed if the seven justices had agreed, or if there had been some material amendment or facts that would have made the question of law in the commission's action different from the prior decision. The court determined that seven justices were not willing to overrule the prior decision, so it controlled the outcome of the action. The court noted that the legislature could have authorized price fixing without violating the Due Process Clause of the Georgia Constitution only if the milk industry was affected with the public interest. Because it was not, the court ruled that the scheme was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for an injunction against the commission in the supermarket's action regarding milk price fixing.

Frances Wood Wilson Foundation, Inc. v. Bell


No. 24209


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 588; 157 S.E.2d 287; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 615


September 11, 1967, Argued  
September 21, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Rockdale Superior Court. Before Judge Hubert.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff foundation's action against defendants solicitor general and county commissioner challenging the constitutionality of a local act prohibiting the placement of certain minors in private institutions and seeking an injunction, the foundation appealed a judgment of the Rockdale Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained the defendants' general demurrers and dismissed the action.


OVERVIEW: Conceding, but not deciding, that the foundation had named proper parties defendant against whom it might, in an appropriate action, have relief, the court found that the petition failed to set forth a cause of action for any of the relief prayed for. The court further found that until the foundation could show either that the statute in question had been invoked against it, or that there was a direct threat by the authorities to invoke it, it had no standing to come into court and have the court declare the statute invalid. Because the only basis upon which the foundation contended it was entitled to have its rights declared was upon its contention that the statute was unconstitutional, the court concluded that the foundation was not entitled to any of the substantial relief prayed for in its petition, and that the trial court did not err in sustaining the general demurrer and in dismissing it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Manor v. State


No. 24224


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 594; 157 S.E.2d 431; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 619


September 12, 1967, Argued  
September 21, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.

This is an appeal from a murder conviction and sentence without a recommendation for mercy, and is the second appearance in this court, the first trial having been held to be null and void. See Manor v. State, 221 Ga. 866, supra. Many of the facts are the same and reference is made to the above report for a complete study of the case. However, the accused was reindicted, and the present case is entirely different. A resume of the evidence is hereinafter set out. The accused allegedly broke and entered the dwelling of the deceased where his fingerprints were found and identified. She was found dead in a bathtub shortly after the burglary, having died by reason of drowning, and had multiple cuts and bruises on the face and neck with a fracture of the thyroid cartilage of the neck allegedly caused by pressure. The unsworn statement of the accused made at the former trial was read into the record in which he admitted he had gone to her home to take certain items, she surprised him, he "grabbed" her, but did not intend to kill her, that she came in and found him, that he got frightened, pushed her aside to get out of the [***2] way, that "maybe she fainted or maybe he knocked her too hard, but I put her in the bathtub and got scared and run," and he put her in the bathtub to talk to her and ask her forgiveness. He made no statement and offered no evidence during this trial.

The defendant, after conviction, filed a motion for new trial which was subsequently amended to add 37 additional special grounds. The enumerated errors complain of the overruling of the motion for new trial, as amended, and list 40 alleged errors both in the overruling of the motion and occurring during the trial. Because of the quantity of the alleged errors they will not be set out since they are considered in the various headnotes which reflect the grounds argued in appellant's brief.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder. The trial court convicted defendant. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred when it admitted certain evidence. The court held that: (1) reference to other crimes not shown to be connected with the one on trial, reference to an FBI record, and references in a letter that served no relevant purpose squarely put defendant's character as a claimed criminal, even without proof of conviction, into evidence; (2) the references were highly prejudicial and harmful to defendant; (3) the trial court erred when it allowed the matter in question into evidence and when it allowed it to go out to the jury room with the jury; and (4) the errors required the grant of a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that a new trial would be necessary.

 

1159 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Griffith v. Merritt


No. 24218


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 562; 157 S.E.2d 23; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 607


September 11, 1967, Argued  
September 11, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Bell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant democratic party officials sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Bibb County (Georgia) in favor of plaintiff city electors. The electors sought a mandamus against requiring the officials to qualify plaintiff incumbent city mayor as a mayoral candidate and sought a determination of the validity of 1967 Ga. Laws 2180, § 12 (c). The mayor's candidacy was rejected because it was contended that he could not succeed himself.


OVERVIEW: The court stated that the title of the 1967 Act amending the city charter, 1967 Ga. Laws 2180, in addition to dealing with the election of the mayor and aldermen, dealt with other matters affecting the city government. Under the charter prior to the 1967 amendment, a mayor was ineligible to succeed himself. Under the 1967 Act amending the charter, the mayor was eligible to succeed himself for one term. The body of the 1967 Act repealed the provisions of the charter making the mayor ineligible to succeed himself. Section 12 (c) contained matter different from that contained in the title of the Act and violated the Georgia Constitution. The title of the Act declared the intent and purpose of the Act was to make the mayor eligible to succeed himself for one term. Section 12 (b) expressly carried out that purpose, but § 12 (c) denied the right of the present mayor to succeed himself for one term. To remove § 12 (c) from the Act left § 12 (b) unaffected. Section 12 (b) did not re-enact the prohibition against a second successive term. The 1967 Act removed the prohibition by permitting a second successive term. The trial court did not err in granting mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Elliott v. Leathers


No. 24080


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 497; 156 S.E.2d 440; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 583


July 10, 1967, Argued  
July 14, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 115 Ga. App. 352 (154 SE2d 694).



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Court of Appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From two adverse judgments filed against him, appellant filed an action in the Court of Appeals of Georgia. Appellant sought review, by writ of certiorari, from a judgment of the Court of Appeals of Georgia, which dismissed the appeals because the transcript was not filed in the trial court within 30 days after filing of the notice of appeal.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals noted that appellant's counsel timely presented an order for an extension of time that the judge refused to sign. Thereafter, counsel abandoned his original application and filed a new one that was too late. Had counsel relied upon his original application and assert his right to have the judge grant an extension under the mandatory provisions of the last sentence of § 11 of the Appellate Practice Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 6-806, he had his remedy by mandamus to secure judicial review of the judge's ruling that the mandatory feature of the Act was unconstitutional. Counsel did not pursue that remedy, but abandoned his timely application, and sought to pursue an untimely one. The appeals court determined that it had no discretion and that it had to declare the applicable law and dismiss the appeal. The court deemed the dismissal erroneous. The court held that appellant, having complied with the requirements of the Act for obtaining an extension of time for filing of the transcript and thus, having done all he could do toward obtaining it, was entitled to an extension as originally applied for.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals.

 

1161 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. State


No. 24113


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 531; 156 S.E.2d 446; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 598


June 13, 1967, Submitted  
July 14, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Using opprobrious words and abusive language, etc.; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Andrews, Emeritus.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled his demurrers to the indictment, denied his motion for new trial, denied his motion for arrest of judgment, and convicted him for assault and battery on a police officer and the use of opprobrious words and abusive language pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 26-6306.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was one several people who picketed an Army building in opposition to the Viet Nam war. When inductees arrived the protesters blocked the door. The police asked them to move but refused to do so. When the police tried to remove them a scuffle ensued. Defendant was subsequently convicted for assault and battery and the use of opprobrious words or abusive language, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 26-6303. The trial court overruled his demurrers to the indictment and post trial motions. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that § 26-6303 was not so vague, indefinite, or uncertain as to be unconstitutional. Furthermore, it was not necessary for the indictment to specify how the opprobrious words tended to cause a breach of the peace. The assault and language counts charged different offenses and there was no error in the denial of the motion for arrest of judgment on due process and equal protection grounds. Finally, the motion for new trial was properly denied because the evidence was sufficient to warrant conviction. The court also noted that a misnomer in the indictment was immaterial and a relevant malicious mischief charge was appropriately limited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for using opprobrious words and abusive language, and for assault and battery.

 

1162 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Clarke v. Grimes


No. 24146


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 461; 156 S.E.2d 91; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 569


June 14, 1967, Submitted  
June 22, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 6, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus after he was convicted of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and his conviction was affirmed. Defendant's application for a writ of habeas corpus was based on the allegation that prospective jurors were asked on voir dire examination if they conscientiously opposed capital punishment. Defendant did not object to the composition of the jury until after his verdict was rendered. On appeal, the court upheld the trial court's judgment. The court stated that defendant's objection to the qualification of the jury as to persons with conscientious objections to capital punishment was waived because he did not object until after the verdict was rendered. The court determined that, if the attack had been timely, such challenge would not have been meritorious because certain testimony would have established that the jurors, who had conscientious scruples against capital punishment, were not impartial. The court concluded that such jurors were properly subject to challenges for cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1163 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Richmond County Business Asso v. Richmond County


Nos. 24014, 24015


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 337; 155 S.E.2d 395; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 518


April 12, 1967, Argued  
May 4, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 18, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Killebrew.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed on the main appeal; affirmed on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both appellants, citizens and taxpayers, and appellees, county and city government officials, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia), which overruled the government officials' special demurrers and denied the citizens and taxpayers' request for an injunction to restrain the government officials from acting on an election regarding the annexation of property.


OVERVIEW: The citizens and taxpayers asserted that the government officials were preparing to expend large amounts of money regarding the annexation of property but that the expenditures would be illegal because the provisions as to the notice of the holding of the election were not complied with as set forth in 1953 Ga. Laws 2610, § 4. The citizens and taxpayers argued that the election was void because notice of the election was not given at least 30 days before the election in each of the daily newspapers, as required. Proper notice was published in one newspaper but was not published in a second newspaper at least 30 days before the election. The court held that it was error to have denied the request for an injunction because the failure to give the 30 day notice in both the daily newspapers rendered the election void. An injunction was an available and appropriate remedy. In their cross appeal the government officials contended that the allegations in the petition were too vague and indefinite regarding the citizenship of the citizens and taxpayers. The court disagreed and concluded that all of the named citizens and taxpayers were either taxpayers or citizens of the city or county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of an injunction and affirmed the trial court's judgment that overruled the special demurrer filed by the government officials.

 

1164 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Whitehead v. Henson


No. 24017


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 329; 155 S.E.2d 391; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 515


April 13, 1967, Argued  
April 20, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 4, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 115 Ga. App. 81 (153 SE2d 581).

This case is fully reported in Whitehead v. Henson, 115 Ga. App. 81 (153 SE2d 581). The writ of certiorari was granted to review the decision of the Court of Appeals holding that the tax assessors might use part of the findings of the arbitrators as to market value and reject other alleged unauthorized findings of the assessment, and assess property based on the fair market value rather than to use the assessment arrived at by a majority of the arbitrators in conformity with Code Ann. § 92-6912. The court then held a petition by the taxpayer alleging that the tax assessors refused to follow the findings of the majority of the arbitrators as to the assessment did not allege a cause of action, it not being alleged therein that the assessment of the arbitrators was fair, just or equalized.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff taxpayer's action against defendant tax assessors alleging that the assessors refused to follow the findings of the majority of the arbitrators as to an assessment, the taxpayer appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Georgia), which affirmed the trial court's judgment that the petition did not allege a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the taxpayer's petition alleged that the assessment of the majority of the arbitrators had been ignored by the taxing authorities who were proceeding to attempt to collect taxes on a basis other than the arbitrators' assessment, and that it prayed to have their action adjudged illegal and to enjoin further action. The court held that had the arbitrators ignored the established policy and custom and made their assessment at full value, that would have contradicted their oaths to assess according to law, justice and equity. As related to tax law, the court found that the assessment was the amount on which the taxpayer pays taxes. The court further found that to collect taxes on any other basis than the arbitrators' assessment would be contrary to law and that no official except the Revenue Commissioner could be allowed to tamper with or alter that assessment. The court concluded that the petition alleged a cause of action, and that the lower court erred in affirming the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment.

 

1165 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Woodside v. Fulton County


Nos. 23932, 23933


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 316; 155 S.E.2d 404; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 513


February 14, 1967, Argued  
April 6, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 4, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part on the main appeal. Affirmed on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner brought suit in the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) alleging wanton negligence by defendants, county, the State Highway Department (department), and its contractors, and creation of a nuisance, and simple negligence. The property owner requested injunctive relief against the city to prohibit prosecution for safety violations. The trial court sustained the general demurrers and the property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Reversing the sustaining of the county's and department's demurrers, the court explained that the allegations of negligent construction were sufficient to give rise to a cause of action for damages to property under the eminent domain provision of Ga. Const. art. I, § III, para. I, Ga. Code Ann. § 2-301, sometimes called an "inverse condemnation" proceeding. Private property must have been negligently taken or damaged for a public purpose in order for the action to prevail against the defense that recovery was barred by a previous condemnation award. However, the court ruled that the trial court properly sustained the demurrer of the contractors, explaining that the claim was not authorized by Ga. Code Ann. § 95-1710, and that the four-year statute of limitation, Ga. Code Ann. § 3-1001, was applicable, making the claim untimely. The court added that the demurrer of the city was properly sustained because enforcement authorized by the building code was criminal, or at least quasi-criminal in nature, and could not have been restrained by an action in equity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with regard to sustaining the demurrer of the contractors and reversed the judgment with regard to sustaining the demurrer of the county and department in the suit the property owner brought alleging an inverse condemnation. The court affirmed the sustaining of the city's demurrer with regard to the property owner's request that the trial court forbid the city from enforcing its building code.

 

1166 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hawes v. Cordell Ford Co.


Nos. 24002, 24003


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 260; 154 S.E.2d 599; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 489


March 14, 1967, Argued  
March 24, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ad valorem taxes on motor vehicles. Laurens Superior Court. Before Judge Ward.

The present action arose as a result of the enactment of the Act of 1966 (Ga. L. 1966, p. 517), providing for the collection of ad valorem taxes on motor vehicles at the time license plates are purchased rather than at the time ad valorem taxes are paid on other tangible property. The plaintiffs allege that the Act violates various provisions of the Constitution and is being interpreted and enforced contrary to provisions of the Act. Demurrers of the State Revenue Commissioner and of the Tax Commissioner of Laurens County were overruled and it is to such judgment adverse to them that they now appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State Revenue Commissioner (Georgia) and a county tax commissioner, sought review of a judgment of the Laurens Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled their demurrers in an action by plaintiffs, a corporation and others, alleging that 1966 Ga. Laws 517 was unconstitutional and that defendants were interpreting and enforcing it in an unlawful manner.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs petitioned for declaratory relief, claiming that defendants were interpreting and enforcing 1966 Ga. Laws 517, related to the ad valorem taxation of automobiles, in an improper and unfair manner and that the Act was constitutionally infirm. The trial court overruled defendants' demurrers to the petition. The court reversed, concluding that plaintiffs' petition failed to set forth a cause of action for declaratory relief. The court found that no constitutional violation was shown by plaintiffs' allegations that the motor vehicles in their inventory were assessed differently than the inventory of other merchants. Further, the court found that the fact that the caption or title to the Act did not expressly state or refer to the penalty provided for in § 4 thereof did not contravene the constitutional provision against having more than one subject matter in an act or having different subject matter from that expressed in the caption. The court also found that the plaintiffs' claim regarding defendants' enforcement of the Act did not present a justiciable controversy and that their claim of unconstitutional application of the Act was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1167 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Chatterton v. Dutton


No. 23981


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 243; 154 S.E.2d 213; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 479


March 13, 1967, Argued  
March 23, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Reidsville City Court. Before Judge Carr.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Reidsville City Court (Georgia), which denied and dismissed his petition for habeas corpus and returned him to the custody of respondent prison warden. The inmate was found guilty of murder by a jury in a superior court in another county and sentenced to death. The Supreme Court of the United States denied certiorari and he filed the petition.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was found guilty of murder by a jury and given the death penalty. After his appeals were denied, he filed a habeas corpus petition that alleged that the warden of the Georgia State Prison was illegally restraining him of his liberty. The warden maintained that the inmate was in his custody by virtue of his death sentence. The court held that O.C.G.A. § 26-1005 was not unconstitutional or void because it did not violate the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, nor was he denied his due process rights under the statute. The court held that under O.C.G.A. § 26-1005, the jury was entitled to recommend life in prison due to the nature of the crime committed by the inmate. The court noted that the inmate had been afforded a trial in a court of justice, before his peers and had not been treated any differently than any other inmate. Further, the court found that § 26-1005 provided no standard to guide the jury in determining the penalty recommended by it to the trial court and did not give the jury the benefit of an investigation regarding the incident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denied of the inmate's petition for habeas corpus.

Shaffer v. Atlanta


No. 23983


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 249; 154 S.E.2d 241; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 481


March 14, 1967, Argued  
March 23, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed from an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed his petition seeking a declaration that parts of the Housing and Slum Clearance Code, Atlanta, Ga., Ordinance § 15-22, and 1955 Ga. Laws 354, 375 be declared null and void and for an injunction to keep defendants, the City of Atlanta and its officials, from denying him a hearing on whether his properties were nuisances.


OVERVIEW: The city officials found that the property owner's properties violated several sections of the housing code. The property owner claimed that the law and ordinance on which such determinations were based violated his due process and equal protection rights. He also charged that the city officials used the alleged unconstitutional law and ordinance to destroy his property and prevent him from correcting the alleged defects prior to a hearing on whether or not nuisances existed because he was denied the building permits needed to abate the alleged nuisances. The court reversed the judgment dismissing the property owner's petition for declaratory action and injunctive relief and declared that Housing and Slum Clearance Code, Atlanta, Ga., Ordinance § 15-22, which authorized the determination by the city officials of the unfeasibility of rehabilitation of a dwelling, amounted to the taking of private property without due process, without just and adequate compensation therefor, and was discriminatory in its denial to the owner of the equal protection of the laws in violation of both the state and federal Constitutions, and that in that respect the ordinance was null and void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the property owner's petition seeking a declaration that parts of the Housing and Slum Clearance Code and a state law be declared null and void and for an injunction to keep him from being denied a hearing on whether his properties were nuisances.

 

1169 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Berta v. State


No. 23926


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 267; 154 S.E.2d 594; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 492


February 13, 1967, Argued  
March 23, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 6, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Violating the Sabbath day; constitutional question. Savannah City Court. Before Judge Oliver.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Savannah City Court (Georgia) for violating the Sabbath day.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a manager of a drug store, was accused of permitting his employee to sell a pack of playing cards on the Sabbath. The customer admitted that the cards were not necessary for works or charity. Defendant argued that O.C.G.A. § 26-9605, which prohibited labor on Sunday, was discriminatory because it selected the Christian Sunday as the Sabbath day and discriminated against those religious groups that used Saturday as the Sabbath day. The court noted that opinions could differ as to whether abstaining from labor on Sunday was a religious duty; but that it was certain that the legislature of Georgia prescribed it as a civil duty. The court ruled that § 26-9605 could be fairly and rationally be treated as a legitimate police regulation and was thus valid. The court reasoned that the fact that a determination must be made in each case as to whether the act charged as violating § 26-6905 was a work of necessity or charity did not make § 26-6905 or the accusation drawn under it, so vague, indefinite, and uncertain as to render it unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1170 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hinton v. State


Nos. 23956, 23957


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 174; 154 S.E.2d 246; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 457


February 14, 1967, Submitted  
February 23, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 9, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Damaging flags, etc.; constitutional question. Crisp Superior Court. Before Judge Horne.

The defendants were indicted, tried and convicted under Code § 26-7202 and the Act of 1960 (Ga. L. 1960, p. 985; Code Ann. § 86-1210). After indictment a motion to quash the indictment and challenge the array of the traverse jury was filed in each case and after hearing overruled. Demurrers were filed challenging the Act under which the indictments were made in one case and after verdict the defendants' motions for new trial were overruled. They now appeal and enumerate as error these rulings adverse to them.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Crisp County (Georgia), which convicted them of damaging flags under O.C.G.A. §§ 26-7202, 86-1210.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were involved in a "freedom march" and a crowd had gathered at the county courthouse. Defendants moved over to the flagpole and proceeded to lower the flags. One defendant stated that the African-American community was in a state of mourning and he intended to lower the flag to half-mast to symbolize the state of mourning. As the flag was being lowered, others in the group closed in, removed the flags from the lanyard, actually tearing the American flag and damaging the State's flag. They were convicted of damaging the flags, and they appealed. The court rejected defendants' argument that the jury was unfairly drawn because the court determined that the jury represented a proper make-up of the community. The court also found that §§ 26-702, 86-1210 were not so vague and uncertain as to be unconstitutional. Moreover, the court held that the trial court's action in directing the jury to return to the jury room and arrive at a unanimous verdict if possible was not error because the poll of the jury disclosed that its verdict was not unanimous. Finally, the court concluded that the evidence authorized the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for damaging flags.
