Calhoun v. State Highway Dep't


No. 23867


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 65; 153 S.E.2d 418; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 416


January 9, 1967, Argued  
January 19, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 25, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 114 Ga. App. 501 (151 SE2d 806).

A certiorari writ was granted in this case of condemnation to review the Court of Appeals in its decision reported in State Hwy. Dept. v. Calhoun, 114 Ga. App. 501 (151 SE2d 806), where it was held that the lower court erred in refusing to grant a motion for new trial complaining that the court erred in charging the jury that it should look to all circumstances affecting the value of land taken at the time of taking including enhancement resulting from knowledge of the impending taking. The applicant alleges error in that the trial court correctly charged the law and the Court of Appeals should not have reversed because (1) the appellant failed to raise that question in the lower court in conformity with Code Ann. § 70-207 (a) (Ga. L. 1965, pp. 18, 31, as amended); (2) the 1966 Act defining just and adequate compensation (Ga. L. 1966, p. 320), which allegedly changed the method of determining value of property taken, which specifically denies consideration of enhancement resulting from knowledge of the impending taking, deprived the appellee of vested rights [***2] and therefore should not have been applied since it was adopted as law after the trial of the case; (3) its application by the Court of Appeals was in violation of constitutional guarantees specifically provided by the Georgia Constitution; and (4) the 1966 Act, supra, is otherwise unconstitutional. Because of the apparent confusing state of the law as to what rule of the law the Court of Appeals should have applied, this court granted certiorari.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Georgia), which granted certiorari in a condemnation action to review its prior decision that reversed a lower court's decision refusing to grant a motion for a new trial because the trial court erred in charging the jury that it should have looked to all circumstances affecting the value of land taken at the time of taking including enhancement.


OVERVIEW: The applicant alleged inter alia, that the trial court properly charged the jury and that the decision should not have been reversed. He further alleged that the 1966 Act defining just and adequate compensation, which allegedly changed the method of determining value of property taken, which specifically denied consideration of enhancement resulting from knowledge of the impending taking and should not have been applied because it was adopted into law after the trial of the case, and that its application by the appellate court was in violation of constitutional guarantees specifically provided by the Georgia Constitution. The court held that Ga. Const. of 1945, art. I, § 3, para. I (amended 1960), O.C.G.A. § 2-301, removing the requirement of "being first paid" as to property taken for public roads and streets, did not alter the demand that "just and adequate compensation." The court held that because the 1966 Act was an attempt to invade the exclusive jurisdiction of the judicial department, it offended the constitutional separation of powers and was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

1172 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Fortson


No. 23919


Supreme Court of Georgia


223 Ga. 7; 152 S.E.2d 847; 1967 Ga. LEXIS 397


January 3, 1967, Argued  
January 6, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction; transmission of returns from election for Governor, etc. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters appealed the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) that denied their petition for an interlocutory injunction against defendants, the Georgia Secretary of State and other state officials, to prevent the Secretary from presenting returns from an election for governor to the general assembly to decide the outcome.


OVERVIEW: An election for governor was held, and no candidates received a majority of the votes. No runoff election was held under Ga. Code Ann. § 34-1514. Instead, the Secretary planned to present the election returns to the general assembly to decide the outcome of the election pursuant to Ga. Const. art, V § I, paras. II, II, and IV. The voters filed a petition for an interlocutory injunction to prevent the Secretary from presenting the returns to the general assembly. The trial court refused to grant the voters an injunction and dismissed their petition. The voters appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly denied injunctive relief. The court reasoned that Ga. Const. art V reserved the power and right to the general assembly to elect a governor from the two persons having the highest number of votes where no person received a majority of the votes cast in the general election. Further, the runoff provision in Ga. Code Ann. § 34-1514 did not apply because the legislation had to defer to the conflicting provisions dealing with the election of a governor in Ga. Const. art. V as the supreme law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the voters' request for an interlocutory injunction and dismissing their petition.

 

1173 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. Wade


Nos. 23796, 23797, 23798


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 805; 152 S.E.2d 745; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 636


November 14, 1966, Argued  
December 5, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nonresident motorist; constitutional question. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff survivor, in which service was sought against the nonresident motorist's estate under the Nonresident Motorists Act of 1937 (Act), 1937 Ga. Laws 732, as amended 1957 Ga. Laws 649, Ga. Code Ann. § 68-810, appellants, administrator and others, challenged the order of the Muscogee Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled appellants' pleas to the jurisdiction, the traverse of service, and the pleas in bar.


OVERVIEW: In an action brought by the survivors against appellants, service was sought under the Act and made on the Secretary of State of Georgia. No other claim or service was had on appellants nor was the claim filed in the foreign state. Appellants specially appeared and filed pleas to the jurisdiction and bar, and traverses of service. The trial court overruled the special pleas. The court affirmed the ruling and held that § 68-810 was not subject to the constitutional attacks made upon it. The legislature provided that, in the exercise of police power in regulating state highways, service was made upon the personal representative of a nonresident motorist who had died and who was the subject of an action. When the nonresident motorist drove on the state's highways, he subjected himself to the court's jurisdiction and consented to bind his legal representative in an action arising out of any accident. The statute was narrowly drawn, provided for due process, and applied only to actions arising in Georgia. The fact that the survivor failed to file notice of her claim against the estate of the nonresident motorist with the foreign state was not a bar or a defense to the action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellants' pleas of jurisdiction and bar and traverse of service, in an action by the survivor against the decedent's estate under the Act.

L. 1964, p. 128, Sec. 12, et seq.). Constitution, and by attempting to exercise the power of eminent domain without provision for the payment of just and adequate compensation, without due process of law, and impairing the obligations of contracts. The prayers are for equitable relief and the declaration that Sections 12 and 13 (c) of Ga. L. 1964, p. 128, be declared unconstitutional [***2] and void. I, § III, para. I, the court held that the Act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which found for petitioners in their action seeking to enjoin the Department from removing certain outdoor signs on petitioners' property pursuant to the Georgia Outdoor Advertising Control Act of 1964.

Glendale Estates v. Americus


No. 23688


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 610; 151 S.E.2d 142; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 576


September 13, 1966, Submitted  
October 13, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Sumter Superior Court. Before Judge Marshall.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mobile home park owner sought review of a judgment from the Sumter Superior Court (Georgia) sustaining the general demurrer of defendant mayor and city council and dismissing the petition for an injunction preventing the city from making a monthly charge for water supplied to each mobile home space.


OVERVIEW: The mobile home park owner constructed a supply line to each mobile home pad. The mobile home park owner subsequently discovered that the city was making a monthly charge for water supplied to each mobile home space. The mobile home park owner then filed a petition seeking an injunction. The trial court dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The mobile home park owner contended that the city violated an agreement and understanding that all of the mobile home spaces would be served by one master meter, that the charge for each space was excessive and beyond the established legal rate, that the charge was discriminatory and arbitrary, and that the charge was a tax and violated certain stated provisions of the federal and state constitutions. The court found that the monthly minimum rate upon each single family mobile home dwelling unit was for the purchase of water supplied by the city and not a tax. The court found that any agreement between the city and the mobile home park owner was ultra vires and was not binding on any future mayor and council to prevent them from enacting an ordinance changing or altering the terms of the purported agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court sustaining the general demurrer of the mayor and the city council and dismissing the petition for an injunction preventing the city from making a monthly charge for water supplied to each mobile home space.

1177 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


McDonald v. State


No. 23694


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 596; 151 S.E.2d 121; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 570


September 13, 1966, Submitted  
October 6, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motor vehicle certificate of title violation; constitutional question. Habersham Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted and charged with a misdemeanor. Defendant appealed the decision of the Habersham Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled defendant's demurrers and sustained the State's demurrers to defendant's special plea.


OVERVIEW: The indictment charged that defendant acquired a motor vehicle, sold and disposed of it as wreckage and salvage, and failed to mail and deliver the certificate of title and manufacturer's serial plate from the motor vehicle to the State Revenue Commissioner as required by law. Defendant, by special plea and also a ground of demurrer, attempted to show that the statute was unconstitutional as being a burden on interstate commerce. The court held that neither the plea nor the ground of demurrer specified any constitutional provision as the one defendant contended was being violated. The court also held that a demurrer could attack only those defects which appeared on the face of the indictment and that where a demurrer sought to add extrinsic matter, it failed as a speaking demurrer. Therefore, the court held that the trial judge did not err in overruling defendant's demurrers to the indictment nor in sustaining the State's demurrers to the special plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court overruling defendant's demurrers and sustaining the State's demurrers to defendant's special plea.

 

1178 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ga. Bar Asso v. Lawyers Title Ins. Corp.


Nos. 23613, 23614


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 657; 151 S.E.2d 718; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 592


July 12, 1966, Argued  
October 6, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 3, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment; constitutional questions. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Long.

Lawyers Title Insurance Corporation, a corporation engaged in the business of writing title insurance, filed an action for declaratory judgment against the Georgia Bar Association, alleging that the association is contending that the petitioner is engaged in the unauthorized practice of law with respect to certain of its activities, and the association has sent the petitioner a copy of a resolution formulated by the Board of Governors of the Georgia Bar Association, which directed the executive secretary of the association to write a letter to each title insurance company doing business in Georgia requesting it to cease specified activities which the Committee on Unauthorized Practice of Law of the association deems to constitute the unlawful practice of law, and threatening to bring an action to restrain the practices specified unless it agrees to cease such practices. The petitioner asserted that its activities which the association claims constitute the unlawful practice of law are not violative of the applicable statutes of the State of Georgia.

 [***2] The Georgia Bar Association by demurrer attacked the provisions of the Act of 1931 (Ga. L. 1931, pp. 191-194), codified as §§ 9-401 through 9-405, as amended by Ga. L. 1937, pp. 753-754, as being violative of stated provisions of the Constitution. It filed an answer in which it asserted the unconstitutionality of these statutes, and a cross action which specified the particulars in which it claimed that the petitioner is engaged in the unauthorized practice of law. It prayed that the justiciable issue between the parties be decided, and that the petitioner be permanently restrained from the acts enumerated. The trial judge upheld the validity of Chapter 9-4 of the Code, as amended by Ga. L. 1937, pp. 753-754.

A pre-trial order approved the stipulation of the parties that the issue in the case remaining for decision was "whether or not the evidence shows any activity of the plaintiff, as alleged in the pleadings, if proven, is a violation of the Georgia statutes defining the practice of law as those statutes may have been construed by the Appellate Courts of Georgia."

On November 16, 1965, the trial judge entered an order declaring the activities which, in his opinion, violated [***3] the Georgia statutes. An appeal was filed by the Georgia Bar Association, and a cross appeal by Lawyers Title Insurance Corporation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed on both the main appeal and the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Bibb Superior Court (Georgia) entered a judgment declaring that certain activities of appellee title insurance corporation did not constitute the unauthorized practice of law and did not violate Ga. Code Ann. §§9-401 through 9-405. The trial court also sustained the assertions of appellant state bar association that other acts of the title insurance company constituted the unauthorized practice of law. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state bar association and the title insurance corporation challenged the trial court's judgment that the evidence at trial showed that the only activities of the title insurance corporation that violated Ga. Code Ann. §§ 9-401 through 9-405 were the walk-in business and the advertisements encouraging it. On appeal, the court held that the trial court correctly determined the issues of law and fact. In reaching its decision, the court agreed with the trial court that Ga. Code Ann. § 9-403 allowed the title insurance corporation to examine records, issue abstracts of title, certify to the correctness of them, issue policies of insurance on titles to real or personal property, and receive payment for those services. The court also agreed with the trial court that the title insurance corporation violated state law when it held itself out to the public as being authorized to render legal services and advice in the handling and closing of real estate transactions between title insurance applicants and third persons, advertising that the employment of an attorney was not necessary, and advertising that the fees and charges for its services were the same as those charged by attorneys.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgment entered by the trial court.

 

1179 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. State


No. 23669


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 525; 150 S.E.2d 834; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 539


September 13, 1966, Argued  
September 22, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Failure to pay for agricultural products; constitutional question. Sumter Superior Court. Before Judge Marshall.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for failure to pay for agricultural products in violation of O.C.G.A. § 5-9914. Defendant sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Sumter County (Georgia), which overruled his demurrers and his motion to quash the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant bought corn, but failed and refused to pay for it. Defendant contended that § 5-9914 violated his due process rights under Ga. Const. art. I, § 1, para. III. Defendant further asserted that O.C.G.A. § 5-9914 violated Ga. Const. art. I, § 1, para. XXI, which prohibited imprisonment for a debt, and violated O.C.G.A. § 26-201. The court held that O.C.G.A. § 5-9914 was not unconstitutional as a whole for any of defendant's attacks upon it. Although defendant did attack the § 5-9914 as a whole as being violative of O.C.G.A. § 26-201, the word "intention," as used therein, did not mean an intention to violate a penal statute, but an intention to commit an act prohibited thereby.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1180 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Lee v. Jesup


No. 23679


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 530; 150 S.E.2d 836; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 543


September 13, 1966, Argued  
September 22, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petition. Wayne Superior Court. Before Judge Flexer.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Wayne County (Georgia), which sustained the demurrer filed by appellee city and dismissed the residents' action challenging the city's annexation of a tract of land.


OVERVIEW: The residents filed an action that challenged a special act passed by the city to annex a tract of land. The city filed a demurrer to the complaint, and the trial court sustained the demurrer and dismissed the action. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the existence of a prior statute that permitted the enlargement of municipal boundaries did not deprive the general assembly of the power to have altered or amended the municipal boundaries without the consent of the parties affected. Ga. Const. art. III, § I, para. I, vested the authority to create or alter municipal systems in the general assembly. The court explained that an action that expanded municipal boundaries did not violate the constitutional protections of due process or the equal protection of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1181 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Rice v. Cook


Nos. 23623, 23602, 23606


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 499; 150 S.E.2d 822; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 528


July 14, 1966, Argued  
September 8, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 22, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore.

While three appeals were filed by the separate appellants, all three are the same, and these appellants comprise the State school officials, and the local school officials of Fulton and DeKalb Counties, all named as defendants in this mandamus action brought by the school officials of the City of Atlanta, an independent school system, in their official capacities and as citizens and taxpayers. The petitioners seek to prevent the state officials in the administration of the Minimum Foundation Program of Education Act (Ga. L. 1964, pp. 3, 49; Code Ann. §§ 32-601 to 32-657) from giving effect to a proviso therein which has the effect of reducing the allotment of state school funds to all municipal or independent school systems, including the Atlanta system, from the amounts which such systems could receive if the proviso were to be ignored or held unconstitutional. The petition, as amended, in count 1, seeks to have the proviso declared unconstitutional for a number of reasons; and, in count 2, to have the court make the state officials ignore it in determining the school funds for the [***2] Atlanta school system. Inasmuch as, under the law, an increased allotment of state school funds for Atlanta would come at the expense of the county school systems of DeKalb and Fulton, these local school officials were named also as defendants. Under the minimum foundation program, local school systems -- area, independent and county -- are required to furnish, according to a formula, local funds to support the program of education. The proviso mentioned above requires all independent school systems in a county to be calculated on a percentage greater than 100% which, in effect, causes all such systems to produce more local funds and thereby reduces the amount of state funds the system would receive. The Atlanta system seeks to be considered without reference to the proviso applying to independent school systems because it is in more than one county, and this proviso which requires an increased financial ability to pay, that is, increased local funds with decreased state participation, is not applicable because it is, in the language of the statute, not "located within a county" but rather is located in two counties, and that the state officials be required to calculate its financial [***3] ability to pay by the proviso applying to all local units of administration without applying the special proviso required of independent school systems within a county. Demurrers were filed, and after a hearing, the court refused to rule on the constitutional attack but overruled the demurrers to count 2 and ordered the state officials to calculate the Atlanta system's financial ability to pay according to the Act without giving effect to the proviso applying to independent school systems. The appeal is from this final judgment overruling the general demurrers to count 2 and granting the mandamus absolute.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city school officials filed a mandamus action against defendant state and county school officials to prevent the state officials from giving effect to a provision under the Minimum Foundation Program of Education Act, O.C.G.A. §§ 32-601 to 32-657. Defendants appealed the overruling of their demurrers by the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that the offensive provision under the Act had the effect of reducing the allotment of state school funds to all municipal and independent school systems. Plaintiffs sought consideration without reference to the provision applicable to independent school systems because their school was located in more than one county. Plaintiffs sought to have the provision declared unconstitutional and to have defendants ignore it in determining school funds for the city school system. The court held that the provision was intended to apply to independent school systems, such as that of plaintiffs, and that defendants correctly used it as a basis for determining the amount of local money the city school system had to raise.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1182 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ingram v. Payton


No. 23557


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 503; 150 S.E.2d 825; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 529


June 15, 1966, Argued  
September 8, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 22, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Peeler.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the superintendent and members of a city board of education, applied for a writ of mandamus against defendants, the superintendent and members of the state board of education. The Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia) sustained the state board's general demurrer, and the city board sought review.


OVERVIEW: The city board sought to require the state board to calculate the city board's financial needs under the Minimum Foundation Program of Education Act (Act), 1964 Ga. Laws 3-49, without applying § 22(B)(1) of the Act. The main issue was whether there was a rational basis for classifying local units of school administration differently so as to create disparity of fiscal treatment that imposed on independent school systems the requirement to pay a greater share of the costs imposed by the Act than was imposed on other local units of school administration. The court held that: (1) the Georgia constitution classified independent and county school systems separately; (2) there was a reasonable basis for such classification; (3) the classification was not offensive although it was made without mathematical nicety and might have resulted in some inequality; (4) the city board's complaint should be directed to the legislature; and (5) prior case law determined that § 22B of the Act was applicable even though the city board's jurisdiction fell within two separate counties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1183 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 23584


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 552; 150 S.E.2d 868; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 552


July 11, 1966, Argued  
September 8, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 22 and October 6, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Validation of bonds; constitutional question. Telfair Superior Court. Before Judge O'Connor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment of the Telfair Superior Court (Georgia), which found in favor of appellees, the State of Georgia and a county, and validated the county's issuance of revenue bonds in the taxpayers' action for a declaration that an amendment to the Georgia Constitution for the issuance of revenue bonds was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county issued revenue bonds pursuant to 1960 Ga. Laws 1400, which was an amendment to Ga. Const. art. VII, para. V, in order to finance the construction of a plant for lease to private industry. The taxpayers filed an action for a declaration that the amendment violated the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment because it failed to limit the issuance of bonds for public purposes. The trial court validated appellees' issuance of such bonds. On appeal by the taxpayers, the court reversed, holding that the amendment violated the Fourteenth Amendment. The amendment permitted the issuance of revenue bonds for a purely private purpose by exempting certain private industry from ad valorem taxes for constructing new buildings or plants, even if the industry already had such buildings or plants in the county. Therefore, the amendment did not provide for the public purpose of promotion and development of new industry. Such differentiation in taxation constituted a taking of the property of the taxpayers and other private industries that were not exempt from such taxes without due process of law. It also denied the taxpayers equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that validated an amendment to the Georgia Constitution concerning the issuance of revenue bonds.

 

1184 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Shaffer


Nos. 23559, 25360


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 334; 149 S.E.2d 668; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 477


June 15, 1966, Argued  
June 23, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 7, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Alverson.



DISPOSITION: Appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants brought actions against defendant landlord seeking injunctions to prevent their eviction. The Superior Court, Fulton County (Georgia), struck both petitions and the tenants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tenants sought injunctions to prevent their evictions in dispossessory warrant proceedings on the ground that Ga. Code Ann. § 61-303 was unconstitutional. They argued that it violated due process by requiring tenants in such an action to file a bond as a condition to entering a counteraffidavit. The trial court struck the petitions and the tenants appealed. The court dismissed the appeals, holding that since the tenants had already been evicted, their actions to enjoin removal had become moot. The suits as related to declaratory judgment not only became moot, but they set forth no cause for that relief.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the tenants' appeals.

 

1185 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Atlanta Americana Motor Hotel Corp. v. Undercofler


No. 23482


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 295; 149 S.E.2d 691; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 461


May 11, 1966, Argued  
June 23, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for tax refund. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pharr.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a decision by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained defendant State Revenue Commissioner's (commissioner) general demurrers to the taxpayer's petition seeking a tax refund.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer asserted that it was entitled to maintain the action as a "taxpayer" by virtue of the two statutory refund provisions, Ga. Code Ann. § 92-3434(a); Ga. Code Ann. § 92-8436(b), which the taxpayer pleaded as the jurisdictional bases for the action. The court stated that the statutory authority to sue for a refund did not provide the standing to attack the constitutionality of a statute where the facts alleged showed no injury from enforcement of such statute. The court found that the taxpayer itself used the property to make its rooms livable and rentable to guests. The fact that a part of the charge for the rooms was allegedly attributable to such property did not cause such use of it to be a resale. Although the taxpayer's guests also used the property while occupying the rooms, the guests used the property as a part of the rooms, which they rented. Not many of them would have cared to use the rooms without any of the items such as carpeting and furniture. The taxpayer's allegations did not show that the taxpayer's purchase of the personal property was for the purpose of resale. Thus, the court affirmed the judgment sustaining the commissioner's general demurrers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which sustained the commissioner's general demurrers to the taxpayer's petition seeking a tax refund.

 

1186 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Holland Furnace Co. v. Willis


No. 23430


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 156; 149 S.E.2d 93; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 423


April 11, 1966, Argued  
May 26, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to vacate judgment for damages. Macon City Court. Before Judge Phillips.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a judgment of the City Court of Macon (Georgia), which sustained appellee's demurrers to the corporation's motions to vacate and set aside appellee's judgment for damages against the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The corporation contended that the judgment against it was void because the corporation was denied due process by operation of Ga. Code Ann. § 22-1508 which provided for service of process on nonresident corporations through the secretary of state. The corporation further contended that § 22-1508 failed to assure it of a reasonable time within which to prepare a defense and file defensive pleadings. The court held that there was no applicable law which guaranteed the corporation a reasonable time within which to prepare and file a defense after service of process by the secretary of state and despite the fact that the corporation did receive notice of the suit pending against it by appellee, the corporation was denied due process because it was not provided, as a matter of right, with notice and an opportunity to be heard. The court further held that the corporation had standing to attack the validity of § 22-1508 because the defective feature of the statute operated injuriously to the corporation's property interests. The court held that the trial court erred in sustaining the demurrers to the motions to vacate and set aside the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment which sustained appellee's demurrers to the corporation's motion to vacate and set aside the judgment for damages against the corporation.

 

1187 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Continental Casualty Co. v. Swift & Co.


No. 23407


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 80; 148 S.E.2d 489; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 404


April 12, 1966, Argued  
April 19, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.

This is a suit seeking to enjoin an alleged collusive agreement between a tortfeasor and the injured party who received certain workmen's compensation payments from the plaintiff for an injury arising out of and in the course of his employment which will have the alleged effect of voiding the legal liability of the tortfeasor to pay damages to the injured person who received the workmen's compensation benefits from the plaintiff. The petitioner likewise prayed for a money judgment. The brief history of the statute under which this suit is allegedly brought is as follows: In 1937 the General Assembly amended a number of sections of the Workmen's Compensation Law. One of the amended sections was Code § 114-403, the legislature striking the words "under circumstances creating a legal liability in some person," in the second line thereof and substituting in lieu thereof the words, "under circumstances whereby payment is made by some person." Ga. L. 1937, p. 528. In Lloyd Adams, Inc. v. Liberty Mut. Ins. Co., 190 Ga. 633 (10 SE2d 46), this language declaring that an injured employee may maintain a suit against a tortfeasor [***2] after having accepted payment from him for damages sustained was held to be a legal absurdity, unconstitutional, null and void.

The present suit is predicated upon the clearly stricken words "under circumstances creating a legal liability in some person," the insurance carrier of the employer seeking the right of subrogation under Code § 114-403 before the 1937 amendment. General demurrers were sustained to the petition, and the appeal is to the judgment dismissing the petition.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of the decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) that sustained general demurrers to the insurer's petition and dismissed the action. The action was filed against appellee injured party and tortfeasor and sought to enjoin an alleged collusive agreement between them by which the injured party would receive workmen's compensation payments which would void the legal liability of the tortfeasor to pay damages.


OVERVIEW: The injured person filed suit against the tortfeasor and was entering into an agreement of settlement when the insurer filed suit to enjoin the alleged collusive agreement between them. The injured person was hurt during his employment, and the insurer was responsible to pay under the workmen's compensation laws. The insurer filed suit under O.C.G.A. § 114-403. The lower court sustained the general demurrers of the injured person and tortfeasor and dismissed the suit. The court affirmed the dismissal because it found that O.C.G.A. § 114-403 provided no subrogation rights to the insurer at all. The insurer for the injured person's employer had no right to intervene, enjoin, or otherwise affect the suit by the injured person against the tortfeasor to prevent a settlement between them or to be subrogated to the claim of the injured person against the tortfeasor for the amount it had paid the injured person under the terms of its contract with the employer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1188 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Strange v. Strange


No. 23395


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 44; 148 S.E.2d 494; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 393


March 15, 1966, Argued  
April 7, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for child support. Spalding Superior Court. Before Judge McGehee.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the judgment of the Spalding Superior Court (Georgia), which ordered the father to pay for the support of his three minor children to their mother until each one reached the age of 18 years, married, or became self-supporting. The father challenged the constitutionality of the Georgia Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act.


OVERVIEW: The father asserted that under O.C.G.A. § 2-5101 he was entitled to a jury trial, and since the Georgia Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act did not provide for a jury trial or give to him the right to a trial by jury, it was void. The court disagreed and held that at common law, prior to the first Constitution of Georgia, there was a duty imposed upon the father of a minor child to support it either during coverture or subsequent to a divorce of the parents. The court held that prior decisions constituted a ruling that the divorced mother could not bring a common law action against the father of the minor children. The Act for the support of the dependent children and others was wholly of statutory origin and unknown to the common or statutory law of England prior to the first Georgia Constitution, and therefore, in a proceeding under the Act, the father of the minor children was not entitled to a jury trial as a constitutional right. The court held that the Act was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1189 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Fulton County v. Woodside


Nos. 23343, 23344


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 90; 149 S.E.2d 140; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 407


February 15, 1966, Argued  
April 7, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 5, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction, etc.; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and others, sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Georgia), which continued temporary restraining orders against the city prohibiting it from prosecuting plaintiff for building code violations in an action brought by plaintiff in which he challenged the Chief Judge Act, 1963 Ga. Laws p.646, as being unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action seeking to enjoin defendants from prosecuting him for building code violations on the basis that the Chief Judge Act was unconstitutional. The trial court continued a temporary restraining order it had issued against defendants. Upon review, the court reversed. The court found that plaintiff had standing to attack the constitutionality of the legislation where plaintiff alleged that the Act deprived him of his right to present his petition to any particular judge of the superior court. The court held that the trial court erred by declaring 1963 Ga. Laws p. 646, §§ 2 and 3 of the Act unconstitutional under Ga. Code Ann. § 2-3801 where the power given to the Chief Judge under the Act did no more than make the Chief Judge responsible for the administrative and expeditious disposition of the business of the superior court. The court determined that some method of assigning the business of the court among the various judges was needed. The court concluded that it was not inconsistent that the multiple judges of the circuit court shared co-equal jurisdiction and yet were to be subject to reasonable rules designed to expedite the business of the court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that continued temporary restraining orders against the city prohibiting it from prosecuting plaintiff for building code violations in a declaratory action brought by plaintiff in which he challenged the constitutionality of an act regarding the administration of the superior court.
