Nash v. Nat'l Preferred Life Ins. Co.


No. 23331


Supreme Court of Georgia


222 Ga. 14; 148 S.E.2d 402; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 385


February 15, 1966, Argued  
March 14, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment, etc. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hubert.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, taxing officials of the county, sought review of a declaratory judgment, entered by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), ruling that appellants were prohibited from imposing taxes and levies upon appellee, a life insurance company, because of the provisions of Ga. Code 1933, § 56-1310.


OVERVIEW: Appellee alleged officials of the county, appellants, levied premium taxes and license taxes against appellee and all other life insurance companies doing business within the county, pursuant to a 1959 Act and ordinance. Appellee prayed that appellants be temporarily enjoined from enforcing levies and that the court enter a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was void because it was repealed by Ga. Code 1933, § 56-1310 (the Act). The Act provided that the state pre-empted the field of tax imposition and levies upon life insurance companies with exceptions. The trial court entered a declaratory judgment ruling the Act repealed the right of the county to apply provisions of the license tax ordinance to insurance companies and the license tax ordinance was void. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding the Act was not unconstitutional, as appellants contended. The Act clearly intended that the county would not have such taxing power.


OUTCOME: On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling that the appellants improperly imposed levies and taxes upon appellee because the state had pre-empted the appellant's authority to do so.

 

1191 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Southern Guaranty Ins. Co.


No. 23259


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 804; 147 S.E.2d 424; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 702


December 13, 1965, Submitted  
February 23, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Injunction, etc. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.

Southern Guaranty Insurance Company brought an action for declaratory judgment and injunction against James H. Nelson, Gerardo Otero, and Pacific Indemnity Company. On July 7, 1963, the plaintiff issued a policy of automobile liability insurance to Gerardo Otero, for a term from July 7, 1963, to July 7, 1964, covering two automobiles, which policy contained an exclusion endorsement as follows: "It is agreed that the insurance afforded by this policy shall not apply with respect to any claim arising from accidents which occur while any automobile is being operated by Ferdinand Otero, son, nor Gerardo A. Otero, Jr., son." On November 1, 1963, Gerardo A. Otero, Jr., was operating one of the automobiles covered by the policy, when he was involved in an accident with James H. Nelson, and a suit for damages was filed by Nelson against Gerardo A. Otero.

The plaintiff sought a declaration that it was not liable to provide any insurance coverage, or to defend any suit filed by Nelson, as a result of the accident on November 1, 1963. Pacific Indemnity Company was named as a defendant because it is subrogated to the rights [***2] of James H. Nelson against Gerardo Otero to the extent of payments made by Pacific Indemnity Company to James H. Nelson, on behalf of Nelson's employer, as required by the Workmen's Compensation Law. The plaintiff further sought a declaration that it is not bound to provide any insurance coverage or defense with respect to any lien or right of subrogation claimed by Pacific Indemnity Company. Injunction was prayed to maintain the status until the question of the liability of the plaintiff could be adjudicated.

Answers were filed, and amendments to the answers and to the petition. The plaintiff and the defendant Nelson both filed motions for summary judgment. The trial judge granted the motion for summary judgment of the plaintiff and denied that of the defendant Nelson. In his judgment he declared that: The policy of insurance, including the endorsement, affords no coverage with respect to the automobile accident on November 1, 1963, and imposes no obligation upon the plaintiff to defend any suit arising out of this accident, and imposes no obligation upon the plaintiff to pay any damages that might be recovered by James H. Nelson or Pacific Indemnity Company. Section 56-407A [***3] (c) of the Code (Ga. L. 1963, p. 588) is unconstitutional since it contains matter different from that expressed in the caption, in contravention of the Constitution, Art. III, Sec. VII, Par. VIII (Code Ann. § 2-1908). All of the defendants were permanently enjoined from taking any action against the plaintiff to collect any sum of money as damages for injuries arising out of the accident of November 1, 1963.

James H. Nelson and Pacific Indemnity Company appealed from the judgment granting the motion for summary judgment of the plaintiff, and enumerated as error the rulings made in that judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, driver, insurance company, and insured, sought review of an order from the trial court (Georgia), which granted a summary judgment in favor of plaintiff insurance company in a declaratory action involving automobile insurance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action seeking a declaration that it was not liable to provide any insurance coverage or to defend any suit filed by defendant driver as a result of an automobile accident. The trial court granted a summary judgment in favor of plaintiff. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that 1963 Ga. Laws § 54-407A(c) was unconstitutional under Ga. Const. art. III, § VII, para. VIII. (Ga. Code Ann. § 2-908) where the actual statutory amendment had no connection whatsoever with uninsured vehicles and the caption of the amendment stated that the statute was to provide coverage for uninsured motorists. The court held that the trial court did not error by granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff where the insurance policy issued by plaintiff contained an unambiguous exclusion endorsement that provided plaintiff was not liable for any accident that occurred when defendant insured's sons were driving.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that granted a summary judgment in favor of plaintiff in a declaratory action involving automobile insurance liability.

 

1192 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


CTC Finance Corp. v. Holden


No. 23263


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 809; 147 S.E.2d 427; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 703


February 15, 1966, Argued  
February 23, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 112 Ga. App. 443 (145 SE2d 597).

This case is reported in Holden v. CTC Finance Corp., 112 Ga. App. 443 (145 SE2d 597), and relates to the question of the right of a trial judge or court in the first grant of a new trial and an interpretation of Ga. L. 1959, pp. 353, 354, which seemingly restricts the court in granting same, the Court of Appeals holding that the matter of stating the ground, or grounds, upon which the first grant of a motion for new trial is granted is not discretionary but mandatory. The applicant is before this court contending the decision is erroneous because it is in conflict with the power of superior courts to grant new trials under the constitutional mandate (Constitution of 1945; Code Ann. § 2-123) and is an invasion of the judicial powers by the legislature under the separation of powers clause of the State Constitution (Constitution of 1945; Code Ann. § 2-3906). The writ of certiorari has been granted to review the decision and judgment of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted a writ of certiorari to an applicant from the Court of Appeals (Georgia) to hear its appeal related to the rights of a court in the first grant of a new trial, and to interpret 1959 Ga. Laws 353, 354, which apparently restricted courts in granting new trials. The appellate court had held that the grounds upon which the first grant of a motion for new trial was granted were not discretionary but mandatory.


OVERVIEW: The applicant argued that the appellate court's decision was erroneous because it was in conflict with the power of superior courts to grant new trials under Ga. Const. art. VI, § 4, para. 6, and was an invasion of the judicial powers by the legislature under the separation of powers clause of Ga. Const. art. I, § 1, para. 23. The court noted that those constitutional clauses created insuperable barriers to any legislative control or interference with the courts in the exercise of their powers to grant new trials. The court reasoned that if 1959 Ga. Laws 353 was not construed as discretionary instead of mandatory, it could have nullified the unrestricted constitutional power of the courts regarding the grant of a new trial. Therefore, declaring the act discretionary, the court held that the lower courts could have complied with it if they wished, but a failure to do so was not error and was no grounds for reversing a judgment granting a new trial. In so reversing the appellate court, the court also pointed out that the entire 1959 Act was a nullity and was not subject to further consideration on remand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment.

 

1193 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Corinth Publ'ns v. Wesberry


No. 23227


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 704; 146 S.E.2d 764; 1966 Ga. LEXIS 676


December 13, 1965, Argued  
January 18, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Georgia State Literature Commission filed an action for a declaratory judgment that respondent publisher's book was obscene. The publisher sought review of the judgment of the Muscogee Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled the publisher's demurrers, refused the publisher's demand for a jury trial, and declared that the publisher's book was obscene.


OVERVIEW: The Commission claimed that the publisher's book contained obscene material. The publisher claimed that the State's obscenity laws were unconstitutional on their face and that it was entitled to a jury trial. The trial court adjudicated the publisher's book obscene. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the action was a civil proceeding, that 1963 Ga. Laws p. 78 was not applicable, that 1953 Ga. Laws p. 135, 1958 Ga. Laws p. 391, and 1964 Ga. Laws p. 161 did not restrain or delay the publication of literature, but authorized remedial action after publication, that the publisher's claim that the statutes were unconstitutional was not meritorious, and that the trial court did not err in denying the publisher's demand for a jury trial. The court also held that the publisher's book was filthy and disgusting and that the trial court's adjudication that the book was obscene was amply supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment declaring the publisher's book obscene.

 

1194 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Stinson v. Manning


Nos. 23141, 23142


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 487; 145 S.E.2d 541; 1965 Ga. LEXIS 507


September 15, 1965, Argued  
October 11, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 4, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Injunction. Laurens Superior Court. Before Judge Ward.

On June 2, 1965, the petitioners, E. S. Stinson, Jack Lewis and Elmer Dixon, filed their petition in the Laurens Superior Court against a plethora of named defendants, including the Secretary of State, the Ordinary of Laurens County, and various members of Boards of Education in that county, in which they sought injunctive relief, a declaration that a Constitutional Amendment purportedly adopted in 1964 was improperly ratified and praying that an Act of 1965 enacted pursuant to the Constitutional Amendment be declared unconstitutional and void.

The allegations of the petition with which we shall be concerned in a decision of this case are as follows: that prior to November 3, 1964, there were in existence two school systems in Laurens County, to wit, the Laurens County School System (hereinafter referred to as the County System) and the Independent School System of Dublin (hereinafter referred to as the Independent System); that on November 3, 1964, an amendment (Ga. L. 1964, p. 903) proposing to merge the two systems into a Dublin Laurens County School System was submitted for ratification;  [***2] that such amendment was a local amendment required to be separately submitted to the electors of the two school systems and required to be approved by a majority of each of the two systems voting separately; that the Dublin Election District is larger in territory than the Independent System and comprises electors of both systems; that electors of the Dublin Election District were not separately voted, but at the election all votes cast in that election district were counted without regard to the school system to which they belonged; that within the Dublin Election District it was impossible to determine how many electors of the County System cast their votes for or against the proposal or how many of the electors of the Independent System voted for or against the proposal; that of the votes counted in the Dublin Election District there were several hundred electors, to wit, in excess of 500, who resided in the County System and whose votes were counted with and included in the totals of the electors residing in the Independent System; that it was impossible to tell if the votes of the several hundred electors of the County System had been counted with the other electors of such system [***3] and hence whether the amendment was ratified or rejected; that there were only 19 more votes for ratification than against ratification of the amendment in those areas of the County System where the electors voted separately (the county area outside the Dublin Election District); that relative to the ratification of the amendment there exists an insurmountable uncertainty incident to the method of submission and the counting of votes which would overcome the apparent and announced result of the "referendum"; that there were 493 absentee ballots which were counted and included without regard to the school district of which each absentee voter was an elector, the votes being added to the totals of the Dublin Election District; that of the absentee electors at least 100 were electors of the County System and their votes were not separately reflected or reflected with any other election district outside the Independent District; that a failure to have the votes properly counted would nullify the petitioner's votes against ratification and require a result different from that which would have appertained had the votes been properly counted; that as a result the amendment was not duly ratified.

 [***4] The petition further alleged that in 1965 the General Assembly enacted into law an Act (Ga. L. 1965, p. 2023) purporting to implement the amendment; that pursuant to that Act an election was held for members of the Dublin Laurens County School Board and that certain defendants were elected; that the petitioners did not bring this petition prior to June 1965, because an action which sought to require a proper certification of the referendum on the amendment had been filed in January 1965, by other parties and this court rendered a decision on that case May 19, 1965; that this action was brought while a rehearing was pending before this court.

The petition also alleged that the Election Code of 1964 (Ga. L. 1964, Ex. Sess., p. 26) is not an adequate remedy at law and is inapplicable, but if it is applicable it is unconstitutional and void; that the Act of 1965 (Ga. L. 1965, p. 2023) was unconstitutional and void in the absence of the adoption of the Constitutional amendment.

The defendants filed their demurrers to the petition as amended on the grounds: that no cause of action was set forth; that the petitioners failed to show any legal standing to bring the suit; that the petitioners [***5] failed to avail themselves of the provisions of the Election Code of 1964, supra, to contest an election and that they had an adequate and complete remedy at law under that Act; that by virtue of their long delay in bringing the petition and allowing the State and local governments to proceed to implement the provisions of the amendment, the petitioners are guilty of such laches as to bar them from bringing the action. The defendants also filed a special plea based on three grounds, to which plea the petitioners demurred.

After a hearing on the demurrers to the petition, the trial judge entered an order in which he found that the petition showed, as a matter of law, that it did not set forth a cause of action for the reason that the Election Code governed, and since petitioners had not proceeded under that law they could not now bring this action. The judge also ruled against the plaintiffs' contention that the Election Code was unconstitutional and ruled that the enabling Act was valid and that the petitioners were guilty of laches. He also sustained the petitioners' demurrers to ground 1 of the defendants' plea, but overruled the demurrers as to grounds 2 and 3. To the adverse [***6] rulings contained in the order, the plaintiffs except and bring the case to this court for review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents sought review of a decision of the Laurens Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained the demurrers filed by appellees state and county officials, to the residents' petition seeking injunctive relief and a declaration that [a Constitutional Amendment purportedly adopted in 1964 ] was improperly ratified, and praying that an Act of 1965 enacted pursuant to the Constitutional Amendment be declared unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: The residents asserted that the vote to consolidate the districts was illegal and the trial court sustained the officials' demurrer, finding that that the petition did not set forth a cause of action as the Election Code governed. Because the residents had not proceeded under that law, they could not now bring their action. It also ruled against the contention that the Election Code was unconstitutional and ruled that the enabling Act was valid and that the petitioners were guilty of laches. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the trial judge erred in sustaining the demurrers of the defendants attacking the petition on the grounds that the petitioners were barred by laches. The legislature passed 1965 Ga. Laws 2023, that allowed the voters of a county school district and a local school district to vote on whether to consolidate the two districts.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the residents' challenge to the election was reversed.

 

1195 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hinson v. First Nat'l Bank


No. 23094


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 408; 144 S.E.2d 765; 1965 Ga. LEXIS 479


September 14, 1965, Argued  
October 7, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Confirmation of sale of realty; constitutional question. Charlton Superior Court. Before Judge Hodges.

The First National Bank in Waycross filed its application in Charlton Superior Court seeking confirmation of a sale of real property under a power of sale contained in a deed to secure debt and naming J. B. Hinson and J. B. Paul Hinson as defendants. It was alleged that Paul Hinson executed a note for $ 49,880.79 plus 6% interest, which note was endorsed by J. B. Hinson; that the note was secured by a deed to secure debt to a certain tract of land on which was located a motel, fixtures and personalty; that the note was in default with an amount due of $ 30,157.35 plus interest; that foreclosure proceedings were instituted under the power of sale contained in the security deed and, after due and legal advertisement made, the sale took place; that the highest and best bid for the property was $ 21,000, such bid being made by an agent and director of the bank; that such amount was insufficient to pay the note and a substantial deficiency exists; that a confirmation of the sale under Code Ann. § 37-608, et seq. (Ga. L. 1935, p. 381) is desired; that the court hear evidence as [***2] to the true market value of the property sold and that the sale be confirmed if the court is satisfied the property brought its true market value at the foreclosure sale.

The defendant J. B. Hinson filed a plea to the jurisdiction asserting that he is a resident of Camden County and that the superior court of that county has jurisdiction rather than Charlton Superior Court; that the statute in question violates the Constitutional provisions as to venue since it requires the sale be reported "to the judge of the superior court of the county in which the land lies . . ."

The defendant J. B. Hinson also filed his demurrers on the grounds: that the petition set forth no cause of action; that the statute (Code Ann. §§ 37-608 -- 37-611) violates Art. VI, Sec. XVI, Par. I of the Georgia Constitution in that it deprives the defendant of the right to a trial by jury; that the provision for venue contained in the statute (Code Ann. § 37-608) contravenes Art. VI, Sec. XIV, Par. III and Art. VI, Sec. XIV, Pars. IV, V and VI of the Georgia Constitution.

The trial judge overruled the plea to the jurisdiction and the defendant's demurrers. The defendant answered, denying the material allegations [***3] of the bank's application and asserting the plaintiff bank was estopped to seek confirmation by its conduct in re-selling the property pending the confirmation.

The evidence adduced before the trial court, on the testimony of a single witness, an official of the bank, was substantially as follows. The property, real and personal, was sold for $ 21,000. The market value of this property was about $ 19,000, of which $ 8,900 was the approximate value of the personalty and $ 10,100 the approximate value of the realty. The witness admitted his evaluation of the market value of the property was based in part on an appraisal made by another party, who was not called as a witness, and in part on his somewhat cursory examination of the premises. He also testified that the bank and a third person had executed instruments for the sale of the property. However, no delivery had taken place and the trust department of the bank was holding "in escrow" the papers and two checks tendered to the bank by the prospective purchaser pending the confirmation of the sale made pursuant to the power of sale contained in the security deed.

The trial court entered an order confirming the sale. Exception [***4] is taken to that judgment and to the order overruling the plea to the jurisdiction and the demurrers.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Charlton County (Georgia), which confirmed plaintiff bank's sale of the property owners' motel due to non-payment of a note. The property owners also challenged the trial court's order that overruled their plea to the trial court's jurisdiction and that overruled their demurrers.


OVERVIEW: The property owners fell behind on their payments to the bank, so the bank foreclosed on the property. The trial court confirmed the sale of the real and personal property for one lump sum amount. On appeal, the court reversed. O.C.G.A. § 37-609 applies only to the sale of foreclosed real property and provided that the trial court had to have evidence before it showing the true market value of the property sold. The sale could not be confirmed unless the trial judge was satisfied that the property sold brought its true market value. The property covered by the security instrument, consisting of both real and personal property, was sold for one lump sum. Although the approximate value of the real and personal property was shown, there was no evidence as to what each species of property sold for separately. The trial court should have ordered a resale of the property, at which the real and personal property would be sold separately.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1196 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Chatterton v. State


No. 23109


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 424; 144 S.E.2d 726; 1965 Ga. LEXIS 483


September 14, 1965, Argued  
October 7, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 19, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Chattooga Superior Court. Before Judge Coker.

At the January term of Chattooga Superior Court, Roy Dale Chatterton and Woodrow Whisman were separately indicted by the grand jury of Chattooga County for the offense of murdering Billy A. Copeland.

The defendant and Whisman were hitchhiking through this State from West Virginia to Florida on December 15, 1964, when they accosted the victim Billy Copeland who permitted them to enter his automobile and ride as his guests. Copeland had started from LaFayette to Rome to carry his son home from school for the Christmas holidays. After traveling several miles in the automobile the defendant and Whisman, by use of a knife and pistol, commandeered Copeland's automobile and kidnapped him. They drove to a lonely and deserted house in Chattooga County, forced their victim to remove all of his outer clothing and robbed him of various articles including his knife, watch, gloves and jacket, together with $ 40 in money. While rifling his pockets the thieves came upon a picture or private papers of Copeland. When he asked for the picture or papers they became enraged and both struck him heavy [***2] blows with a board. They then bound and dragged him into a back room of the house. They left him semiconscious and in a critical condition. The culprits drove the victim's automobile to Kentucky and when it finally would run no farther, they stole a Buick. The latter car they drove to Guyton, Ga., where they were apprehended by officers on December 18, 1964. At the time they were possessed of Copeland's coat, watch and gloves.

Concerning their arrest, Detective Randolph Strickland testified that when apprehended and arrested on suspicion of having stolen the automobile they then were driving, Whisman, who had been placed by the officers with his hands against a wall, attempted to lower his hands in an effort to procure a knife he had in his pocket. The officer related that Whisman in Chatterton's presence made the remark that had he been able to get to the knife he would have left the officer's "guts" lying in the street. Strickland also testified that when arrested Chatterton gave his name as Caulfield and Whisman identified himself as Adkins. They both protested they were entirely innocent.

Lodged in the Chatham County jail, the defendant and Whisman were interviewed by [***3] Billy W. Fields and Randolph Strickland. On December 22, 1964, the defendant made a written confession in the presence of Patricia Brown and Detectives Billy Fields and Randolph Strickland. The circumstances concerning this confession were related by Billy Fields. He testified: "Q. I will ask you if Mr. Chatterton and Mr. Whisman made certain statements to you admitting that they killed Billy Copeland, the deceased in this case? A. Yes, sir, they did. Q. At any time prior to the making of any statement to you on the 22nd or after the 22nd, prior to that time, did you or anyone ever threaten, threaten or intimidate or harass Mr. Chatterton or Mr. Whisman in any way, nature or form whatsoever? A. No, sir, we did not. Q. Did you or anyone in your presence threaten to harm them in any way whatsoever, that is to say Chatterton or Whisman? A. No, sir, we did not. Q. Did either you or anyone in your presence, offer them any reward or benefit or hope of reward or benefit which could in any way possibly accrue to the advantage of either, in order to get them to make these various statements? A. No, sir, we did not. Q. The statements which they made, which Chatterton made and Whisman [***4] made on the 22nd and at times after that, were all of those statements freely and voluntarily made by Mr. Chatterton and Mr. Whisman? A. Yes, sir, they were."

Later the defendant made a similar confession to Emmett Whitfield, Jack Knott and Bill Hart. The State's witnesses testified the defendant's confessions were freely and voluntarily made, and further testified the defendant was fully advised of his constitutional rights and positively stated he did not want a lawyer.

The defendant in an unsworn statement insisted the confessions were induced by a threat and promise of F. B. I. Agent Boyle. His statement was: that he was arrested on Friday night and taken to the Chatham County jail where he was kept in solitary confinement for approximately four days or until Tuesday morning; that he was out of solitary confinement before he made a statement; that he was interrogated at night, mostly by the F. B. I., three times while he was there; that he asked for an attorney when first brought to jail and was told they would give him one, but never got one; that when interrogated by the F. B. I. they suggested he make a statement and offered him inducements; that they did not offer him [***5] anything the first time he was interrogated; that he asked for a lawyer but did not get one; that the second time he was interrogated no offers were made but he again requested a lawyer and still didn't get one; that an offer was made to him the night he confessed; that "the gentleman in charge" said "if I would make a confession that he would see to it that I was committed to a mental institution;" that the agent said if the defendant didn't admit being involved in the beating of Copeland "he would see to it that I burned."

The defendant further related in his statement: that he asked for clothes and money and was told by the F. B. I. agent he would see about getting it; that the defendant had no way of even buying cigarettes and that Fields and Strickland were "all time sending us cigarettes and coffee and stuff while we was in confinement"; that he never told Fields about only being able to fry once; that when he made his confession to Fields he was still under the influence of statements made by the F. B. I.; that he wouldn't have talked with Fields except for the agent's influence and was relying on "their promise to get him committed to a mental institution."

Sidney Smith,  [***6] an F. B. I. Agent, testified that he was present during the entire time that Agent Boyle interviewed the defendant. He did not recall Boyle having made a promise to the defendant that he would get off on a plea of insanity or that Boyle threatened that if the defendant did not confess he would see that the defendant got the electric chair. On cross examination he admitted, in response to questions: "Q. Do you recall Boyle advising him that if he would go ahead and make a statement, that he would see that he was able to enter a plea of insanity in his trial? A. There was some talk of Chatterton saying that he had asked for psychiatric help at one time. Q. And isn't it true that Mr. Boyle told him that if he didn't give a statement and get off on an insanity plea, that Mr. Boyle would see that he burned in the electric chair? A. I don't recall that he said that. Q. You recall some conversation about the electric chair, though, don't you? A. Yes, I do."

The defendant was interrogated by officers at night on several occasions.

The defendant was found guilty. The exception is to the trial court's judgment overruling his amended motion for new trial, consisting of the general [***7] grounds and nineteen special grounds. The general grounds and special grounds 6, 7, 8, 9, 17 and 18 were abandoned.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Chattooga Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of murder. Defendant filed an exception to the trial court's judgment overruling his amended motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his friend were picked up while hitchhiking. They kidnapped the driver and smashed his head with a board. The jury returned a guilty verdict to murder. On appeal, the court held that: (1) defendant's confessions were not induced by threats and promises; (2) newspaper accounts of the trial, individually and collectively, were not extremely prejudicial to his case and did not prevent him from obtaining a fair and impartial trial; (3) there was no evidence that jurors who read newspapers or heard broadcasts about defendant were not influenced adversely by them; (4) defendant's ground that his confession was not voluntarily made did not show that any ruling of the court was invoked in reference to the admissibility or weight to be given the alleged confessions; and (5) the jury charge instructing the jury that they could not impose a life sentence unless they found that defendant was entitled to mercy was proper was patently not subject to criticism.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder.

 

1197 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


McCullers v. Williamson


No. 23009


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 358; 144 S.E.2d 911; 1965 Ga. LEXIS 464


June 14, 1965, Argued  
September 13, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 7, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Quo warranto. Walton Superior Court. Before Judge Barrow.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, residents, citizens and taxpayers of the county, appealed from the Walton Superior Court (Georgia), which decided that a constitutional amendment provided a fair, reasonable, equitable and rational method of selecting members of the board of education.


OVERVIEW: The resolution that was adopted changed the education system. Prior to the resolution, three separate and distinct school systems existed in the county, and after, there was only one school district under the management of one county board of education. The petition alleged that a majority of those voting in the election in each of the systems approved the amendment, but that a majority of the voters of an independent school system voted against ratification. It was alleged that the approval of the majority of voters of the independent school system was required before the local amendment could become a part of the constitution. The court agreed with the lower court that the independent school system was not directly affected by the amendment. The amendment left that school system just as it was prior to the amendment. Thus, the amendment did not require ratification by the voters of the independent school system. The court further disagreed with the contention that the amendment violated the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the Constitution, U.S. amendment. XIV. The amendment provided a rational method of selecting members of the board of education.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1198 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dunn v. Dunn


No. 23055


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 368; 144 S.E.2d 758; 1965 Ga. LEXIS 465


July 13, 1965, Submitted  
September 13, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 7, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Motion to set aside divorce decree. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Dyer.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband had filed an exception to the ruling of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled his motion to set aside and vacate a final judgment and decree that awarded plaintiff wife a divorce and awarded plaintiff permanent alimony.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had rendered a final judgment and decree that granted the wife a new trial, and awarded the wife a divorce, and permanent alimony. The husband then filed a motion to set aside and vacate the final judgment and decree on the ground that he was never served personally with the motion for a new trial. The trial court had overruled the husband's motion, and he filed exceptions to the ruling. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had erred in overruling the motion to set aside the final judgment. The court found the husband was not personally served with the motion for a new trial, as provided in Ga. Code Ann. § 70-306. Further, where there was no service of process or waiver of the service of process, the trial court was without jurisdiction and its judgment was void and could be attacked in any court where such judgment was attempted to be enforced. The court held that the trial court's judgment in granting the wife a new trial, and awarding her a divorce and permanent alimony was void because the trial court was without jurisdiction to do so where the husband had not been served with notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling that had overruled the husband's motion to set aside and vacate a final judgment and decree that awarded the wife a divorce and awarded the wife permanent alimony.

 

1199 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hornstein v. Lovett


Nos. 23047, 23048


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 279; 144 S.E.2d 378; 1965 Ga. LEXIS 432


July 12, 1965, Argued  
September 9, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus, etc. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.

This is an equitable and mandamus action against the governing authorities of Chatham County seeking injunctive relief and to require the re-issuance of a building permit and a business license to build and operate a trailer park in that county. The allegations show the building permit was issued but thereafter revoked, and suit filed to require the re-issuance of same and in a different count to enjoin interference with its use if valid, but upon agreement of both parties, the petitioner then applied for a business license to operate the trailer park, and after the filing of the litigation and the application for a license, a licensing ordinance was adopted which would prevent the operation of a trailer park within 1,200 feet of any school ground or college campus, after which the licensing application was likewise denied, and the petitioner amended his petition to add an additional count to demand the issuance of the business license. The crux of the matter is the location of the proposed trailer park within 1,200 feet of Armstrong State College, a part of the University System of Georgia. The Board of Regents [***2] objected to the location of the trailer park and by intervention seek to prevent its licensing and construction, alleging it is in violation of the licensing ordinance requiring it to be more than 1,200 feet from any school ground or college campus, the ordinance being adopted to protect the safety, health, welfare and public morals of the citizens of Chatham County on October 30, 1964. The licensing ordinance is apparently adopted under and by virtue of the authority of Ga. L. 1952, p. 617 (constitutional amendment authorizing Chatham County to police said county and to levy occupational taxes) and Ga. L. 1919, p. 604 (authorizing Chatham County to adopt ordinances and regulations for the security and welfare of its inhabitants). The amended petition attacks the provisions of the ordinance requiring that trailer parks be more than 1,200 feet from any college campus as being unconstitutional, unlawful, arbitrary, capricious, unreasonable and discriminatory in that the passage of same involved the petitioner's private property rights and was passed without proper notice, public or private, which is violative of the due process clauses of the State Constitution (Code Ann. §§ 2-102,  [***3] 2-103; Const. of 1945), the same being designed to specifically exclude petitioner from the use of his property. The case came on for a hearing before the court without the intervention of a jury, and after hearing evidence and consideration of the stipulation of facts, the court granted the mandamus as to the issuance of a building permit but denied the prayers for the granting of a business license. The plaintiff filed a motion for new trial which was later amended, and after a hearing overruled. The main bill excepts to the final judgment on the motion for new trial as amended, and the cross bill excepts to the court order requiring the county to issue the building permit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed on the main bill; cross bill dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error property owner sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Chatham County (Georgia), which found in favor of defendant in error county authorities in the owner's action to compel the authorities to issue him a business license to operate a trailer park. The authorities cross-appealed the portion of the judgment that required them to issue the owner a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The owner filed an action for equitable relief after the authorities denied his applications for a business license and a building permit in connection with a proposed trailer park. The trial court granted mandamus as to the building permit but denied relief as to the business license. Both parties appealed. The court affirmed the judgment as to the owner's bill of exceptions and dismissed the authorities' cross bill. The court found that the denial of the business license was a proper exercise of the authorities' power to regulate trailer parks. The court found that an ordinance prohibiting such parks from operating within 1200 feet of any educational facility was a valid exercise of the power conferred upon the authorities by 1919 Ga. Laws 604 and 1952 Ga. Laws 617. The court dismissed the authorities' cross bill, which challenged an order requiring the authorities to reissue the owner's previously-revoked building permit. Citing O.C.G.A. 6-901 (1957), the court found that it was without jurisdiction to review the order, noting that the final judgment involved in the cross bill would not have been affected even if the owner had been granted the relief that he requested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment on the main bill and dismissed the cross bill.

 

1200 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Sims v. State


No. 22939


Supreme Court of Georgia


221 Ga. 190; 144 S.E.2d 103; 1965 Ga. LEXIS 416


May 10, 1965, Argued  
July 14, 1965, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 26, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rape. Charlton Superior Court. Before Judge Hodges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Charlton Superior Court (Georgia) of rape by force.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's first of many challenges to his conviction was that the jury array did not fairly represent the county based upon the systematic exclusion of Negroes from jury service. The court rejected the claim because the jury array was prepared from the tax digests which by law were divided by race, and one jury commissioner asserted that race did not factor into the compilation of the jury array. Furthermore, defendant was not entitled to a jury makeup that was proportionate to the percentage of Negroes in the county. Denial of a motion for new trial was proper where the evidence that established the violence of rape supported the conviction for rape by force. It was not erroneous to admit defendant's confession where defendant during the investigatory stage volunteered the confession, and he had been advised of his rights but refused counsel. The trial judge's instruction that left the jury to decide if the confession was voluntary was not erroneous even though it did not follow federal precedent which the court took to task as illogical, and as not involving Ga. Code Ann. § 38-420, which required the confession to have been corroborated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.
